State v. Hampton


Appeal No. 2004AP2310


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 194; 296 Wis. 2d 417; 722 N.W.2d 399; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 772



August 22, 2006, Decided  
August 22, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. CONEN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF1815.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed from an order summarily denying his motion for postconviction relief by Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: Incident to a plea bargain, the inmate pled guilty to second-degree reckless homicide while armed, and second-degree recklessly endangering safety while armed, in exchange for the State's motion to dismiss a possession of marijuana charge and its sentencing recommendation of an unspecified period of confinement. The trial court accepted the inmate's guilty pleas, dismissed the marijuana charge, and imposed eighteen- and four-year consecutive sentences, comprised of equal nine- and two-year periods of confinement and extended supervision. Postconviction counsel was appointed, but she refused to pursue the claims the inmate identified, and rather than pursuing a no-merit appeal, she closed the file as the inmate requested. Defendant failed to pursue postconviction or appellate relief, but later filed a pro se postconviction motion pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2003-04). The appellate court affirmed the denial of the inmate's motion as (1) the inmate's guilty plea waived his defenses regarding an unconstitutional arrest, and (2) the inmate did not allege that but for his counsel's alleged ineffectiveness that he would have instead proceeded to trial.


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's motion was affirmed.

State v. Gray


Appeal No. 2004AP1194


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 194; 296 Wis. 2d 417; 722 N.W.2d 399; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 745



August 15, 2006, Decided  
August 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Gray, 2007 WI 59, 299 Wis. 2d 325, 731 N.W.2d 635, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 92 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Gray, 2008 WI App 160, 314 Wis. 2d 506, 758 N.W.2d 224, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 686 (2008)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Gray v. Wis. Dep't of Corr., 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15473 (E.D. Wis., Feb. 9, 2010)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Gray, 2015 Wisc. App. LEXIS 738 (Wis. Ct. App., Oct. 9, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, denying his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2001-2002) postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of attempted first-degree intentional homicide and armed robbery. The circuit court imposed a forty-year sentence for the attempted homicide, and withheld sentence and imposed a twenty-five-year consecutive term of probation for the armed robbery. The instant action was appellant's third postconviction motion. The appellate court found that in the instant motion, appellant failed to offer the circuit court any reason, much less a sufficient reason, for his failure to raise the particular ineffective-assistance claim in his prior postconviction motions. The appellate court ruled that the circuit court therefore properly held that appellant's claim was procedurally barred by the Wisconsin Supreme Court Escalona-Naranjo decision. Also, the circuit court correctly denied appellant's motion for a new trial based upon newly discovered evidence. Appellant failed to provide in his postconviction motion any newly discovered evidence that would corroborate the recantation.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

803 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Milwaukee County Pers. Review Bd. v. Clarke


Appeal No. 2005AP1388


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 186; 296 Wis. 2d 210; 723 N.W.2d 141; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 749


June 6, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
August 15, 2006, Decided  
August 15, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: M. JOSEPH DONALD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV658.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff appealed an order of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court, Wisconsin, which granted a writ of mandamus ordering the sheriff to reinstate intervenor employee as a deputy sheriff sergeant. The sheriff had relieved the employee of his duties as a sergeant and reassigned the employee pending a hearing before respondent county personnel review board (PRB) on the sheriff's petition to demote the employee.


OVERVIEW: The PRB sought a writ of mandamus to enforce its order made pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 59.52(8)(b) (2003-2004) that the sheriff did not have the authority to demote the employee while the sheriff's petition to demote the employee was pending before the PRB. The court concluded that the PRB had standing to seek the writ and that the issue was not moot. The court also concluded that both the PRB and the employee had a clear right to relief. The sheriff had a positive and plain legal duty to follow the PRB's reinstatement order and was not free to simply ignore it. The employee was personally affected by the sheriff's order relieving him of duties as a sergeant. The PRB was substantially damaged by the sheriff's decision to ignore its order reinstating the employee to the rank of sergeant. Neither the PRB nor the sheriff had an adequate remedy at law. Without the mechanism of mandamus, the PRB had no ability to preserve the authority it had been given, or the integrity of the disciplinary system that it oversaw. The employee sought out the only remedy available when he believed the sheriff's actions toward him were in violation of relevant statutes and ordinances.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Gehl v. Conrad


Appeal No. 2005AP2589


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 194; 296 Wis. 2d 420; 722 N.W.2d 400; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 719



August 10, 2006, Decided  
August 10, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Gehl v. Conrad, 2007 WI 59, 299 Wis. 2d 327, 731 N.W.2d 637, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 142 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Gehl v. Town of Perry, 2006 WI App 156, 295 Wis. 2d 490, 719 N.W.2d 800, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 536 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed consolidated actions for declaratory judgment and certiorari relief after respondent town denied the owner's application for approval to construct a new residence on family farm land.


OVERVIEW: The property owner filed an application for approval to construct a new residence on family farm land in an exclusive agricultural district. A zoning administrator denied the application. The town board of adjustment upheld the decision. The trial court consolidated the owner's certiorari action with an ongoing declaratory judgment action. The trial court upheld the zoning administrator's method for calculating substantial income from a farm operation and upheld the board's decision. On appeal, the court saw no reason why the zoning administrator could not have undertaken both the substantial income review and the conformity-with-agricultural-use analysis at the same stage in its review of an application for a zoning permit. The fact that the zoning administrator might have incorrectly labeled the considerations under Dane Co., Wis., Code of Ordinances § 10.123(9)(f) (2000) as part of the analysis under subsection (2)(b) did not change the substance of his reasoning. Notwithstanding the zoning administrator's reference to "farm income plan" review, it was clear from the entirety of his discussion that the application was rejected under § 10.123(9)(f), not (2)(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Ford v. Holm


Appeal No. 2002AP1828-W


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 176; 296 Wis. 2d 119; 722 N.W.2d 609; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 720


June 16, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
August 10, 2006, Decided  
August 10, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. Ford v. Holm, 2007 WI 16, 298 Wis. 2d 94, 727 N.W.2d 34, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 915 (2006)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Ford v. Lundquist, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 195 (W.D. Wis., Jan. 3, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: HABEAS CORPUS original proceeding. Cir. Ct. No. 1997CF57.
State ex rel. Ford v. Holm, 2004 WI App 22, 269 Wis. 2d 810, 676 N.W.2d 500, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 74 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus after he pled no contest to second-degree sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus. The court granted the writ in part and denied it in part. The Wisconsin Office of the State Public Defender (SPD) filed a motion to reconsider and requested to intervene. The court granted the SPD permission to intervene. After reviewing the briefs, the court found that petitioner knowingly and voluntarily waived his right to pursue an appeal challenging the validity of his plea of no contest to second-degree sexual assault. The court rejected petitioner's claim that he received ineffective assistance of appellate counsel when his attorney did not pursue the plea withdrawal issue. Further, petitioner's constitutional right to effective representation for the purpose of exercising his right to directly appeal his conviction did not require his postconviction counsel to offer him the option of a "partial no-merit" report on any potential issues remaining after petitioner declined for strategic reasons to pursue an issue having arguable merit. It could not be a violation of "professional norms" to not file a no-merit report when one was not clearly required by Wis. Stat. § 809.32 (2003-04) or by the federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

806 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Bilda v. Milwaukee County


Appeal No. 2005AP52


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 159; 295 Wis. 2d 673; 722 N.W.2d 116; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 654


December 7, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
July 20, 2006, Decided  
July 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Bilda v. Milwaukee County, 2007 WI 16, 727 N.W.2d 34, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 922 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV1766. APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT R. PEKOWSKY, Reserve Judge.
Bilda v. County of Milwaukee, 2006 WI App 57, 292 Wis. 2d 212, 713 N.W.2d 661, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 253 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant class representatives brought a class against respondents, Milwaukee County and the Employes' Retirement System Pension Board, alleging that changes to the Milwaukee County ordinances governing the retirement system constituted a taking of the class members' property interest without just compensation. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, granted the respondents' summary judgment motions. Class representatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: Milwaukee County, Wis., Ordinance 00-15 made four changes to the Employes' Retirement System. Ordinance 00-15 enhanced benefits for some but not all participants in the retirement system and reduced the vesting period for benefits from ten to five years. Class representatives of members of the Milwaukee County Employes' Retirement System argued that the ordinance constituted an unconstitutional taking because the changes reduced stability. The court disagreed. Ordinance 00-15 created benefit enhancements. The class representatives did not demonstrate that the ordinance was the cause of negative effects on the retirement system. Referral of the ordinance to the Pension Study Commission satisfied the referral requirement in 1965 Wis. Sess. Laws ch. 405, § 2. The Commission's minutes and a letter from the retirement system's actuary constituted a "written report" within the meaning of 1965 Wis. Sess. Laws ch. 405. The court did not err in striking the affidavit of a legal expert submitted by the class representatives, because it contained only conclusions of law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

807 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Terrell


Appeal No. 2005AP1499-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 166; 295 Wis. 2d 619; 721 N.W.2d 527; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 637


June 5, 2006, Oral Argument  
July 18, 2006, Decided  
July 18, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: Karen E. Christenson, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF2259.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of orders from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his motions to dismiss the charges against him for violating Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(h) (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed by a county sheriff's department and worked as a bailiff at a courthouse. He was charged with one count of misconduct in public office and one count of second-degree sexual assault; sexual contact or intercourse by a correctional staff member, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(h) (2003-04). The trial court denied his motions to dismiss the charges against him. On appeal, the court found that, based on the plain meaning of the statute, defendant was not a "correctional staff member." The statute did not extend to a county sheriff's deputy who was assigned to work in a courthouse. The courthouse was not a "correctional institution." Although defendant's work as a bailiff caused him to enter the criminal justice facility to move inmates from that building to the courthouse, such incidental conduct did not fall under the plain meaning of "working at a correctional institution." The plain meaning of the statute clearly applied to those who worked within the criminal justice facility, not to a courthouse bailiff who entered the facility simply to move inmates to the courthouse.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court and remanded the case with directions to the trial court to dismiss the complaint against defendant based on violations of § 940.225(2)(h).

Brown County v. Marilyn M. (In re Marilyn M.)


Appeal No. 2005AP3051


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2006 WI App 156; 295 Wis. 2d 491; 719 N.W.2d 800; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 572



June 27, 2006, Decided  
June 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from order of the circuit court for Brown County: PETER J. NAZE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1996GN172.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, continuing her protective placement under Wis. Stat. ch. 55 (2003-2004).


OVERVIEW: The individual's protective placement began in June 1998, and the individual's placement had been subject to annual court reviews. The individual's most recent review was held in July 2005, nearly fourteen months after her last review. The individual was seventy years old and had significant mental health problems. The individual's thyroid gland had been removed, requiring her to take daily medication. The individual had been diagnosed with paranoid schizophrenia and chronic paranoid personality disorder, and exhibited the "inevitable deterioration of aging." The appellate court ruled that the individual waived her right to challenge the circuit court's competency to proceed with her review because she failed to raise the issue before the circuit court. Also, the evidence was sufficient to support the protective placement order. The individual was so totally incapable of caring for herself as to substantially risk self-harm. The individual's inability to self-medicate created a substantial risk of harm to herself because it created a substantial risk that, if the individual were living independently, she would stop taking her medication.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

809 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Larson v. Burmaster


Appeal No. 2005AP1433


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 142; 295 Wis. 2d 333; 720 N.W.2d 134; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 574


May 1, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
June 27, 2006, Decided  
June 27, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Larson v. Burmaster, 2006 WI 126, 297 Wis. 2d 320, 724 N.W.2d 203, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 796 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: RICHARD J. SANKOVITZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV159.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the father and his son, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of defendants, instructor, principal, department chair, and superintendent (district), in the father and son's action claiming that the son could not be required to complete summer homework.


OVERVIEW: The father and son appealed from an order dismissing their action against the district. They had brought an action claiming that the son could not be required by the instructor to complete summer homework. The trial court dismissed the case for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, concluding that under Wis. Stat. §§ 118.001, 120.12(14) and 120.13 (2003-04), it was within the school district's, and therefore the instructor's, authority to require summer homework. Summer homework, particularly for an honors class for which students received additional credit, fit comfortably within the range of what was reasonable. The court concluded that the instructor had the authority to assign summer homework, that Wis. Stat. §§ 118.001, 120.12(14) and 120.13 (2003-04) were not unconstitutional, and that summer homework did not infringe on parents' right to direct the education and upbringing of their children. The court also concluded that the appeal was frivolous and remanded the matter to the trial court for a determination of reasonable costs and attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded to the trial court for a determination of reasonable costs and attorney fees for a frivolous appeal.

County of Milwaukee v. Williams


Appeal Nos. 2005AP2686, 2005AP2687


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 153; 295 Wis. 2d 389; 720 N.W.2d 177; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 567; 2006-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P75,326


June 6, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
June 27, 2006, Decided  
June 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, Sub nomine at County of Milwaukee v. Hegney, 2006 WI 126, 724 N.W.2d 202, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 745 (2006)
Review granted by County of Milwaukee v. Williams, 2006 WI 126, 724 N.W.2d 202, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 744 (2006)
Reversed by, Cause remanded by County of Milwaukee v. Williams, 2007 WI 69, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 396 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, taxicab drivers, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, which found the drivers guilty of violating Ordinance 4.05, for picking up taxicab passengers at the airport without an airport permit. The drivers alleged that the Ordinance was invalid, because appellee County lacked the authority to enact an ordinance prohibiting certain taxicabs from picking up passengers at the airport.


OVERVIEW: Drivers were found guilty of violating the County Ordinance 4.05(3)(b)(5), for picking up taxicab passengers at the airport without an airport permit. They were fined $ 250. On appeal, the drivers claimed that: (1) the County lacked the authority to enact an ordinance prohibiting taxicabs from picking up passengers at the airport; and (2) the Ordinance was void because it conflicted with Wis. Stat. §§ 349.24(1), 194.02, and 133.01. The court affirmed the convictions. It held that Wis. Stat. § 114.14 gave the County the authority to regulate taxicab operations at the airport, that no other Wisconsin Statute conflicted with that authority, and that the state antitrust statute did not apply to the County, because specific statutory authority was given to the County to operate the airport. Therefore, the County Ordinance 4.05 was valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

Reardon v. Braeger


Appeal No. 2005AP2189


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2006 WI App 156; 295 Wis. 2d 491; 719 N.W.2d 800; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 525



June 14, 2006, Decided  
June 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Reardon v. Braeger, 2006 WI 126, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 822 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Ozaukee County: JOSEPH D. MC CORMACK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV314.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant brother appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County (Wisconsin) enjoining him from contact with appellee sister or her immediate family for two years.


OVERVIEW: The sister swore out a petition for a temporary restraining order against her brother accusing him of a verbal harassing attack on her the day before while she and her children were at a country club. On appeal, the court held that the brother's conduct that resulted in the injunction constituted a "course of conduct" as contemplated by Wis. Stat. § 813.125 (2003-2004). The brother angrily approached his sister at the pool and began calling her offensive names in a loud voice. He leaned over her in a threatening manner and pointed his fingers in her face. The more she ignored him the louder and angrier he became. His actions drew the attention of others in the area. As the family left the pool area, a tennis ball was aimed at and struck one of the children. The sister's children were frightened then and remained frightened for some time afterward. The instant episode represented an escalation of a prior encounter at the club between the brother and the sister's husband.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

812 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nelson


Appeal No. 2005AP2300-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 124; 294 Wis. 2d 578; 718 N.W.2d 168; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 463


March 3, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
May 25, 2006, Decided  
May 25, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Nelson, 2006 WI 113, 721 N.W.2d 486, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 661 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DALE T. PASSELL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF532.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) convicting him of two felony counts of capturing representations depicting nudity in violation of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 942.09(2)(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for videotaping the victims, women who were his next door neighbors, while they were using their bathroom. On appeal, the court held that the phrase "reasonable expectation of privacy" as used in § 942.09(2)(a) meant that the person who was depicted nude was in a circumstance in which he or she had an assumption that he or she was secluded from the presence or view of others, and that assumption was a reasonable one under all the circumstances. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because the victims he videotaped had a reasonable expectation of privacy: (1) the bathroom was on the second floor of the building; (2) defendant's house appeared vacant and actually was generally vacant during the summer; (3) there was a tree that blocked the view of the bathroom window from the ground during the summer; (4) over 10 feet separated defendant's house from the victims' house; (5) the victims were located four to five feet from the window when defendant videotaped them; and (6) a reasonable jury could infer that defendant was using a zoom feature to see the victims.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State ex rel. Walker v. Bartow


Appeal No. 2004AP2200


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 130; 294 Wis. 2d 695; 717 N.W.2d 852; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 425



May 16, 2006, Decided  
May 16, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by State ex rel. Walker v. Bartow, 2006 WI 113, 721 N.W.2d 487, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 696 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CLARE L. FIORENZA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV4772.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed pro se from the order dismissing his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. He argued that habeas corpus was the proper mechanism for reviewing the constitutionality of Wisconsin's "sexual predator" law, Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2003-04), under which he is currently committed. Because the inmate had legal remedies other than habeas corpus available to challenge his commitment, the court affirmed the circuit court's order. Whether he had been denied relief improperly was a question that should have been raised in an appeal, not in a habeas corpus petition. Moreover, were the court to assume that the inmate was not barred from seeking habeas corpus relief, his request for relief would still be meritless because it was based on an inaccurate analysis of the case law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

814 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Nicholas C. L. v. Julie R.L. (In re Nicholas C. L.)


Appeal No. 2005AP1754


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 119; 293 Wis. 2d 819; 719 N.W.2d 508; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 417


March 7, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
May 10, 2006, Decided  
May 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Nicholas C. L. v. Julie R. L., 2006 WI 126, 724 N.W.2d 204, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 808 (2006)
Subsequent appeal at Martin L. v. Julie R. L. (In the Interest of Nicholas L.), 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 66 (Wis. Ct. App., Jan. 31, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: J. MAC DAVIS, JUDGE. Cir. Ct. No. 2005JG11.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dispute with appellee mother, appellant grandparents sought guardianship of appellant grandchild. The Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, dismissed the petition. The grandparents and the grandchild appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father had primary placement of the grandchild, but the father died. The grandparents and the grandchild raised numerous issues on appeal. First, they challenged the legal standard applied by the circuit court. They also challenged the circuit court's application of that standard to the facts. Next, they contested the circuit court's credibility determinations. Finally, they contended that the circuit court heavily relied on the guardian ad litem (GAL). The appellate court first addressed whether the Barstad standard was the applicable legal standard for a guardianship action under Wis. Stat. § 880.09. The appellate court determined that the circuit court properly applied the standard to the evidence when it found that there was a need for a guardian. Further, extraordinary circumstances that drastically affected the welfare of the child, which would compel awarding guardianship to the grandparents, did not exist. The circuit court's discretionary rulings regarding the evidence were supported by the record facts and were explained in a rational way on the record. Finally, there was no evidence that the circuit court simply adopted the GAL's opinion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's order dismissing the petition.

 

815 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Walker (In re Walker)


Appeal No. 2005AP673


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 130; 294 Wis. 2d 696; 717 N.W.2d 852; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 403



May 9, 2006, Decided  
May 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by State v. Walker, 2006 WI 113, 721 N.W.2d 487, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 700 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KAREN E. CHRISTENSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1996CF963471.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner sought discharge from his Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2003-04) commitment. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, denied the request. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a chapter 980 petition upon the petitioner's discharge from his juvenile adjudication, even though the petitioner was also serving an adult criminal sentence. Upon completion of his adult sentence, the petitioner's custody was transferred to the Department of Health and Family Services (DHFS) to begin his commitment. The circuit court denied the petitioner's motion to declare chapter 980 unconstitutional as applied against African-Americans and his motion to declare his continued confinement unconstitutional. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the petitioner had failed to present even some evidence to establish that he was no longer a sexually violent person under chapter 980. The petitioner provided no basis to suggest that he should no longer be committed under chapter 980.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order.

Gentilli v. Bd. of Police & Fire Comm'rs


Appeal No. 2005AP1818


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 130; 294 Wis. 2d 698; 717 N.W.2d 853; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 414



May 9, 2006, Decided  
May 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: MORIA KRUEGER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CV1585.
Gentilli v. Bd. of Police & Fire Comm'rs, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 32, 688 N.W.2d 653, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 990 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employee, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of respondent, the Board of Police and Fire Commissioners of the City of Madison (Board), and affirmed the Board's decision to terminate the employee's employment with the fire department. The case was before the circuit court on certiorari review.


OVERVIEW: The employee, a fireman, appealed from the order affirming the Board's decision to terminate his employment. The employee contended that he was discharged under fire department rules that were unconstitutionally vague as applied. Disciplinary charges had been filed against the employee and others pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 62.13(5)(b) (1999-2000), for violating rules of the fire department, which included possessing and using cocaine and marijuana. The court disagreed and affirmed, stating that the rules had been previously applied by the fire department and the Board to off-duty conduct. The employee effectively admitted that a plain reading of the rules informed firefighters that the rules applied to off-duty conduct. The court further stated that it was satisfied that the record did not reflect that the employee's expectation that discharge was not among the possible penalties was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hartwich v. Peterson (In re Colt T. Hartwich)


Appeal No. 2005AP438


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2006 WI App 130; 294 Wis. 2d 696; 717 N.W.2d 852; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 387



May 2, 2006, Decided  
May 2, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Chippewa County: THOMAS J. SAZAMA, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002PA53.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Chippewa County, Wisconsin, granted judgment in favor of respondent father by applying the serial-family payer rule and the shared placement formula and set the amount of child support the father had to pay at $10 per month, even though the father paid $1,050 per month for another child born subsequently but who obtained a support order first. Appellant mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the trial court erred in applying the serial-family payer formula to reduce the father's child support obligation. The appellate court found that in order to properly exercise discretion justifying a disparity where the child support award for one child was $1,050 per month and the award for another child was $10 per month, the trial court had to consider the factors in Wis. Stat. § 767.25(1m) (2001-02). The trial court erroneously exercised its discretion by failing to consider the statutory factors and articulate its reasoning in this case. When applying the statutory factors, the court was free to refuse to apply the serial-family payer rule if, after consideration of the enumerated factors, it determined by the greater weight of the credible evidence that use of the rule would be unfair to the child or one of the parties. Basic fairness required that, at the very least, the serial-family payer analysis had to take into consideration the income level used to establish the first support order. The trial court did not indicate whether it considered that the mother's expenses apparently exceeded her income.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

818 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Dunn County v. Wis. Empl. Rels. Comm'n


Appeal No. 2005AP1917


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 120; 293 Wis. 2d 637; 718 N.W.2d 138; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 384


January 17, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
May 2, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dunn County: WILLIAM C. STEWART, JR., Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV241.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin), which upheld an order from the Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission (WERC) that contested provisions in a collective bargaining agreement with respondent union were mandatory subjects of bargaining under Wis. Stat. § 111.70(1)(a) (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: The union was the collective bargaining representative for two units of employees in the county sheriff's department. The collective bargaining agreement between the union and the county expired. The expired agreement contained several provisions that the union wanted to include in the new agreement. The county refused. Because the county disputed whether it was required to bargain over the provisions, it filed a petition for a declaratory ruling with WERC pursuant to § 111.70(4)(b). WERC concluded that the contested provisions were mandatory subjects of bargaining under § 111.70(1)(a). The circuit court upheld WERC's decision. On appeal, the court concluded that only the "court security officer" provision impermissibly intruded upon the sheriff's constitutionally protected prerogatives. Because the sheriff chose the ways and means of performing protected duties, the balance between various and competing prerogatives had to ultimately be struck by the sheriff, not a collective bargaining agreement. The remaining provisions related only to hours and conditions of employment and were properly considered to be mandatory bargaining subjects.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the holding that the "court security officer" provision of the collective bargaining agreement was a mandatory subject of bargaining between the union and the county. The remainder of the order was affirmed.


 

819 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Jackson v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


Appeal No. 2005AP2123


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 97; 293 Wis. 2d 332; 715 N.W.2d 654; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 343


February 6, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
April 27, 2006, Decided  
April 27, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: JAMES A. WELKER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2005CV984.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) dismissing, sua sponte, his petition for review of a decision of respondent Labor and Industry Review Commission. The circuit court concluded that the petition did not state the nature of petitioner's interest, facts showing he was aggrieved, and the grounds on which the agency decision should be reversed or modified, as required by Wis. Stat. § 227.53(1)(b) (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that it was unfair for the circuit court to dismiss his petition for a "technical reason" and without giving him the opportunity to present his arguments. The appellate court reversed, concluding that (1) dismissal of a petition for failure to state facts showing the petitioner was aggrieved was governed by Wis. Stat. § 227.56(3) (2003-04), and that provision did not permit the circuit court to sua sponte dismiss a petition without a motion from the respondent and without the petitioner having at least one opportunity to amend the petition on the terms described; (2) dismissal for failure to state the nature of the petitioner's interest and the grounds on which the agency decision should be reversed or modified was not expressly addressed by statute but the more reasonable construction of the relevant statutes was that the circuit court did not have the authority to dismiss a petition on these grounds in the absence of a motion from the respondent and without the petitioner having a reasonable opportunity to request leave to amend the petition; and (3) in the instant case, the petition, liberally construed, was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for it to conduct such further proceedings as were appropriate and consistent with the appellate court's decision.

English Manor Bed & Breakfast v. The Great Lakes Cos.


Appeal No. 2005AP1358


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 91; 292 Wis. 2d 762; 716 N.W.2d 531; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 326


February 2, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
April 19, 2006, Decided  
April 19, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: GARY LANGHOFF, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV4.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff businesses appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County, Wisconsin, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a city and resort condominiums, in the businesses' challenge to the city's appropriations for the resort under Wis. Stat. § 66.0615 (2003-04). The businesses objected to the agreement between defendants because it allowed the city to finance the resort project with tax dollars.


OVERVIEW: The city's master plan for the property at issue called for a convention center. The businesses also objected to the expenditure of room tax dollars for other purposes. The court held that under § 66.0615(1m)(d)2, the city's expenditures were proper so long as the city limited them to tourism promotion or development. The court concluded that the legislature intended "tourism promotion and development" to mean the promotion and development of travel for recreational, business or educational purposes. The record demonstrated that the resort did draw travelers for those purposes. Nothing in the record indicated that the resort's operation of both the resort and a restaurant led to commingling of either capital or revenues. The businesses' argument that the resort was a "conference" center as opposed to a "convention" center failed because the court relied on the average person's perception of the work. Also, because of its integration with the conference center, the court deemed the city's use of room tax dollars to retire debt related to the restaurant proper. As to equal protection, the city's objective of revitalizing blighted property was certainly a legitimate municipal purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Zak v. Zifferblatt


Appeal No. 2004AP2698


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 79; 292 Wis. 2d 502; 715 N.W.2d 739; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 308


January 30, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
April 11, 2006, Decided  
April 11, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marinette County: DAVID G. MIRON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV60.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant health care providers challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Marinette County (Wisconsin) in favor of appellee patient in the patient's action claiming that he was negligently discharged from the hospital despite evidence of a life-threatening infection. The patient cross-appealed the trial court's reduction in damages.


OVERVIEW: The patient suffered a severe burn at work, and after awaking with chills sought attention at the hospital where he was treated by the providers. His wound was treated and the patient was discharged. Later, the hospital phoned the patient and told him that his blood tests were abnormal. Due to a severe infection, the patient's bladder was destroyed and he required surgery and other treatment. The court held that a contributory negligence instruction was not warranted because no expert evidence was presented that any delay in the patient's return to the hospital contributed to his injury. Also, the causation instruction was proper because the instruction used equivalent language to Wis. Jury Instructions Civ. No. 1023 (2004), and a reasonable jury would not interpret "substantial factor" to mean "less than a substantial factor." Because the parties failed to adhere to Wis. Stat. § 227.40, the court remanded for the circuit court to address the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 655.015 (2003-04) and the administrative rule implementing it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed as to the constitutional issue and remanded for the circuit court to address the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 655.015 (2003-04) and the administrative rule implementing it. The court otherwise affirmed the judgment.

March 23, 2006, Decided  
March 23, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Preuss, 2006 WI 113, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 604 (2006)
Review denied by State v. Preuss, 2006 WI 113, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 605 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Rock County: MICHAEL J. BYRON, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2002CF1528, 2002CF2243.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgments of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) convicting him of one count of burglary of a building or dwelling and one count of battery by a prisoner as a habitual criminal.


OVERVIEW: While on parole from a prior conviction, defendant was charged with burglary and theft and then charged with battery by a prisoner while in jail. At the battery trial, the victim testified that defendant and a group beat him. Due to some misunderstandings about the plea agreement, defendant pled guilty to burglary and the trial court dismissed the theft and battery charges. On motion of the State, the trial court reopened the battery case and vacated defendant's battery and burglary pleas. The court held that defendant waived the arguments that because the trial court made no explicit finding regarding the true terms of the plea agreement, the State should be bound by the terms recited at the plea hearing and his double jeopardy argument because the arguments were not made below. Defendant was not denied a unanimous verdict because jurors needed not unanimously agree whether defendant was guilty because he was the direct actor or he aided and abetted a direct actor. The evidence was sufficient in that while defendant admitted calling the victim a derogatory name in the presence of people who were beating the victim and thus he was supportive of the direct actors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Bilda v. County of Milwaukee


Appeal No. 2004AP2539


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 57; 292 Wis. 2d 212; 713 N.W.2d 661; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 253


August 10, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
March 23, 2006, Decided  
March 23, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Bilda v. County of Milwaukee, 2006 WI 108, 718 N.W.2d 724, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 439 (2006)
Subsequent appeal at Bilda v. Milwaukee County & Milwaukee County Employes' Ret. Sys. Pension Bd., 2006 WI App 159, 722 N.W.2d 116, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 654 (Wis. Ct. App., July 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT R. PEKOWSKY, Reserve Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CV5460.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees, purported class representatives, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) dismissing their action against defendant county employees' retirement system seeking compensation and declaratory relief claiming that a change in the way in which retirement fund administrative expenses were paid constituted a taking of property for a public purpose without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The county amended Milwaukee County, Wis., Ordinance, ch. 201 to provide that administrative expenses of the retirement system were made obligations of the system. The court affirmed and held that the system complied with 1965 Wis. Laws, ch. 405 in that several days before the board's adoption of the amendment, the system's actuary presented his projections and advised it that the system was adequately funded to accommodate the change, and that the change would not materially affect the funding of the plan. The system participants did not have a right to dictate how the system was administered on a day-to-day basis. The legislature empowered the county to make any changes in the system which may be deemed necessary for the continued operation of the system, provided participants' rights and benefits were neither "diminished" nor "impaired" by the change. The method by which the system's administrative costs had been paid since the amendment was neither illegal nor unconstitutional, and there is no violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court.

NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult entertainment gift store appealed from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that granted summary judgment dismissing the store's complaint for a declaratory judgment that the defendant city's comprehensive adult entertainment ordinances and a new zoning ordinance, Oak Creek, Wis., City Code Ordinance §§ 7.203, 3.40, 17.0901, and 17.0317, were unconstitutional and that the license fees were reasonable.

State v. McGrath


Appeal No. 2005AP1888-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2006 WI App 78; 292 Wis. 2d 487; 713 N.W.2d 193; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 228



March 15, 2006, Decided  
March 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. McGrath, 2006 WI 108, 292 Wis. 2d 413, 718 N.W.2d 726, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 523 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Walworth County: JOHN R. RACE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CT315.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After entering a guilty plea, defendant was convicted, before the Circuit Court for Walworth County, Wisconsin, for operating a vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), third offense. The trial court sentenced defendant in accordance with a sentencing matrix. Defendant moved, postconviction, for a sentence modification, which the trial court denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his motion, defendant contended that, although the trial court had acknowledged the existence of mitigating factors, the trial court nonetheless sentenced according to the matrix. The motion also contended that the trial court had disregarded home detention as an appropriate alternative. Defendant submitted that, in view of his extenuating personal circumstances, the trial court should have exercised its authority under Wis. Stat. § 973.03(4) (2003-04) to order home confinement with electronic monitoring. The appellate court noted that the concern about using an insufficiently proven fact to increase a penalty beyond the statutory maximum was not implicated in this case. The sentencing court considered defendant's refusal to submit to a chemical test only in determining the length of sentence within the statutory limits, not to exceed them. The Sixth Amendment was not implicated because the sentence fell within statutory limits.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order.

State v. Stewart


Appeal Nos. 2005AP979-CR, 2005AP980-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 67; 291 Wis. 2d 480; 713 N.W.2d 165; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 227


February 2, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
March 15, 2006, Decided  
March 15, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and orders of the circuit court for Walworth County: ROBERT J. KENNEDY, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2004CF35, 2003CF519.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgments of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin) convicting him of felony bail jumping under Wis. Stat. § 946.49(1)(b) (2003-04), and felony fleeing and orders denying his postconviction motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to felony bail jumping. The trial court reasoned that the maximum term of probation for a felony bail jumping conviction, a class H felony, was six years in that the maximum term of confinement is three years and the maximum term of extended supervision was three years under Wis. Stat. § 973.01(2)(b) and (d) (2003-04). The trial court then added one year for each of defendant's felony convictions for a total term of probation of eight years pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 973.09(2)(b) (2003-04). The court reversed. The court commuted defendant's eight-year term of probation to a five-year term because § 973.09(2) plainly and unambiguously provided that the maximum term of probation was dependent upon the maximum term of confinement for the crime committed and not, as the trial court held, the maximum term of imprisonment. The maximum term of confinement for a class H felony was three years. Also the condition of probation and extended supervision banishing defendant from a township was unduly restrictive. The dual goals of rehabilitation and protection of the community interest were already functionally accomplished by a more narrowly drawn no contact condition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Racine County, Wisconsin, denying his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2003-2004) motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was found guilty of first-degree intentional homicide for killing a young man who disappeared while soliciting door-to-door. The State's theory was that young man was the victim of "homosexual overkill," and videotapes, photographs and magazines depicting actual murders, mutilation, homosexual acts and other pornography were seized from the petitioner's home and introduced as evidence at trial. 828 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gardner


Case No.: 2005AP1372-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 92; 292 Wis. 2d 682; 715 N.W.2d 720; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 302



March 7, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
April 11, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN A. FRANKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF1249.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of one count of injury by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(am) (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: Defendant crashed his vehicle into a tree, severely injuring his passenger. No alcohol was detected in defendant's blood, but substantial amounts of cocaine and metabolites of cocaine were found. He pled no contest to one count of injury by intoxicated use of a motor vehicle. On appeal, he challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 940.25(1)(am). The court found that the statutory scheme did not create rebuttable and irrebuttable presumptions of guilt. Rather, the statute simply defined a criminal offense and an affirmative defense to that offense. Further, the statute did not create an impermissible "status offense." The statute penalized conduct, not status. A defendant could not be penalized simply for being a drug addict. Finally, § 940.25(2)(a) did not unconstitutionally shift the State's burden of proof to defendant, but rather set forth an affirmative defense. The affirmative defense did not shift to defendant the burden of proving that he was innocent. Rather, it required him to prove that despite the fact that the State had satisfied the elements of the offense, he could not be held legally responsible under the statute. The statute did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Olson (In re Olson)


Appeal No. 2004AP412


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 32; 290 Wis. 2d 202; 712 N.W.2d 61; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 150


December 15, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
February 15, 2006, Decided  
February 15, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Olson, 2006 WI 108, 292 Wis. 2d 410, 718 N.W.2d 723, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 421 (2006)
Subsequent appeal at State v. Olson(In re Olson), 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 339 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 17, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and order and order of the circuit court for Washington County: ANDREW T. GONRING, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CI1.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which committed him to the Wisconsin Department of Health and Family Services pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: In September 2003, the trial court signed an order committing respondent to the Department pursuant to ch. 980. On appeal, respondent claimed that ch. 980 was unconstitutional because its definition of "dangerousness" lacked "a temporal context" limited to "imminent danger." The court found that the Wisconsin Supreme Court had many opportunities to invalidate ch. 980. The court assumed that it did not do so because it did not find the statutory definition of "dangerous" objectionable. Moreover, in the context of ch. 51 commitments, it rejected precisely the "imminence" requirement that respondent advocated. Because mentally disordered sex offenders presented a much greater threat to the public than those committed under ch. 51, the State of Wisconsin had an even greater interest in rejecting an "imminence" requirement in the ch. 980 context. Wis. ch. 980 was not vague just because the legislature did not limit the "foreseeable future" to an arbitrary period of time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

City of Milwaukee Post 2874 v. Redevelopment Auth. of Milwaukee


Appeal No. 2004AP3266


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 56; 290 Wis. 2d 510; 712 N.W.2d 86; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 138



February 14, 2006, Decided  
February 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Milwaukee Post 2874 v. Redevelopment Auth., 2006 WI 126, 297 Wis. 2d 319, 724 N.W.2d 203, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 765 (2006)
Subsequent appeal at Milwaukee City Post #2874 VFW v. Maharishi Vedic Univ., Inc., 2007 WI App 130, 731 N.W.2d 383, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 171 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: FRANCIS T. WASIELEWSKI, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CV9524.
City of Milwaukee Redevelopment Auth. v. VFW Post 2874, 2003 WI App 225, 267 Wis. 2d 960, 671 N.W.2d 717, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 918 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant veteran's post appealed an order dismissing its claim for relocation benefits in appellee city redevelopment authority's eminent-domain proceeding. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granted the authority's motion for summary judgment, because, inter alia, the comparable-replacement-property claim was barred under claim-preclusion because it had been decided by another court's order granting a writ of assistance.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the post argued that the instant trial court erred when it concluded that the post's comparable-replacement-property claim was barred under the doctrine of claim-preclusion. The post sought replacement property "comparable" to its leasehold interest, which, it valued as encompassing its right to pay only $1 per year in rent. The appellate court agreed with the instant trial court that that contention was barred by claim-preclusion. The post could have but had not specifically argued that its $1-per-year rental agreement entitled it to some $ 900,000 more than the $ 300,000 awarded to it in the initial condemnation proceeding. Thus, under claim-preclusion principles it could not do so on appeal. Moreover, the comparable-replacement-property issue had been raised before another court during a writ-of-assistance proceeding. That court ruled, as a predicate to granting the writ, that the authority had offered the post comparable replacement property, despite the post's leasehold right to pay only $1 per year in rent. The appellate court also held that the $ 50,000 limit on business-replacement damages under Wis. Stat. § 32.19(4m)(a) did not violate Wis. Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

831 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Manke v. Physicians Ins. Co. of Wis., Inc.


Appeal No. 2005AP1103


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 50; 289 Wis. 2d 750; 712 N.W.2d 40; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 131


December 7, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
February 9, 2006, Decided  
February 9, 2006, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Manke v. Physicians Ins. Co., 2006 WI 108, 292 Wis. 2d 412, 718 N.W.2d 726, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 498 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for La Crosse County: JOHN J. PERLICH, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV814.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed suit in the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) against, inter alia, defendant doctor alleging medical malpractice. The jury found for plaintiff. The court set aside the verdict and ordered a new trial on the ground that inappropriate material had been introduced into the jury room and it was prejudicial to the defense. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued, inter alia, that the circuit court erred in setting aside the verdict and ordering a new trial based on the dictionary definition of "neglect" brought into the jury room by a juror because the doctor did not make a sufficient preliminary showing to entitle him to an evidentiary hearing at which the jurors testified. The court of appeals disagreed. According to a paralegal's affidavit, the information the juror shared with the other jurors was not his understanding of what negligence meant based on his own experiences. Rather, he read the definition he found in a dictionary. A specific dictionary definition of a word--even a common word--was not the type of general knowledge or accumulated life experiences that jurors were expected to possess. In addition, the only reasonable inference from the jurors' statements in the affidavit was that the dictionary definition the juror read was not part of the trial record but was the result of the juror's independent consultation of a dictionary. Therefore, the dictionary definition of "neglect," that was brought to the jury room and read aloud by another juror, was "extraneous information."


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

832 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Corbisier


Appeal No. 2005AP667-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2006 WI App 56; 290 Wis. 2d 511; 712 N.W.2d 87; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 104



February 7, 2006, Decided  
February 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown County: MARK A.WARPINSKI, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CT1918.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant performed poorly on field sobriety tests, he was arrested for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence obtained from the stop. The Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, granted defendant's motion because the officer failed to corroborate the information provided by the informant before seizing defendant. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended there was no Terry stop and, alternatively, that the officer had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant. The appellate court found that the officer showed his authority when he blocked defendant's ability to leave when he parked his squad in back of defendant. A reasonable person would not have felt free to drive away. As such, defendant was seized for Fourth Amendment purposes. However, the appellate court agreed that the officer had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant based on an informants' tip. As the informant made clear that he personally witnessed the information he was reporting, was not completely anonymous as he approached the officer face-to-face, the appellate court found that the manner in which the tip was conveyed supported its reliability. Further, there were sufficient indicia of reliability to support the informant's tip, independent of any police corroboration. As such, suppression of the evidence was improper.


OUTCOME: The suppression order was reversed and the cause was remanded.

 

833 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Wingo v. Hepp


Appeal No. 2004AP451


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 31; 289 Wis. 2d 548; 710 N.W.2d 725; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 86



January 31, 2006, Decided  
January 31, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Motion denied by Wingo v. Schwartz, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 64184 (E.D. Wis., Sept. 7, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM SOSNAY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CV10619.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner filed three Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (1999-2000) postconviction motions, which were denied. The petitioner then filed the petition that was the subject of the instant appeal. In his petition, the petitioner claimed that the charges against him were unconstitutionally multiplicitous and that his trial attorney was ineffective for failing to preserve that claim for appeal. The circuit court concluded that the petitioner was barred because he was not entitled to pursue habeas corpus relief, and that the petition was barred because the petitioner had filed the same or similar claims in prior postconviction filings and they had been denied. Caselaw provided that all grounds for postconviction relief must be presented in the original postconviction motion and successive motions and appeals, which could have been brought were barred unless there was a sufficient reason for the failure to raise the claims in the original postconviction or appellate proceedings. The appellate court observed no viable basis for declining to apply caselaw simply because the petitioner styled his filing as a habeas corpus petition.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

834 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sigmon


Appeal No. 2004AP3261


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 31; 289 Wis. 2d 549; 710 N.W.2d 725; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 66



January 26, 2006, Decided  
January 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Sigmon, 2006 WI 39, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 280 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sauk County: PATRICK TAGGART, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF47.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pleaded no contest in the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin) to two counts of second-degree sexual assault of a child. After his request for postconviction relief was denied, the petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to withdraw his plea. The court of appeals disagreed. Initially, the court of appeals determined that the plea colloquy was inadequate in that it did not establish the petitioner's understanding of the element "sexual contact or sexual intercourse," and therefore he established a prima facie case for plea withdrawal. However, the motion was properly denied because the fact that the trial court might have misapplied the burden did not require a remand for it to make findings of fact using the proper burden. Counsel specifically stated that he and the petitioner discussed the statutory definition of "sexual contact," including the gratification aspect. In addition, counsel from an earlier case testified at the hearing that he had discussed with the "sexual contact" element in that case, including the sexual gratification part, and that the petitioner was present when the jury was read the instruction that included that definition. The testimony did not appear inherently incredible or internally inconsistent so as to compel rejection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

835 of 1225 DOCUMENTS



Lake Country Racquet & Ath. Club, Inc. v. Morgan


Appeal No. 2004AP3061


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2006 WI App 25; 289 Wis. 2d 498; 710 N.W.2d 701; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 61


May 23, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
January 26, 2006, Decided  
January 26, 2006, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Dane County: ROBERT DE CHAMBEAU, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV6.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff health clubs sought review an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied their motions for summary judgment and awarded summary judgment to defendants, Young Men's Christian Associations (YMCAs), the Wisconsin Department of Revenue, and the Secretary of Revenue, in an action challenging the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 70.11(12)(a) (2003-04), which exempted from taxation property owned by the YMCAs.


OVERVIEW: The clubs brought a suit against defendants, challenging the constitutionality of a portion of § 70.11(12)(a), which exempted from taxation property owned by the YMCAs. The clubs claimed that the statute violated the ban on private legislation in Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18 and the equal protection guarantees of the state and federal constitutions. The trial court denied the clubs' motions for summary judgment and granted defendants' motions for summary judgment. On appeal, the court concluded that the legislature adequately considered the bill and, thus, the bill was entitled to a presumption of constitutionality. Further, because the YMCAs were located in communities throughout Wisconsin and their programs served thousands of individuals, whether they were exempt from taxation was an issue of statewide dimension. Because the challenged part of § 70.11(12) was not private legislation beyond a reasonable doubt, it did not violate Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. The YMCA exemption did not contravene the equal protection guarantees of Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. The clubs and the YMCAs were not similarly situated. The YMCAs were benevolent organizations; the clubs were for-profit businesses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Kenosha County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Katrina R. (In re Quiana T.)


Appeal No. 2005AP1581


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2006 WI App 31; 289 Wis. 2d 551; 710 N.W.2d 726; 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 25



January 17, 2006, Decided  
January 17, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Kenosha County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Katrina R., 2006 WI 108, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 512 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MARY KAY WAGNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003TP74.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which terminated her parental rights to her child and held that she was not denied effective assistance of trial counsel in an action brought by petitioner, a county division of children and family services.


OVERVIEW: The division filed a petition for the termination of the mother's parental rights to her child. The division also sought to terminate the parental rights of the child's father, who was incarcerated. The trial court found that termination of both parents' rights was in the child's best interest. The case was later remanded to the trial court to address the mother's ineffective assistance of counsel claim. The trial court found that counsel was not ineffective. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not lose competency to proceed when the factfinding hearing was set beyond the 45-day requirement in Wis. Stat. § 48.422(2) (2003-04). Good cause in the record, pursuant to § 48.315(2), supported the continuance, and the delay did not exceed what was necessary to accommodate the parties' competing interests and schedules. Further, the mother's plea to the petition was freely and knowingly made. The mother's trial counsel rendered reasonably effective representation. There was no reason to vacate the termination order in the interest of justice. Finally, evidence of the mother's efforts to meet the conditions of return was not wrongly excluded at the dispositional hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State v. Parrish (In re Parrish)


Appeal No. 2005AP564


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 20; 289 Wis. 2d 220; 709 N.W.2d 112; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1140



December 28, 2005, Decided  
December 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at State v. Parrish (In re Commitment of Parrish), 2011 Wisc. App. LEXIS 106 (Wis. Ct. App., Feb. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DAVID A. HANSHER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1998CI12.
State v. Parrish (In re Parrish), 2002 WI App 263, 258 Wis. 2d 521, 654 N.W.2d 273, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1127 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, found defendant to be a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. § 980.05 (2003-04) and committed him to institutional care. Defendant filed a petition seeking discharge from his commitment pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.09 (2003-04), which was denied. He then filed a petition for discharge and a motion to declare the procedures unconstitutional, which were also denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from an order denying his postconviction motion. He claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion, which asserted that Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2003-04) was unconstitutional as applied to African-Americans in Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, and that he should have been entitled to a jury trial at each recommitment level. The appellate court noted that defendant's argument that the statutes governing Wis. Stat. ch. 980 (2003-04) cases were unconstitutional as applied to African-Americans was meritless because he did not explain how the statute discriminated against African-Americans and otherwise violated their constitutional rights. The appellate court held that defendant's petition and motion did not assert that his condition had changed so as to warrant a hearing; rather, it was simply another petition in a series of filings, which was rightfully denied as frivolous by the trial court. The appellate court concluded that there was no basis to extend the Confrontation Clause to a trial court's review of psychological reports and records for the purpose of determining whether to conduct a discharge hearing, which was a civil commitment proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
