Madden v. Bd. of Police & Fire Comm'rs


Appeal No. 2004AP3052


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 31; 289 Wis. 2d 549; 710 N.W.2d 725; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1136



December 22, 2005, Decided  
December 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Madden v. Bd. of Police & Fire Comm'Rs of Madison, 2006 WI 39, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 275 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: John c. albert, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV2158.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner firefighter sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which upheld a decision by respondent, a board of police and fire commissioners, suspending and demoting the firefighter for committing violations of fire department rules. The firefighter had brought his action against the board and respondents, a fire chief and board members.


OVERVIEW: The fire chief filed disciplinary charges against the firefighter pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 62.13(5)(b) (1999-2000). The charges alleged that the firefighter used and possessed cocaine and marijuana, lied to investigators, acted in a way that would bring the fire department into disrepute, failed to report violations of fire department rules to a superior officer, and distributed cocaine. The board found that the firefighter had committed the violations and, with respect to each, imposed a 90-day unpaid suspension and a reduction in rank. The suspensions were ordered to run concurrently. The trial court upheld the board's decision. On appeal, the firefighter argued that the rules under which he was disciplined were unconstitutionally vague as applied. The court found that the record did not show that the fire department or the board failed to previously apply the disputed rules to identified instances of off-duty conduct. The firefighter failed to show that the board allowed off-duty rule violations to go undisciplined. Further, the firefighter could have reasonably expected that suspension and reduction in rank were within the range of authorized penalties for his rule violations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

December 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by State v. Patricia E.K., 2006 WI 23, 712 N.W.2d 39, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 194 (2006)
Appeal dismissed by State v. Patricia E.K., 2006 WI 23, 712 N.W.2d 39, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 195 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the circuit court for Brown County: William M. Atkinson, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2004JC35, 2004JC36.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed disposition orders entered by the Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, finding her children to be in continuing need of protection and services. The mother also appealed the court's denial of her post-adjudication motions in each case.


OVERVIEW: On March 1, 2004, the State filed petitions alleging that the children were in need of protection and services. The petitions alleged abuse, risk of abuse, and neglect. At a hearing on March 15, the mother denied the allegations. A trial date was later set for May 10. On May 7, the mother moved for an adjournment based upon the State's late disclosure of several witnesses. The court granted the adjournment and rescheduled the trial for July 21. On June 25, the mother moved for an adjournment and substitution of counsel. The State objected to any substitution that would further delay the trial and asserted that an adjournment would not be in the best interests of the children; the court agreed and denied the motion. The jury found the children were abused and neglected and in need of protection and services. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of the adjournment under Wis. Stat. § 48.315(2) (2003-04) as the mother conceded it was not in the children's best interests. The decision finding that the children were in need of protection and services was also affirmed as the evidence showed that the mother did not attend counseling sessions recommended by the State.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders were affirmed.

Adams Outdoor Adver. v. City of Madison


Appeal No. 2005AP508


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1099



December 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition granted by Adams Outdoor Adver., Ltd. v. City of Madison, 2006 WI 23, 712 N.W.2d 39, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 201 (2006)
Findings of fact/conclusions of law at, Cause remanded by Adams Outdoor Adver., Ltd. v. City of Madison, 2006 WI 104, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 400 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] CERTIFICATION BY WISCONSIN COURT OF APPEALS. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2003CV777, 2004CV883.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought under Wis. Stat. § 74.37 (2003-04), appellant outdoor advertising company challenged a decision of a circuit court (Wisconsin), which concluded that the company's billboards would be assessed at full market value.


OVERVIEW: When respondent city began placing limits on the number of allowable outdoor signs, the company procured an appraisal estimating the value of its signs using the "cost less depreciation" approach, and the city adopted this appraisal. During the two tax years at issue, the assessor utilized the income approach rejecting the "cost less depreciation" approach. The company contended that the method violated the Uniformity Clause of Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1. The court certified the question to the Wisconsin Supreme Court because there was no direct controlling authority on the question of whether the "income" method or the "cost less depreciation" method was a permissible method for valuing personal property for purposes of the personal property tax when there was no recent sale of the subject property or reasonably comparable sales of other properties.


OUTCOME: The court certified the case to the Wisconsin Supreme Court.

State v. Griese


Appeal No. 2005AP874-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2006 WI App 20; 289 Wis. 2d 220; 709 N.W.2d 112; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1075



December 7, 2005, Decided  
December 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: DALE L. ENGLISH, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF235.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, fourth offense, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2003-2004). Defendant challenged the denial of his motions to suppress evidence on grounds that the officer did not have reasonable suspicion to stop him or probable cause to arrest him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of his motions to suppress, claiming the officer did not have probable cause to stop him because bad weather, darkness and construction combined to produce conditions anyone might have found challenging, and thus the stop was unreasonable; and that he was arrested before sobriety tests were administered. The court noted that although police officers were not required to rule out the possibility of innocent behavior before initiating a brief stop, the officer in this case did not have to consider that possibility because he observed defendant driving in the wrong lane in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.05, and the bad conditions did not diminish the reasonableness of the officer's decision to stop defendant. The court held that, regardless of whether defendant was arrested at the time he was placed in the squad car to go back to the station to finish the sobriety tests due to the bad weather or at the station, probable cause existed for his arrest based on the officer's observation of defendant's driving in the wrong lane, his slurred speech and glossy, bloodshot, and dilated eyes, and his admission that he had been drinking less than two hours before.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

842 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Streff


Appeal No. 2004AP3190-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 1; 288 Wis. 2d 657; 707 N.W.2d 580; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1023



November 23, 2005, Decided  
November 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Streff, 2006 WI 108, 292 Wis. 2d 411, 718 N.W.2d 724, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 454 (2006)
Related proceeding at Streff v. Thurmer, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25775 (E.D. Wis., Mar. 31, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Streff, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 356 (Wis. Ct. App., May 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KAREN E. CHRISTENSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CF3936.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his postconviction motion for sentence modification. Appellant raised a series of arguments challenging the repeater portion of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with recklessly causing his girlfriend's death on July 22, 2001. Appellant acknowledged that he had been convicted of forgery on April 13, 1995, incarcerated until May 2, 1996, and had subsequently spent another 83 days in custody for that offense due to parole violations. Appellant argued that his admissions were insufficient to establish that he had been convicted of a felony within the immediately preceding five-year period because he was actually adjudged guilty of the forgery charge on January 23, 1995, when he entered a plea in that case. The court disagreed. It noted that once a written judgment of conviction had been entered, that document was properly used to establish the date of a prior conviction for purposes of the repeater statute, Wis. Stat. § 939.62(2) (2003-04). The relevant five-year period extended from May 2, 1996, to May 2, 2001, regardless of the fact that one of those years was a leap year. Adding an additional 83 days for time served in relation to parole revocations extended the time period to July 24, 2001. Because appellant committed his offense two days before this time period expired, he was properly sentenced as a repeat offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

State v. Couch


Appeal No. 2005AP1351


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 1; 288 Wis. 2d 659; 707 N.W.2d 580; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1032



November 23, 2005, Decided  
November 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sauk County: GUY D. REYNOLDS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004FO1050.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was cited for littering pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 287.81(2)(a) (2001-02). He was a self-described "artist," and he released over 80 ceramic balls into the Wisconsin River. The Circuit Court for Sauk County, Wisconsin, denied his motion to dismiss the citation. Defendant appealed, asserting that the objects were not "solid waste" under § 287.81(2)(a) or, in the alternative, that said statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant imprinted the subject ceramic balls with various information, purportedly as some type of artistic or communicative endeavor. The circuit court determined that they were salvageable materials under Wis. Stat. § 287.81(2)(a) (2001-02) because they were capable of being "saved for further use." The appellate court impliedly agreed with the circuit court and went on to note that the primary policy concern of Wis. Stat. ch. 287 (2001-02) was that maximum solid waste reduction was in the best interest of the State in order to protect the quality of the natural environment. In short, a material was salvageable if it was capable of being extracted as valuable or as having further usefulness. Said ceramic balls were salvageable, and defendant's depositing same into the river was a violation of Wis. Stat. § 287.81 (2001-02). Secondly, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that § 287.81 was unconstitutionally vague for lack of "proper notice" and an "objective standard for enforcement." A common meaning of "salvageable" included defendant's objects, and the Wisconsin Legislature had given authorities minimal guidelines to determine what behavior violated the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

844 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCoy


Appeal No. 2005AP4-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 1; 288 Wis. 2d 658; 707 N.W.2d 580; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1005



November 17, 2005, Decided  
November 17, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. McCoy, 2006 WI 23, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 114 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DIANE M. NICKS, Judge, and RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Reserve Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CT3621.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, in the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, for operating a vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant appealed, asserting that the police seized her unconstitutionally and that all evidence obtained thereafter should have been suppressed. She also argued that she was placed in police custody and that all statements she made should have been suppressed because she did not receive Miranda warnings.


OVERVIEW: The record showed an officer was able to follow a trail of leaking fluid from the scene of an accident to a nearby home where he spotted a car with fresh damage. At the home, the officer spoke to defendant's husband who stated that defendant, his wife, had been driving the car. Defendant's husband testified that he felt he had no choice but to retrieve his wife from inside their home. On the other hand, he had not raised any objections to the officer's request. Defendant agreed to talk to the officer and she admitted that she had been driving the car. The appellate court held: (1) defendant was not "seized" so as to have invoked the protections of the Fourth Amendment where she had submitted herself to questioning by the officer; (2) she was not "seized" by the police, with her husband acting as their agent, again, since she consented to the encounter with the officer, and because under the totality of the circumstances, a reasonable person would have believed they were free to remain within their home; and (3) defendant was not "in custody" where most of the questioning occurred outside her home, and where she was never told she was under arrest and she was not handcuffed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. McGhee


2005AP504-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1165



November 16, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER EDITING. IF PUBLISHED, THE OFFICIAL VERSION WILL APPEAR IN THE BOUND VOLUME OF THE OFFICIAL REPORTS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. McGhee, 2009 WI App 56, 317 Wis. 2d 730, 768 N.W.2d 62, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 182 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
(L.C. # 2004CF1962).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a Wisconsin trial court of armed robbery, theft of movable property and operating a motor vehicle without the owner's consent. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the trial court violated his constitutional right to present a defense by not allowing him to call two belatedly disclosed alibi witnesses. The appellate court noted that defendant was allowed to testify that he was elsewhere at the time of the crimes. He was precluded only from presenting testimony in support of his alibi from witnesses that he had not disclosed to the State until the morning of the trial. The appellate court found that the trial court's finding that the State struck a juror for non-discriminatory reasons was not clearly erroneous. The State's explanation that it struck the prospective juror based on her comment or question to defense counsel during voir dire, which the prosecutor interpreted as demonstrating a predisposition to believe defendant's version of events, met the requirement that the State proffer a plausible, non-discriminatory reasons for its strike. So long as the trial court found the prosecutor's explanation credible, which it did, the court did not err in rejecting defendant's Batson challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lackershire


Appeal No. 2005AP1189-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 265; 288 Wis. 2d 609; 707 N.W.2d 891; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 996


October 3, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
November 15, 2005, Decided  
November 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Lackershire, 2006 WI 23, 289 Wis. 2d 9, 712 N.W.2d 34, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 30 (2006)
Reversed by, Cause remanded by State v. Lackershire, 2007 WI 74, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 403 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Pepin County, Wisconsin, accepted defendant's plea to second-degree sexual assault of a child, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2), sentenced her to three years of initial confinement plus six years of extended supervision, and denied her postconviction motion for plea withdrawal or resentencing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the plea colloquy was deficient because the elements of the crime were not incorporated in the plea questionnaire or discussed or recited on the record at the time of the plea taking. The court disagreed. The record revealed that the trial court did explain the elements of the crime, in the plain, easily understood language of the statute. The court also found that the plea was valid, even if defendant did not understand that dismissed charges would be treated as read-ins. Because read-ins did not increase the range of punishment, they were indirect consequences, and knowledge of them was not required for a defendant to enter a knowing, intelligent, or voluntary plea. Finally, defendant did not establish that her plea was coerced by showing that a prosecutor with no jurisdiction over the docket would have resisted her request for a trial postponement due to problems with a pregnancy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

Barlow v. Bd. of Police & Fire Comm'rs


Appeal No. 2004AP2614


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2006 WI App 1; 288 Wis. 2d 657; 707 N.W.2d 579; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 986



November 10, 2005, Decided  
November 10, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: JOHN C. ALBERT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CV2217.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Responder, a city board of police and fire commissioners, found that as a result of a police investigation, appellant firefighter had continually used and possessed cocaine over a 12-year period, had distributed cocaine on several occasions, and had aided in its manufacture on one occasion. The board discharged the firefighter. He appealed, and the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) affirmed the board. The firefighter appealed.


OVERVIEW: The firefighter made an as-applied vagueness challenge. He claimed that the board's previous application of the rules failed to give him fair notice that his off-duty conduct was a violation of the rules and subjected him to removal as a firefighter. To conclude that a rule was unconstitutionally vague as applied required a record that showed that the past application of the rules would have led a person to believe that the conduct at issue was not subject to the discipline imposed. In the case at bar, the record did not show that the fire department or the board failed to previously apply the disputed rules to identified instances of off-duty conduct. The only significant evidence the firefighter pointed to was testimony before the board by a fire department lieutenant whose testimony did not show that, under the rules, previous off-duty drug violations were not subject to discipline. The record did not reflect that someone engaging in conduct comparable to the firefighter's was or was not discharged. The appellate court held that under the rules, the firefighter could have reasonably expected that dismissal was within the range of authorized penalties for his rule violations.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

848 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smet


Appeal No. 2005AP690-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 263; 288 Wis. 2d 525; 709 N.W.2d 474; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 978


September 29, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
November 9, 2005, Decided  
November 9, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Smet, 2006 WI 23, 712 N.W.2d 37, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 145 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: PETER L. GRIMM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CT485.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for operating a motor vehicle with "a detectable amount of a restricted controlled substance" in his blood, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(am) (2003-04), in the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Wisconsin. He appealed, asserting that the statute exceeded the scope of the Wisconsin Legislature's police power and thus violated the constitutional guarantees of due process, fundamental fairness, and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(am) (2003-04), which required only proof of "a detectable amount" of a banned substance and not proof of impairment, represented an unconstitutional overstep by the Wisconsin Legislature in the exercise of its police power. That overstep, he submitted, violated his rights to due process and fundamental fairness. However, the appellate court found defendant did not shoulder his heavy burden of demonstrating unconstitutionality beyond a reasonable doubt. Indisputably, regulating the safety of Wisconsin roadways was a proper exercise of the police power. The appellate court held that the per se ban on driving or operating a motor vehicle with a detectable amount of a restricted controlled substance in one's blood, as set out in § 346.63(1)(am), bore a reasonable and rational relationship to the latter goal and was not fundamentally unfair, such that there was no due process violation. The appellate court also held that the statute did not offend principles of equal protection since defendant did not establish that the statute either interfered with a fundamental right or operated to the peculiar disadvantage of a suspect class.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State ex rel. White v. Schwarz


Appeal No. 2004AP2314


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2006 WI App 1; 288 Wis. 2d 657; 707 N.W.2d 579; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 983



November 8, 2005, Decided  
November 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. White v. Schwarz, 2006 WI 23, 289 Wis. 2d 10, 712 N.W.2d 35, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 65 (2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied State ex rel. White v. McCash, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 706 (Wis. Ct. App., Aug. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL GUOLEE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV4529.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner probationer sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which affirmed the revocation of his parole and probation and also denied his motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the affirmation of the revocation of the probationer's parole and probation, the appellate court affirmed. The administrative law judge was persuaded that the hearsay was reliable pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 911.01(4)(c) (2003-04), and the court concluded that its findings were supported by substantial evidence. The probation/parole agent testified that she called the probationer's aunt, who arranged for the probationer's cousin to call the agent, and that the cousin told the agent that he had not asked the probationer to install a car stereo. This was certainly plausible, despite the probationer's assertions that his cousin was lying to avoid becoming involved. Moreover, even without the hearsay, there was sufficient evidence to support the findings. A reasonable factfinder could have concluded that a man walking the streets at 3:30 in the morning, in possession of burglar's tools and a used car stereo, was not actually intending to install a car stereo in the middle of the night. The fact that the probationer was driven to the home he was supposed to be walking to and the homeowner said that the cousin no longer lived there only bolstered such a finding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Goetzka v. City of Black River Falls


Appeal No. 2004AP2917


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 254; 288 Wis. 2d 460; 706 N.W.2d 703; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 923



October 20, 2005, Decided  
October 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Goetzka v. City of Black River Falls, 2006 WI 23, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 94 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 2003CV8. APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jackson County: John A. Damon, Judge.
Town of Brockway v. City of Black River Falls, 2005 WI App 174, 702 N.W.2d 418, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 583 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city annexed respondent developer's land and created a tax incremental financing (TIF) district. The land was zoned as light industrial, and the developer's project plan was approved. Appellants, certain taxpayers and the town where the land was located before the annexation, challenged the TIF district. The Circuit Court for Jackson County, Wisconsin, granted the city's motion for summary judgment. The taxpayers and the town appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the taxpayers and the town contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in accepting the joint review board's finding that the expected development in the district would not occur without use of the tax incremental financing and erred in construing the "not less than 50 percent" requirement in Wis. Stat. § 66.1105(4)(gm)4.a (2001-02) as it related to industrial use. The appellate court found that because the complaint did not name the joint review board as a defendant, the trial court properly granted summary judgment on this issue. Further, the city's finding under § 66.1105(4)(gm)4.a. was based on a proper construction of the statute: the policy of encouraging and promoting the development of industry was furthered by requiring that one of the categories making up at least 50 percent of the district was property that was suitable for industrial use and zoned for that use in order for the municipality to have the benefit of TIF for public improvements and development assistance. This requirement promoted the development of industrial uses over other types of land use, even though it did not promote the development of industrial uses to the exclusion of other uses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Xiong


Appeal No. 2004AP1832-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2005 WI App 254; 288 Wis. 2d 459; 706 N.W.2d 702; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 882



October 11, 2005, Decided  
October 11, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Xiong, 2006 WI 23, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 55 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Marathon County: PATRICK M. BRADY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF394.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Marathon County, Wisconsin, convicting him of attempted first-degree intentional homicide and four counts of first-degree recklessly endangering safety by use of a dangerous weapon, with a penalty enhancer on the reckless endangerment counts as criminal gang crimes contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 940.01(1)(a), 939.32, 939.63, 941.30(1) (2003-2004) and 939.625 (2001-2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose from an incident at a party in which members of the first gang were involved in a fight with a member of a second gang. A first gang member allegedly stabbed a second gang member. Witnesses told police that defendant fired a gun five times into the crowd, hitting three people. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to preclude the State from referring to him by his nickname, "Shotgun." The appellate court ruled that although use of the nickname "Shotgun" at trial could have been prejudicial, it was not unfairly so. The record demonstrated that many of the witnesses had nicknames, and witnesses would inevitably have referred to defendant by his nickname because that was the only name by which they knew him. Further, defense witnesses explained that "Shotgun" was the name of defendant's tattoo business, and perhaps the name of a style of tattoos. Also, a reasonable jury could find that defendant's words and conduct in conjunction with the first gang's battering and stabbing someone they believed was a rival gang member were sufficient to prove defendant's intent to promote or assist the first gang's criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. S. M. L. (In the Interest of S.M.L.)


Appeal No. 2005AP792


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 233; 287 Wis. 2d 829; 705 N.W.2d 906; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 852



September 29, 2005, Decided  
September 29, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SHELLEY J. GAYLORD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004JV192.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile was adjudicated delinquent on two counts fourth-degree sexual assault. As part of the disposition, the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, entered an order compelling him to provide a DNA sample to the Wisconsin Department of Justice pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 938.34(15) (2003-04). Respondent appealed.


OVERVIEW: Respondent argued that it was arbitrary, and therefore a violation of the Equal Protection Clause, to require a DNA sample from delinquent juveniles who had been convicted of fourth-degree sexual assault, while excusing similarly convicted adults and waived juveniles from providing a sample under identical circumstances. The court disagreed, finding that the requirement for juveniles was rationally related to two stated goals of the Juvenile Justice Code, specifically protection of the public and prevention of delinquency. Further, expansion of the DNA databank served the purpose of aiding in the identification of perpetrators of crime. Finally, the significant differences between the juvenile and adult justice systems provided a rational basis for the dissimilar classification. The court also found that respondent, by failing to file a reply brief countering the State's arguments, conceded that he failed to file a timely notice of appeal challenging the circuit court's denial of his request for a stay of the DNA requirement. Under Wis. Stat. § 809.83(2), the delay was grounds for dismissal of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court on the equal protection issue and dismissed the remainder of the appeal.

State ex rel. Pharm v. Bartow


Appeal No. 2004AP583


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 215; 287 Wis. 2d 663; 706 N.W.2d 693; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 812


August 10, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
September 21, 2005, Decided  
September 21, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State ex rel. Pharm v. Bartow, 2006 WI 39, 290 Wis. 2d 20, 712 N.W.2d 895, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 220 (2006)
Affirmed by State ex rel. Pharm v. Bartow, 2007 WI 13, 298 Wis. 2d 702, 727 N.W.2d 1, 2007 Wisc. LEXIS 6 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cir. Ct. No. 2004IP1. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: BRUCE SCHMIDT, Judge.
State v. Pharm (In re Pharm), 2000 WI App 167, 238 Wis. 2d 97, 617 N.W.2d 163, 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 563 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant had previously been serving a life sentence in Nevada. During that period he was also convicted of a crime in Wisconsin. He brought a habeas corpus action in the Circuit Court for Winnebago County, Wisconsin, claiming that his Wis. Stat. ch. 980 commitment as a sexually violent person was unconstitutional because it violated the Interstate Agreement on Detainers (IAD). The circuit court rejected his request for discharge. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: During the time appellant was serving his Wisconsin sentence, the Nevada authorities had periodically wrote to the Wisconsin Department of Corrections, reminding them that he was still under parole supervision in Nevada and that Nevada was to be informed of any impending release of appellant. When he was scheduled for mandatory release from his Wisconsin sentences, the State of Wisconsin commenced the commitment proceeding. The appellate court held that appellant's waiver of extradition and the IAD expressly gave Wisconsin the right to his custody to serve his Wisconsin sentence. At the completion of that sentence, the scope and purpose of his waiver of extradition and the IAD were satisfied and completed. Nothing in his waiver of extradition or the IAD governed or guaranteed future events. Specifically, he had no right or legitimate expectation that he would be returned to Nevada upon the completion of his Wisconsin sentence. Similarly, he had no right or legitimate expectation of immunization from potential commitment proceedings under Wis. Stat. ch. 980. Thus, his waiver of extradition and the IAD did not bar the Wis. Stat. ch. 980 commitment proceedings against him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's order denying appellant habeas corpus relief.

State v. Jones


Appeal No. 2004AP3333-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2005 WI App 233; 287 Wis. 2d 829; 705 N.W.2d 906; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 791



September 14, 2005, Decided  
September 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: ROBERT J. WIRTZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF127.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a guilty plea, the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of possession of cocaine and possession of marijuana, both as party to a crime and as a habitual offender. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion to suppress evidence collected during the search of a vehicle in which he was a passenger.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the vehicle and its occupants were unconstitutionally detained on a hunch after a speeding ticket was issued, completing the purpose of the stop. The court disagreed, concluding that the officers provided specific, articulable facts to support the reasonable suspicion that criminal activity was afoot and thus to justify the continued detention under the Fourth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. Specifically, the driver had red, glassy eyes, an odor of incense emanated from the vehicle, the officer's experience was that air fresheners could be used to mask the odor of marijuana, and the occupants of the vehicle were acting nervous. Although a preliminary breath test established that alcohol was not the reason for the driver's red, glassy eyes, an officer testified that marijuana was another likely cause. The court also found that the officers had probable cause to search the vehicle because the odor of burnt marijuana created an inference that marijuana was physically present and had been smoked recently. Other facts to support probable cause included the presence of air fresheners and the red and glassy eyes and nervous demeanors of the occupants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction and the order denying the motion to suppress.

State v. Herfel


Appeal No. 2004AP3121-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 233; 287 Wis. 2d 828; 705 N.W.2d 906; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 758



September 1, 2005, Decided  
September 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Iowa County: WILLIAM D. DYKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CM7.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Iowa County, Wisconsin, convicting her of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), third offense, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2001-2002).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that her current conviction should not be treated as a third offense because her second conviction was unconstitutionally obtained. Defendant alleged that in the prior proceeding she was denied, and did not waive, her constitutional right to an attorney. Defendant's motion to collaterally attack her prior OWI conviction was denied by the circuit court because it concluded that defendant had failed to make a prima facie case that her right to counsel had been violated. After the circuit court denied the motion, defendant proceeded to a stipulated trial. The appellate court ruled that defendant made a prima facie showing of a constitutional violation of her right to counsel. Rather than address defendant's assertion that she did not waive counsel at all, the circuit court reviewed the case law and concluded that defendant's waiver of counsel was valid. In effect, the circuit court assumed waiver without resolving whether any waiver took place. The appellate court stated that the circuit court would have to assess defendant's credibility, and make a factual finding on the topic.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded with directions.

Kaul v. St. Mary's Hosp.-Ozaukee


Appeal No. 2004AP849


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2005 WI App 214; 287 Wis. 2d 507; 704 N.W.2d 423; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 756



August 31, 2005, Decided  
August 31, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Ozaukee County: JOSEPH D. MCCORMACK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1999CV360.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents' medical malpractice suit alleging their newborn son's brain damage was caused by defendant hospital's negligence resulted in a no causation verdict. The Circuit Court for Ozaukee County, Wisconsin, granted the parents a new trial on the issue of causation because of confusion caused by the jury instructions. The second trial resulted in a verdict for the parents, awarding them damages. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the hospital claimed the trial court erred in granting the parents a new trial and in awarding past medical expenses. The parents challenged the amount of post-verdict interest and the cap on noneconomic damages. The appellate court determined that a new trial was warranted as the jury found the hospital's negligence was not causal but then was entered damages caused by the hospital's treatment; this inconsistency could only have arisen from jury confusion as to the instructions. Causation was a critical inquiry because of the progressive development of the son's condition, and the omitted causation paragraph would have provided the jury with critical information on that inquiry. The appellate court also held that post-verdict interest ran from the first jury verdict. Further, because the jury did not exclude the past medical expenses paid by collateral sources, the parents were entitled to judgment for those sums. Finally, reducing noneconomic damages by the statutory cap in Wis. Stat. § 655.017 (2003-04) was unconstitutional because it violated the equal protection guarantees of the Wisconsin Constitution as per a recent Wisconsin Supreme Court decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in part and remanded with directions that judgment be entered in favor of the parents in an amount not reduced by the cap on noneconomic damages and to include post-verdict interest the first jury verdict. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed. The parents were awarded appeal costs.

State v. Montroy


Appeal Nos. 2004AP3249-CR, 2004AP3250-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 230; 287 Wis. 2d 430; 706 N.W.2d 145; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 748


June 20, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
August 30, 2005, Decided  
August 30, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Montroy, 2006 WI 3, 286 Wis. 2d 663, 708 N.W.2d 694, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 1034 (2005)
Review denied by State v. Montroy, 2006 WI 3, 286 Wis. 2d 663, 708 N.W.2d 694, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 1033 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Pepin County: DANE F. MOREY, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2003CF14, 2003CF16.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for burglary and cocaine possession with intent to deliver in the Circuit Court for Pepin County, Wisconsin. The trial court denied his postconviction motion for sentence modification. He appealed, asserting that his presentence investigation report (PSI) contained inaccurate information. He asserted the PSI incorrectly stated he was convicted of first-degree sexual assault and included too many juvenile adjudications.


OVERVIEW: The State conceded the third (and final) PSI contained inaccurate information. However, it contended the trial court properly struck the sexual assault conviction and pending bail jumping charge. It also argued that the trial court properly considered two juvenile adjudications where defendant was not represented by counsel. The appellate court noted that defendant's accurate criminal record, which did not include the sexual assault conviction or pending bail jumping charges, was lengthy. Thus, the trial court did not have to rely on inaccurate information to reach its conclusion. Secondly, even though the trial court essentially adopted the PSIs sentencing recommendation, the trial court did not demonstrate that it relied on inaccuracies. The two unrepresented juvenile adjudications should not have been included in the PSI; however, the trial court was nevertheless entitled to consider those adjudications. Finally, while defendant was not per se ineligible for an earned release program, the trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying same based on his criminal history, and his sentence, within the statutory limits, did not conflict with Blakely v. Washington.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

State ex rel. West v. Frank

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR

August 25, 2005, Decided  
August 25, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by, Motion denied by, Claim dismissed by West v. Frank, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 49417 (W.D. Wis., July 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: John C. Albert, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CV881.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, dismissed appellant prisoner's complaint against respondents, prison employees, whereupon the prisoner alleged that the employees violated his First Amendment and other rights by preventing him from receiving a newspaper. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court concluded that the complaint failed to state a claim because the alleged policy was reasonably related to a legitimate penological interest. The prisoner argued that the circuit court erred by concluding at the complaint stage, before the employees had offered any justification for the alleged policy, that there was a legitimate penological interest. The appellate court determined that the four-part test found in a previous case was the method by which the appellate court determined whether there was a legitimate penological interest. The prisoner alleged the broad outlines of the no-publications policy as it applied to him, but the actual policy was not before the appellate court. It could not be determined from only the face of the complaint what the employees' precise policy was and whether it was reasonably related to a legitimate penological interest. The circuit court did not err in dismissing the prisoner's other claims where he cited no authority holding that it was an establishment of religion for the State to include Christian programming among the choices.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Kohl v. DeWitt Ross & Stevens (In re Kohl v Zeitlin)


Appeal No. 2004AP328


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 196; 287 Wis. 2d 289; 704 N.W.2d 586; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 698


August 5, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
August 11, 2005, Decided  
August 11, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001FA2105.
Kohl v. Dewitt Ross & Stevens (In re Kohl v. Zeitlin), 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 315 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 14, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, that awarded attorney fees to respondents, her former law firm and counsel, in her divorce action.


OVERVIEW: During the course of her divorce proceeding, the client was represented by respondents. Following the trial court's entry of the judgment of divorce and the resolution of the financial issues, respondents moved to withdraw citing difficulty in their communication with the client. At the time respondents moved to withdraw, there was still pending a trial for resolution of the custody issues. Respondents also requested a judgment against the client in the amount of $14,768 in attorney fees at the time they moved to withdraw. The client did not immediately hire a new attorney to represent her in the action. In reviewing Wis. Stat. § 767.23(3)(a) (2003-04), the appellate court held that § 767.23(3)(a) gave the trial court in an action affecting the family the authority to enter a judgment for the fees owed by the client to an attorney who was permitted by order of the court to withdraw, regardless of when or if the client retained another attorney to replace the withdrawing attorney in that action. Thus, the award of attorney fees was affirmed even though the client did not immediately hire a new attorney.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Strenke v. Hogner


Appeal No. 2003AP2527


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 194; 287 Wis. 2d 135; 704 N.W.2d 309; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 671


April 4, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
August 2, 2005, Decided  
August 2, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Strenke v. Hogner, 2006 WI 3, 286 Wis. 2d 660, 708 N.W.2d 692, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 968 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hogner v. Strenke, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2670 (U.S., Feb. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Barron County: FREDERICK A. HENDERSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CV179.
Strenke v. Hogner, 2005 WI 25, 279 Wis. 2d 52, 694 N.W.2d 296, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 136 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to a decision of the Circuit Court for Barron County, Wisconsin, defendants, an insured and his insurer, appealed a portion of a judgment awarding punitive damages to plaintiff injured person for a car accident that occurred when the insured was driving while drunk (he was a repeat offender). The insured asserted the award was so excessive that it violated his due process rights under the United States and Wisconsin Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: As to the instant case, previously, the instant court had certified questions to the Wisconsin Supreme Court. The supreme court had remanded the case on the question of whether the punitive damages award violated the insured's due process rights. At trial, the jury had found that the insured had acted with intentional disregard. Further, although the injured person had been awarded only $ 2,000 in compensatory damages, the jury awarded $225,000 in punitive damages. The appellate court applied the guideposts set forth in BMW of N. Am., Inc. v. Gore State, the clarification of same set forth in Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Campbell, and the similar Wisconsin test set forth in Trinity Evangelical Luth. Ch. v. Tower Ins., to determine whether the award in the case at bar was constitutional. The appellate court held that like the award in Trinity, the punitive damage award in the instant case served a legitimate state interest in punishment and deterrence in its own jurisdiction. Further, the degree of reprehensibly was the most important factor in any excessiveness inquiry, and the conduct in the case qualified as egregious. Thus, the award was not grossly excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment for punitive damages entered in the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Weimer


Appeal No. 2005AP771-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2005 WI App 193; 287 Wis. 2d 134; 703 N.W.2d 384; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 643



July 26, 2005, Decided  
July 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Weimer, 2006 WI 3, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 1050 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: William D. Gardner, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CM7812.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant offered to pay a woman, who was actually an undercover police officer, a sum of money for sex. He was subsequently convicted for solicitation in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin. He appealed, asserting that there was no proof of what he meant by offering to pay "for sex" and, therefore, the intent element of solicitation for prostitution was not established. He also raised constitutional arguments.


OVERVIEW: In part, defendant argued that his reference to "sex" could have been a reference to, for example, "phone sex." Thus, he asserted that if all he was exploring was whether the woman was willing to call him later that day and make obscene remarks, there was no violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.30. However, the circumstances included defendant circling the block numerous times, and then asking the officer if she was a cop. He then made a proposal of sex for $20. The officer testified that, based on her experience, a prostitute in the vicinity typically charged $20 for sexual intercourse. The appellate court noted the trial court properly found that it could have inferred defendant's intent from his words and actions. If the test had been otherwise, a defendant could always defeat a solicitation charge by testifying that his or her subjective intent, when offering money "for sex," was really to take the other person to a movie or to dinner. Finally, § 944.30 was not unconstitutionally vague because a factfinder had to consider all of the surrounding facts and circumstances; merely uttering the word "sex" would not be sufficient to sustain a conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Reversed by State v. Booker, 2006 WI 79, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 373 (2006)

.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of exposing a child to harmful materials and two counts of second-degree sexual assault, contrary to Wis. Am. Eagle Ins. Co. v. Wis. Ins. Sec. Fund


Appeal No. 2004AP274


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 177; 286 Wis. 2d 689; 704 N.W.2d 44; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 637


September 23, 2004, Oral Argument  
July 21, 2005, Decided  
July 21, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: WILLIAM D. JOHNSTON, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 1998CV135, 2001CV3496, 2002CV2571.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant reinsurance corporation, a reinsurer of town mutual insurance companies, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) affirming a $ 15,047 assessment against the reinsurer by appellee Wisconsin Insurance Security Fund (Fund) and dismissing an action alleging procedural infirmities. The reinsurer contended that the Fund exceeded its statutory grant of authority by its assessment.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, the Fund asserted that Wis. Stat. § 646.31(2)(a)1. (2001-02) permitted town mutuals to submit claims to the Fund, and consequently subjected the insurers of town mutuals to assessment under Wis. Stat. § 646.51(3)(am)2. Because the reinsurer and the Fund each offered reasonable interpretations of Wis. Stat. § 646.31(2)(a), the statute was ambiguous. The court therefore turned to extrinsic sources to ascertain the statute's meaning. The court agreed with the Fund's contention that the 1979 comment and 1987 legislative reference bureau (LRB) analysis clarified that under § 646.31(2)(a), a town mutual ceding certain risks with a reinsurer could make a claim with the Fund for those risks if the reinsurer went into liquidation. Accordingly, under the assessment scheme of Wis. Stat. ch. 646, the Fund had the authority to assess reinsurance companies of town mutuals, an authority it had to exercise to ensure the Fund's solvency. The legislative history of the statute showed the intent to permit assessment of the reinsurer. The reinsurer waived most of its objections to the Fund's procedures, and those procedural objections it had not waived were rejected.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Yourchuck Video, Inc. v. Burnett County


Appeal No. 2004AP2345


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2005 WI App 193; 287 Wis. 2d 133; 703 N.W.2d 383; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 588



July 6, 2005, Decided  
July 6, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Burnett County: ROBERT H. RASMUSSEN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV6.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Burnett County, Wisconsin, dismissed appellant corporation's claims against appellee county after the corporation challenged the constitutionality of the county's sign ordinance. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before moving to a new building, the corporation applied for a permit to construct a new sign. The county denied the application because the proposed sign did not comply with the ordinance, Burnett County, Wis., Ordinance No. 2000-01. The ordinance did not include a variance procedure. The corporation argued that the county ordinance violated its right to due process under the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The appellate court noted that the county's only response to the corporation's constitutional argument was that certiorari provided an adequate post-deprivation remedy. The county effectively conceded the two premises of the corporation's argument: it was deprived of a constitutionally protected property interest, and due process of law was not provided before the deprivation. Because the ordinance had no variance or exception procedure, there was no hearing to present evidence or arguments. There was no relief a certiorari court could even consider.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

Kartes v. Kartes


Appeal No. 2004AP1974


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2005 WI App 193; 287 Wis. 2d 133; 703 N.W.2d 383; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 592



July 6, 2005, Decided  
July 6, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: ROBERT G. MAWDSLEY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003FA339.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) entered a judgment of divorce. Appellant mother challenged that portion of the judgment awarding the parties equal physical placement of their child and requiring her to make a $ 7,500 contribution to appellee father's attorney fees based on overtrial.


OVERVIEW: At the commencement of its placement decision, the trial court noted its concern for the young child being overexposed to the hostility between the parents, particularly during transitions between parents. Restricting transitions was a goal of the placement arrangement. Implicit was the finding that transitions at the day care, which would occur on two of the three required transitions, would be easier for the child because there would be little interparental contact. Further, there was evidence that placement in day care was good for the child. In addition, the trial court found that the child was able to adjust to both parental environments. Furthermore, the proper factors were taken into consideration. Thus, the placement decision was a proper exercise of discretion. With regards to the overtrial, the mother's overall lack of candor with the trial court permeated the entire trial. Also, the record supported the trial court's finding that with respect to the financial matters the mother engaged in unreasonable litigation. However, the trial court failed to make the required finding that the amount of attorney fees awarded - $ 7,500 - was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the child placement decision, but reversed the contribution award and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings on the contribution award.

State v. Muller


Appeal No. 2004AP2987-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2005 WI App 193; 287 Wis. 2d 134; 703 N.W.2d 384; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 605



July 6, 2005, Decided  
July 6, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Walworth County: JOHN R. RACE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CM113.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which convicted her of possession of tetrahydrocannabinols (THC or marijuana), contrary to Wis. Stat. § 961.41(3g)(e), and carrying a concealed weapon, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.23. On appeal, defendant contended that the search of his vehicle violated his Fourth Amendment rights and that all evidence obtained in that search should have been suppressed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was one of three people involved in a minor traffic accident. Defendant was belligerent and uncooperative after the other two people called police to the scene. The officer requested permission to search defendant's vehicle. Defendant twice refused to give the officer permission to search the vehicle, but defendant said he would not prevent the search. The officer then failed to advise defendant that he could refuse consent to the search of his vehicle's console. Upon opening the console, the officer noticed the barrel of a gun. On appeal, the court concluded that the officer's warrantless search of defendant's vehicle, without defendant's unequivocal consent, violated the Fourth Amendment. Furthermore, the search of a vehicle included the search of the console, and, therefore, the officer's search of the console of defendant's vehicle was tainted by the original illegal act. Finally, the court held that any consent from defendant to search the console was invalid; no intervening event attenuated the illegal vehicle search from the console search.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

State v. James


Appeal No. 2004AP2391-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2005 WI App 188; 285 Wis. 2d 783; 703 N.W.2d 727; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 610


May 16, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
July 6, 2005, Decided  
July 6, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. James, 2005 WI 150, 286 Wis. 2d 100, 705 N.W.2d 661, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 849 (2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by James v. Wisconsin, 126 S. Ct. 1060, 163 L. Ed. 2d 885, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 645 (U.S., Jan. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: Bruce E. Schroeder, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2004CF470.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which sustained defendant's objection to the introduction of videotaped statements of two child witnesses in a sexual assault trial.


OVERVIEW: The action arose when the State, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 908.08 (2003-04), sought to introduce the videotaped statements of two child witnesses in a sexual assault trial in lieu of full-blown live direct examination and to subsequently make the children available for questioning at the defendant's request. The trial court sustained defendant's objection to this mode of testimonial presentation, observing that in its past experience, child witnesses sometimes refused to submit to cross-examination, thereby necessitating a mistrial in order to avert a violation of defendant's Sixth Amendment right. Invoking Wis. Stat. §§ 904.03, 906.11 and 908.08(3) (2003-04), the trial court required any live testimony to occur first. The court reversed and remanded with instructions, stating that what was really at issue was the separation of legislative and judicial powers. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 908.08 represented a proper exercise of legislative power and that the statute was not trumped by Wis. Stat. §§ 904.03 and 906.11. Thus, the trial court was not permitted to dictate alternative procedures based on the mere specter of a possible Crawford violation in the future.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded with directions.

State v. Pierce


Appeal No. 2004AP2236-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2005 WI App 176; 285 Wis. 2d 806; 701 N.W.2d 653; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 568



June 28, 2005, Decided  
June 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Pierce, 2005 WI 150, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 840 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN J. DiMOTTO and MICHAEL B. BRENNAN, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 2004AP002236.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) found defendant guilty of two counts of second-degree sexual assault of a child, Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2). After the trial court improperly sentenced defendant, on resentencing, the trial court imposed the maximum, 10 years of imprisonment on each count, to run consecutively. Subsequently, the trial court denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant was arrested some five to five-and-one-half years after he allegedly last assaulted the victim, that, standing alone, did not make the charges constitutionally insufficient. Also, although the charged acts of sexual assault were alleged to have happened over five-and-one-half month and four-and-one-half month time periods, defendant was sufficiently informed of the charges against him. Thus, the complaint was not constitutionally insufficient. Additionally, defendant's alleged crimes were different in fact; thus, the charges were not multiplicitous. In addition, other-acts evidence was permissible to show the context of the crime and provide an explanation of the case, and to show a plan. Furthermore, the probative value of the evidence was not substantially outweighed by any unfair prejudice to defendant. Finally, the trial court considered the appropriate factors and explained why maximum consecutive sentences were warranted because the trial court (1) considered the devastating effect that the assaults had on the victim and his family; and (2) determined that defendant needed to be punished, and that the community needed to be protected from further assaults.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

870 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Smith v. Swenson


Appeal Nos. 2004AP2518, 2004AP2519


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2005 WI App 176; 285 Wis. 2d 806; 701 N.W.2d 653; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 555



June 23, 2005, Decided  
June 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. Smith v. Swenson, 2005 WI 150, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 856 (2005)
Review denied by State ex rel. Smith v. Swenson, 2005 WI 150, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 857 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: Daniel L. Konkol, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2004CV3777, 2001CF3412.
State v. Smith, 267 Wis. 2d 278, 670 N.W.2d 557, 2003 WI App 201, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 770 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for second-degree sexual assault and child enticement-exposure of a sex organ in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin. He appealed from an order denying relief on his petition for a writ of habeas corpus and denying his postconviction motion under Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2003-04). The trial court rejected arguments that he received ineffective assistance from his postconviction counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted he was unconstitutionally deprived of counsel at the time of the blood draw. However, the State drew the blood before charging defendant, and therefore before his right to counsel accrued. In any event, the State obtained the sample pursuant to a search warrant, and he did not challenge the probable cause determination thereon. The appellate court also rejected his claim that the State withheld photographs of the victim that would have impeached testimony that she came away from their encounter with visible bruises, and that counsel failed to raise the issue. In that respect, the photographs were not of record. His claim that they are exculpatory rested on nothing more than his conclusory allegation. Defendant also contended that counsel should have called a police detective to testify he did not observe the physical injuries that other witnesses attributed to the victim. However, the officer had testified that he never looked for said injuries. Finally, defendant's assertion that counsel was ineffective for making inappropriate remarks at closing, as to the "despicable" nature of defendant's act, in no way undermined the defense, where same was based on consent.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.
