State v. Draughon


Appeal No. 2004AP1637-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 162; 285 Wis. 2d 633; 702 N.W.2d 412; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 546


April 14, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
June 22, 2005, Decided  
June 22, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Draughon, 2005 WI 150, 286 Wis. 2d 99, 705 N.W.2d 660, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 825 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Washington County: DAVID C. RESHESKE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF385.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of sexual exploitation by a therapist, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.22(2) (2003-04). His motion for postconviction relief was also denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant earned a bachelor of arts degree in evangelism and was ordained as a pastor for his church. He was counseling a married couple and became sexually involved with the wife. Currently, he appealed his conviction for sexual exploitation by a therapist and an order denying his motion for postconviction relief. He contended that the circuit court improperly instructed the jury. The court agreed that the jury instruction addressing defendant's status as a "therapist" under Wis. Stat. § 940.22(1)(i) (2003-04) was error. Accordingly, the court reversed and remanded the matter for a new trial. The circuit court's instruction to the jury relieved the State of its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was a therapist as defined by § 940.22(1)(i), and therefore the instruction was unconstitutional under the Fifth and Sixth Amendments. The error was not harmless because it was not clear beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury would have found him guilty absent the error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

872 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Wis. Builders Ass'n v. Wis. DOT


Appeal No. 2004AP2388


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 160; 285 Wis. 2d 472; 702 N.W.2d 433; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 534


April 20, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
June 16, 2005, Decided  
June 16, 2005, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ROBERT DE CHAMBEAU, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CV3599.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Wisconsin Department of Transportation (DOT) challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment in favor of appellee builders in an action concerning a dispute over administrative regulations that concerned land abutting public highways.


OVERVIEW: The builders contended that the DOT did not have authority to review all land divisions for property abutting public highways. The circuit court agreed. It also held that the setback restrictions and special exception conditions under Wis. Admin. Code § Transp. 233.08(3n) and Wis. Admin. Code § Transp. 233.11(3)(d) were unconstitutional takings. The DOT then sought review. On appeal, the court determined that the DOT failed to show that any statute gave it the authority to promulgate rules that applied to all land divisions abutting highways. Wis. Stat. § 236.03(1) (2003-04) only applied to local units of government, so the DOT did not have the authority to regulate land divisions that were not subdivisions. Further, Wis. Stat. ch. 84 related only to the DOT's authority regarding the supervision and expenditure of federal and state highway funds. Next, Wis. Stat. § 85.02(1), 86.07(2) (2003-04) did not give the DOT the authority it asserted. Finally, the court rejected the argument that Wis. Admin. Code § Transp. 233.08(3n) and Wis. Admin. Code § Transp. 233.11(3)(d) were unconstitutional under the Fifth Amendment or Wis. Const. art. I, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that the DOT did not have the statutory authority to review all land divisions for property abutting public highways, but it reversed the decision that the regulations in question were unconstitutional takings.

 

873 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Francis


Appeal No. 2004AP1360-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 161; 285 Wis. 2d 451; 701 N.W.2d 632; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 529


April 14, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
June 15, 2005, Decided  
June 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Francis, 2005 WI 136, 703 N.W.2d 378, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 652 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MICHAEL S. FISHER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CF671.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pleaded no contest in the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) to attempted armed robbery and a pleaded guilty several counts of second degree reckless endangerment. The court denied the petitioner's request for postconviction relief. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by accepted her pleas of guilty and no contest without conducting a personal colloquy to ensure that she waived her not guilty by reason of insanity (NGI) plea knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently. The court of appeals disagreed. The petitioner had no right to insist on a personal colloquy as a prerequisite to a valid plea withdrawal. Only fundamental constitutional rights warranted that special protection and an NGI pleas fell outside the realm of a fundamental right. At the time the petitioner entered her subsequent pleas, the trial court had no reason to doubt her sanity. The only doctor's report available clearly opined that she did not lack the mental capacity to commit the crimes charged and, moreover, demonstrated a rational comprehension of the proceedings at the time of the evaluation. That observation was consistent with counsel's testimony and the trial court's own observations. Counsel testified at the postconviction hearing that although he had concerns that county personnel were not adequately treating defendant's depression, he never had any reason to doubt that she understood the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

874 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fisher


Appeal Nos. 2004AP1289-CR, 2004AP2488-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 175; 285 Wis. 2d 433; 702 N.W.2d 56; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 533


April 28, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
June 15, 2005, Decided  
June 15, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Fisher, 2005 WI 136, 703 N.W.2d 379, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 698 (2005)
Review denied by State v. Fisher, 2005 WI 136, 703 N.W.2d 378, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 650 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MICHAEL FISHER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CF747.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of delivering 5 or fewer grams of cocaine, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 961.41(1)(cm)1 (1999-2000); sentenced him to a 12-year sentence with 7 years of initial confinement and 5 years of extended supervision, to be served consecutively to any other sentence; and that denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the length of his sentence and the validity of the conditions of extended supervision that prohibited him from consuming or possessing alcohol or entering a liquor store or tavern. Defendant claimed those conditions were vague, overbroad, and bore no connection to his offense. The court held that the trial court had properly considered the three primary sentencing factors in arriving at the length of defendant's sentence. The court found that although the oral pronouncement of sentence may not have been perfectly clear, the written judgment of conviction and the conditions of extended supervision were crystal clear with respect to what conduct the conditions covered. Also the alcohol conditions were reasonably related to defendant's rehabilitative needs. The court held that defendant's challenge to the validity of the conditions was not premature under Wis. Stat § 302.113(7m)(e)1 (2003-04), which required a defendant to wait until one year before his release to supervision before challenging the conditions, because § 302.113(7m)(e)1 applied where an individual sought modification of an otherwise valid condition, not where he challenged its validity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

State v. Emanuel G. (In re Kedar K.)


Appeal No. 2005AP385


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2005 WI App 176; 285 Wis. 2d 807; 701 N.W.2d 654; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 501



June 7, 2005, Decided  
June 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOSEPH R. WALL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003TP269.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State moved to terminate the parental rights of appellant father. The child, born in 1996, had never lived with the father. The father was incarcerated much of the time between 1996 and 2001. Later he was subject to an absconder warrant. A jury in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin found grounds to terminate the father's parental rights. The trial court ordered a termination order and the father appealed.


OVERVIEW: In effect, the father argued that he was denied due process and equal protection of the law. He asserted that he and the child's mother (her parental rights were also terminated), were treated differently during the children in need of protection and services (CHIPS) and termination of parental rights (TPR) proceedings. His two primary complaints were that he was not given adequate notice of hearings and that the mother was unfairly offered more social services. However, the alleged grounds for termination of his parental rights (in part, abandonment), did not include his failure to meet conditions of a CHIPS order. Thus, unlike with the mother, the State did not need to prove that it made reasonable efforts to assist him. Moreover, he did not identify the social services he wished he had received, or provide proof that he asked for services. In addition, the father admitted that he had never been in a room alone with the child or spent a night with him. The father did not identify how the denial of additional services or "conditions to work on" prevented him from establishing a relationship with his child. Thus, the father was not denied due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

876 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Grove Town Bd. v. Door County Bd. of Supervisors


Appeal No. 2004AP2358


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 166; 284 Wis. 2d 814; 702 N.W.2d 33; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 504


March 14, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
June 7, 2005, Decided  
June 7, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Liberty Grove Town Bd. v. Door County Bd. of Supervisors, 2005 WI 136, 703 N.W.2d 379, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 697 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Door County: D. TODD EHLERS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CV262.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a town board (the town), asserted it had exclusive authority to name roads within the town and that respondent county's ordinance illegally infringed on its road naming authority. In the town's action for declaratory relief and an injunction, the Circuit Court for Door County, Wisconsin, dismissed its claims. The town appealed.


OVERVIEW: By its plain language, former Wis. Stat. § 81.01(11) (2001-02) required a town to assign a name to each road within the town's jurisdiction. On the other hand, the plain language of Wis. Stat. § 59.54(4) (2003-04) (an enabling statute), gave counties discretionary authority to establish a rural naming or numbering system when the purpose of the system was to aid in fire protection, emergency services and civil defense. The statute also gave counties discretion to give each road a name or number and to "cooperate with towns" to implement the system. Thus, the appellate court held the town had initial authority to name town roads. However, the town's authority was subject to the county's discretionary authority, under § 59.54(4). Ultimately, the county had authority to implement name changes, even if the town did not consent, when the name changes were made under the system pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 59.54 (2003-04). The appellate court found the county exceeded its authority as to one part of the ordinance that related to the "efficient delivery of goods and services." However, that invalid portion of the ordinance was severable from the valid provisions at issue in the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Norlander


Appeal No. 2004AP0389-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2005 WI App 176; 285 Wis. 2d 804; 701 N.W.2d 652; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 495



June 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Norlander, 2005 WI 150, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 805 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: LISA K. STARK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001CF26.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County, Wisconsin, convicting him of child enticement, Wis. Stat. § 948.07(1) (2003-2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from an Internet sting operation. The officer posed as a fictitious fourteen-year-old boy. Defendant and the fictitious boy had a sexually explicit discussion, and made plans to meet in a fast-food restaurant to arrange a sexual encounter. Defendant was arrested at the restaurant. Defendant argued that the circuit court erroneously admitted testimony on "grooming techniques" used by sexual predators. The appellate court ruled that the circuit court properly exercised its discretion by admitting testimony on grooming techniques. Defendant's intent was relevant, and the officer's testimony was relevant circumstantial evidence of defendant's intent. Defendant did not explain how the officer's testimony was unfairly prejudicial or how unfair prejudice substantially outweighed the testimony's probative value as circumstantial evidence of his intent. Also, defendant failed to show Wis. Stat. § 948.07 was facially unconstitutional when applied to internet cases. Defendant argued the statute violated due process, but failed to articulate whether he attacked the statute on substantive or procedural due process grounds.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

May 11, 2005, Decided  
May 11, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Figueroa, 2005 WI 136, 703 N.W.2d 376, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 596 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: EMILY S. MUELLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1998CF311.
State v. Figueroa, 240 Wis. 2d 325, 621 N.W.2d 386, 2001 WI App 1, 2000 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1137 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellate inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed pro se from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief, challenging the performance of his trial and appellate attorneys and claiming that he was the victim of prosecutorial misconduct. The court affirmed however, stating that many of the inmate's claims of ineffective trial counsel and prosecutorial misconduct lead to a single destination which was that evidence of the nude photo of the victim should not have been admitted. However, it had already been determined that the admission of the photograph by reason of the improper exploitation charge was harmless error and that the photograph would have otherwise been admissible. Further, the inmate failed to demonstrate what additional investigation or statements from witnesses would have revealed. In addition, the suggestion that the victim was not a virgin at the time of the assaults was totally without foundation and lacked any relevance to the allegations against the inmate since penetration was not alleged. Also, such evidence would not have been admissible under Wisconsin's rape shield law, Wis. Stat. § 972.11 (2003-04).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Yulga


Appeal No. 2004AP2744-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 126; 284 Wis. 2d 571; 699 N.W.2d 253; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 394



May 5, 2005, Decided  
May 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage County: FREDERIC FLEISHAUER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CM447.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of possession of marijuana after a police officer found marijuana and drug paraphernalia during the course of a traffic stop involving defendant, who was the driver, and a passenger. Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) convicting her after denying her motion to suppress the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the circuit court erred when it denied her suppression motion. She argued that the initial stop was invalid and that the officer prolonged the stop without reasonable suspicion to have done so. The appellate court concluded that the initial stop was valid and that defendant waived her argument that the officer unreasonably prolonged the stop. At the time the officer made the stop, he knew the following: (1) the time was approximately 2:30 a.m.; (2) defendant's vehicle was stopped at an intersection for "some time"; (3) the driver of the vehicle failed to signal a turn at the intersection; and, (4) after the vehicle turned, it drifted toward the fog line. The appellate court did not need not determine whether the officer could have formed a reasonable suspicion that defendant committed a statutory signal or lane violation as, based on all the circumstances, the officer could have formed a reasonable suspicion to stop defendant for driving while intoxicated. Accordingly, the initial stop of defendant's vehicle was valid. Also, a reasonable officer could not help but have wondered about the passenger's behavior which constituted articulable and suspicious facts.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Tabor (In re Tabor)


Appeal Nos. 2004AP1986, 2004AP1987


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 107; 282 Wis. 2d 768; 699 N.W.2d 663; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 367


April 6, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
April 26, 2005, Decided  
April 26, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Tabor, 2005 WI 136, 285 Wis. 2d 629, 703 N.W.2d 379, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 676 (2005)
Subsequent appeal at State v. Tabor (In re Tabor), 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 125 (Wis. Ct. App., Feb. 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: Michael B. Brennan, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 2001CI000001, 2003CI000007.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which held that under 2003 Wis. Laws 187, § 8, modifications applied to trials to determine whether appellants should be committed, even though the Wis. Stat. ch. 980 petitions filed against them antedated the effective date of 2003 Wis. Laws 187.


OVERVIEW: 2003 Wis. Laws 187 modified both the definition of a "sexually violent person" and the threshold required to establish that a person whom the State sought to commit under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 was "dangerous to others." 2003 Wis. Act 187, § 8, made these modifications effective to hearings, trials, and proceedings that were commenced on or after April 22, 2004. The Wis. Stat. ch. 980 petitions seeking to commit appellants were filed in 2001 and 2003 respectively, but neither appellant had yet had their trials under Wis. Stat. § 980.05. On appeal, the court agreed with the trial court that the modifications were applicable to both appellants. The court stated that the petitions filed against appellants did not vest in them any immutable right to be tried under the then-existing standard for dangerousness; rather the legislature could modify the threshold for dangerousness so long as the applicable criteria remain relevant to chapter 980's underlying purposes of both protecting society and providing needed treatment to persons whose mental disorder makes them dangerous. In addition, there was no unconstitutional retroactive application of the modifications.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, petitioner, challenged the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, committing him to a secure facility as a sexually violent person.

Kohl v. Dewitt Ross & Stevens (In re Kohl v. Zeitlin)


Appeal No. 2004AP328


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 315



April 14, 2005, Decided  
April 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER EDITING. IF PUBLISHED, THE OFFICIAL VERSION WILL APPEAR IN THE BOUND VOLUME OF THE OFFICIAL REPORTS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, 05/13/2005
Substituted opinion at, Request denied by Kohl v. DeWitt Ross & Stevens (In re Kohl v. Zeitlin), 2005 WI App 196, 287 Wis. 2d 289, 704 N.W.2d 586, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 698 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B O'BRIEN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2001FA2105.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, attorney and law firm, represented appellant, former client, during divorce proceedings. Respondents moved to withdraw and for a judgment against the client in the amount of her outstanding fee balance. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, awarded fees in the amount of $ 15,920, and the client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client argued that the circuit court lacked competency to decide the issue, claiming that the circuit court could enter such a judgment for fees only if authorized by Wis. Stat. § 767.23(3)(a) (2003-2004), but that the statute did not apply to the facts of the case. The client asserted that the only plausible way the statute applied to the case was if a "substitution of attorneys" occurred. The client argued that a substitution did not occur because the law firm withdrew from representation and was not replaced by another attorney. The appellate court ruled that the client's interpretation of the statute was unreasonable. The statute contemplated that when an attorney withdrew, the circuit court had the authority to address attorney fees. The appellate court observed no reason why the reason for the withdrawal, the client's consent or lack of consent, or the fact that no subsequent attorney assumed representation, should lead to a different result. Also, the law firm's request for attorney fees on appeal was denied because the appellate court did not believe that every issue was frivolous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

883 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fitzpatrick


Appeal No. 2004AP2708-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2005 WI App 111; 283 Wis. 2d 510; 698 N.W.2d 133; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 331



April 12, 2005, Decided  
April 12, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] : PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Pepin County: ROBERT W. WING, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CM138.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted for illegally shining deer, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 29.314(3)(a) (2003-04), in the Circuit Court for Pepin County, Wisconsin. He appealed, asserting that the statute violated his right to bear arms under the Wisconsin Constitution. He further argued that the circuit court erred by refusing to allow him to argue to the jury that an unloaded, cased rifle was not a firearm for purposes of the statute.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the facts established that a warden cited defendant for shining deer while in possession of a firearm. The warden seized two spotlights from the vehicle as well as two hunting rifles that were unloaded and cased. The appellate court held that the State's exercise of its police powers in enacting the shining statute, Wis. Stat. § 29.314(3)(a) (2003-04), outweighed an individual's right to be in possession of a firearm while shining deer. Therefore, the statute did not interfere with defendant's constitutional right to keep and bear arms under Wis. Const. art. I, § 25. The appellate court also rejected defendant's argument that a firearm was not a firearm for purposes of the shining statute absent the presence of ammunition. A "firearm" was not defined in Wis. Stat. § 29.314 (2003-04), but case law showed that a firearm did not have to be loaded in order to be considered a firearm. Finally, ammunition could be easily hidden or disposed of by throwing it out a window. In the context of illegally shining deer while in possession of a weapon, the State's ability to regulate the health, safety and welfare of its citizens and to protect wildlife outweighed any inconvenience.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. McGee


Appeal No. 2004AP1005-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 97; 281 Wis. 2d 756; 698 N.W.2d 850; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 335


March 1, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
April 12, 2005, Decided  
April 12, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. McGee, 2005 WI 150, 286 Wis. 2d 99, 705 N.W.2d 660, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 810 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DANIEL L. KONKOL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2002CM010360.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a mother, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied her motion pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 118.15(5)(b)(2), holding that it was premature.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from an order entered after the trial court denied her motion filed pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 118.15(5)(b)(2) (2001-02). In that motion, she sought dismissal of the complaint against her, which alleged one count of failing to cause a child to attend school, contrary the compulsory school attendance law, Wis. Stat. §§ 118.15(1), (5) and 118.16(5) (2001-02). The basis for the motion was that she was unable to comply with the compulsory attendance law because of the disobedience of her child. The trial court held that the motion was premature because application of the disobedience defense did not apply unless there had already been a conviction under Wis. Stat. § 118.15(5)(a). Because the trial court erroneously interpreted the statute to require a conviction before the disobedience defense applied, the court reversed the order and remand for further proceedings. The disobedience exception to § 118.15(5)(b)(2) was an affirmative defense to the charge and thus should have been presented to the fact-finder during the trial for resolution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision.

State v. Trigueros


Appeal No. 2004AP1701-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 112; 282 Wis. 2d 445; 701 N.W.2d 54; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 340


March 1, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
April 12, 2005, Decided  
April 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Trigueros, 2005 WI 136, 285 Wis. 2d 629, 703 N.W.2d 378, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 668 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: TIMOTHY G. DUGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 2003CF4384.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, convicting him of possession of one gram or less of cocaine, with the intent to deliver, Wis. Stat. § 961.41(1m)(cm)1g, and from an order denying his postconviction motion for sentence modification.


OVERVIEW: An officer found .29 grams of cocaine base in defendant's pants pocket during a pat-down search. Before sentencing, the probation department prepared a presentence-investigation report. Defendant told the report writer that he had been selling cocaine "off and on" for about twelve months, and that he had smoked marijuana daily and had used cocaine, but that he had signed up for drug treatment. Defendant argued that the trial court placed too much weight on the need to protect the public, and did not adequately consider what he alleged were mitigating character traits. The appellate court ruled that the trial court considered the appropriate sentencing factors, as it considered the seriousness of the crime, describing the devastating impact drugs had on families and children, and considered defendant's character. Also, the condition restricting defendant's association with the drug community was both reasonably related to his crime and to his rehabilitation, as well as the need to protect the community. The condition that defendant not have contact with the drug community would help him remain drug-free, and ensure that he did not sell drugs in the community again.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

State v. Thames


Appeal No. 2004AP1257


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 101; 281 Wis. 2d 772; 700 N.W.2d 285; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 341


January 4, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
April 12, 2005, Decided  
April 12, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Thames, 2005 WI 136, 285 Wis. 2d 628, 703 N.W.2d 378, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 648 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL B. BRENNAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 1995CF951165.
State v. Thames, 205 Wis. 2d 113, 555 N.W.2d 410, 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1118 (Wis. Ct. App., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his pro se motion filed pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2003-04).


OVERVIEW: Approximately two months before he turned 18, defendant was charged with first-degree reckless homicide using a dangerous weapon, attempted first-degree intentional homicide using a dangerous weapon, and mutilating a corpse. He was charged as an adult. He entered a guilty plea to all of the charges. His convictions were upheld on appeal. In 1997, he filed a pro se motion pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (1997-98). The trial court denied the motion. Defendant's appeal of the denial was dismissed. In 2004, he filed a second pro se motion pursuant to § 974.06 (2003-04). The trial court denied the motion without a hearing. On appeal, the court found that all of defendant's claims were raised, or could have been raised, in his direct appeal or in his 1997 § 974.06 motion. Defendant's arguments were procedurally barred. The fact that his appeal of the order denying his 1997 § 974.06 motion was dismissed pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.83(2) (1997-98) did not change the result. The claimed failure of his trial counsel to advise him of the rights he waived by pleading guilty was precisely the type of issue that was known to him at the time of his first Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (1997-98) motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

State v. McGuire


Appeal No. 04-1618-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 88; 281 Wis. 2d 272; 695 N.W.2d 904; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 295



March 31, 2005, Decided  
March 31, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT TO CITED IN ANY COURT OF OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. McGuire, 2005 WI 134, 700 N.W.2d 274, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 508 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Crawford County: MICHAEL KIRCHMAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CT000094.
State v. McGuire, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 263 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 24, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed motions to suppress all evidence that a police officer acquired after opening the door to defendant's truck after a routine traffic stop and to suppress evidence of a preliminary breath test (PBT). The Circuit Court for Crawford County (Wisconsin) rejected both motions, and defendant pled guilty to operating while intoxicated (OWI), second offense, in violation of Wis. Stat. 346.63 (2003-04). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the arresting officer lacked reasonable suspicion to continue to detain him for an OWI investigation after the initial reason for the traffic stop was resolved. Defendant also argued that the officer conducted an illegal search by opening his truck's door during the stop, obtaining evidence that the trial court should have suppressed. The appellate court held that the facts known to the officer justified the continued detention and investigation. The court agreed that the officer's opening of the truck door was an illegal search. However, the evidence uncovered by the search was admissible under the inevitable discovery doctrine. The odor of intoxication that the search revealed would inevitably have been discovered; it was therefore admissible. While the exclusionary rule generally barred the evidentiary use of such improperly gathered evidence, the officer opened the truck's door while simultaneously ordering defendant to exit the vehicle. Had he not opened the door, defendant would still have been required to exit the vehicle. At that point the officer, standing near the door and preparing to conduct field sobriety tests, would have detected the odor.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds


Appeal No. 04-0064


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 87; 280 Wis. 2d 837; 696 N.W.2d 563; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 262


October 14, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
March 24, 2005, Decided  
March 24, 2005, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds, 2005 WI 134, 282 Wis. 2d 719, 700 N.W.2d 271, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 412 (2005)
Affirmed by Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds, 2006 WI 7, 708 N.W.2d 326, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 6 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CV000094.
Fazio v. Dep't of Emple. Trust Funds, 255 Wis. 2d 801, 645 N.W.2d 618, 2002 WI App 127, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 496 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this class action, plaintiff beneficiary sued defendant Department of Employee Trust Funds claiming that the failure to pay her accrued earnings or interest on her death benefit after the date of her husband's death constituted a taking in violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 13. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, granted the beneficiary's motion for summary judgment. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: In granting summary judgment for the beneficiary, the circuit court held that the Department's failure, for lump sum death benefits paid to beneficiaries under Wis. Stat. § 40.73(1)(c) (2003-04), to include interest or earnings accrued from the date of the participants' deaths until payments were made to the beneficiaries constituted an unlawful taking under Wis. Const. art. I, § 13. The court of appeals disagreed, concluding that the beneficiary did not acquire a property interest in her lump sum death benefit until she satisfied the requirements of Wis. Stat. § 40.71(3). Thus, the Department's failure to pay her interest or earnings on the amount of her death benefit calculated under Wis. Stat. § 40.73(1)(c) between the date of her husband's death and the Department's receipt and processing of her death benefit application did not violate Wis. Const. art. I, § 13. The court of appeals' conclusion did not dispose of the claims of beneficiaries who received account-value benefits under Wis. Stat. § 40.73(1)(am) because the period for which those beneficiaries claimed to have been wrongfully denied interest occurred after they had applied for and received an initial death benefit.


OUTCOME: The appealed order was reversed, and the circuit court was directed on remand to dismiss the beneficiary's complaint.

State v. Russell


Appeal No. 04-0556-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2005 WI App 88; 281 Wis. 2d 271; 695 N.W.2d 903; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 255



March 22, 2005, Decided  
March 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by State v. Russell, 2005 WI 60, 697 N.W.2d 474, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 366 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KAREN E. CHRISTENSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CF006606.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, convicting him of attempted armed robbery, party to a crime, as a habitual criminal, and contributing to the delinquency of a child, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(b) and (2), 939.05, 939.32, 939.62(1)(c) and (2), 948.40(1),(3) and 4(b), and 939.62(1)(c) and (2) (2003-2004).


OVERVIEW: The trial was adjourned to procure a material juvenile witness who participated in the events that led to the charges. The witness was secured in detention, and served with a subpoena. The witness signed the back of the subpoena, acknowledged its receipt and stated that he would be in court on the trial date. The witness was released on his own recognizances, and the trial court was later informed that the witness was not available because he had run away from home. Defendant asserted that the subpoena for the adjourned trial was only mailed to the witness, and as a result, there was no showing by the State that the witness would not appear at trial if personally served with a subpoena. The appellate court rejected defendant's contention that personal service of a subpoena for the new trial date was required in order to conclude that the witness's deposition was admissible under Wis. Stat. § 967.04 (2003-2004). Wis. Stat. § 967.04 did not require personal service of a subpoena, and once the witness was personally served with a subpoena for the first trial date, the service of a new subpoena was not required to maintain the witness's obligation to attend the adjourned trial date.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment and order in appeal No. 04-0669-CR affirmed; judgment and order in appeal No. 04-0670-CR reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The first defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Oconto County (Wisconsin) of assault on a law enforcement officer, Wis. Stat. § 940.20(2) (2001-2002), and disorderly conduct, Wis. Stat. § 947.01 (2001-2002). The second defendant was convicted in the court of obstructing a warden, Wis. Stat. § 29.951 (2001-2002), and disorderly conduct. The trial court denied both defendants' motions for postconviction relief. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two wardens stopped their vehicle when they saw some hunters. The hunters denied having shot any deer. When one of the wardens saw a deer carcass hanging in an open shed at a nearby residence, the warden sought to see if it was properly tagged and registered. The warden then grabbed the first defendant to push him away. An altercation between the two men ensued. The first defendant alleged self-defense under Wis. Stat. § 939.48(1) (2001-2002). The warden's supervisor arrived and began to photograph what was happening. The second defendant also demanded a search warrant and, when that was not produced, he slapped at the supervisor and his camera. On appeal, the court found that there was insufficient evidence to support the obstructing a warden conviction as to the second defendant, and that the jury was improperly charged as to the disorderly conduct. The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the convictions as to the first defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment as to the defendant convicted of obstructing a warden and disorderly conduct was reversed. The judgment as to the defendant convicted of assaulting a law enforcement officer and disorderly conduct was affirmed.

C & C Pawnbrokers, LLC v. City of Eau Claire


Appeal No. 04-2324-FT, 04-CV-355


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2005 WI App 59; 280 Wis. 2d 559; 694 N.W.2d 510; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 109



February 8, 2005, Decided  
February 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by C & C Pawnbrokers, LLC v. City of Eau Claire, 2005 WI 134, 282 Wis. 2d 723, 700 N.W.2d 274, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 527 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: ERIC J. WAHL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin), which granted a motion for a temporary restraining order filed by plaintiff pawnbrokers and declared that a city ordinance was unconstitutional. The ordinance at issue required the pawnbrokers to join the Automated Pawn System (APS), a computerized system that allowed users to track information.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted an ordinance requiring pawnbrokers to join the APS, a computerized system that allowed users to track information about both customers and merchandise. The ordinance imposed a $ 1 fee per transaction. The pawnbrokers filed a complaint and a motion for a temporary restraining order to prohibit the city from implementing the ordinance. The trial court granted the restraining order and declared the ordinance unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that the ordinance was not unconstitutional even though it treated pawnbrokers differently from secondhand dealers. The city had a rational and reasonable basis for applying the APS requirement exclusively to pawnbrokers. During hearings prior to enacting the ordinance, the city council heard evidence that there were more pawn transactions than secondhand transactions, and much more stolen property was recovered from the city's pawnshops than from its secondhand dealers. Based on the data, the city reasonably and rationally concluded it should require heightened monitoring from pawnshops. The court further found that the $ 1 transaction fee did not amount to an unconstitutional tax enacted without taxing authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court.

State v. Hipke


Appeal No. 04-1976-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 38; 279 Wis. 2d 519; 693 N.W.2d 148; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 81



January 27, 2005, Decided  
January 27, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage County: JOHN V. FINN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CT000371.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated as a third offense pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1) (2001, 2002). Defendant asserted that it was error to deny defendant's motion to suppress because the police officer who stopped defendant did not have the reasonable suspicion required to justify the initial stop.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with drunk driving offenses under Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1) (2001-02) after his vehicle was stopped for having excessively loud exhaust noise. The circuit court denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence of defendant's intoxication that the police obtained during the course of the stop. Defendant had alleged that the police did not have probable cause or reasonable suspicion to believe defendant was committing any offense at the time of the stop. Affirming the denial of the motion to suppress, the court held that the police officer had established that there was a reasonable suspicion to stop defendant's car for a violation of Wis. Stat. § 347.39(1) when the police officer observed that the car was excessively noisy and had an excessively loud exhaust. From the officer's testimony, the circuit court reasonably inferred that the officer had experience listening to thousands of car mufflers and that he knew the difference between a loud muffler and an excessively loud muffler. Because there was reasonable suspicion to make the initial stop, the court agreed with the circuit court that the motion to suppress should have been denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

January 19, 2005, Decided  
January 19, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEAN W. DiMOTTO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 85CF001463.
State v. Davis, 141 Wis. 2d 978, 415 N.W.2d 861, 1987 Wisc. App. LEXIS 4039 (Wis. Ct. App., 1987)



DISPOSITION: Circuit court's denial of petition for post-conviction relief and motion for new trial affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, inmate, challenged the orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, denying his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2001-2002) motion for postconviction relief, and denying his motion for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted in 1985 of two counts of first-degree murder while armed with a dangerous weapon, two counts of carrying a concealed weapon, and possession of a controlled substance. In his postconviction motion, the inmate requested that the circuit court order a new trial or modify his sentence. The appellate court ruled that the circuit court correctly held that the inmate had not established a new factor. The inmate contended that his trial counsel possessed psychological evidence of his incompetence but chose not to present it. Thus, the inmate could not satisfy one of the fundamental components of the "new factor" definition, that the fact was unknowingly overlooked by all of the parties. Also, the inmate did not explain how the non-disclosure of the psychological evidence frustrated the purpose of the original sentence. Furthermore, the appellate court failed to see how Wis. Stat. § 973.195 (2001-2002) constituted a change in parole policy for the inmate. Wis. Stat. § 973.195 had no impact on the inmate, thus his sentence could not have been increased by its enactment.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

County of Manitowoc v. Klug


Appeal No. 04-1548


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2005 WI App 38; 279 Wis. 2d 519; 693 N.W.2d 147; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 34



January 12, 2005, Decided  
January 12, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: DARRYL W. DEETS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03TR003787.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County, Wisconsin, convicting her of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), first offense, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2003-2004).


OVERVIEW: The officer went to defendant's apartment to investigate a report of a reckless driver. The officer explained why he was there, and asked defendant if she wanted to step inside or outside to talk, preferring that she not stand in the doorway. Defendant stepped outside and sat on the step outside the porch door. The officer noticed that her balance was unsteady, her speech was slurred, she would hesitate before responding to questions, and there was a strong odor of intoxicants. Defendant pled no contest to the OWI charge after the circuit court denied her motion to suppress evidence. Defendant argued that the arresting officer violated her Fourth Amendment protections when he induced her to step outside of her apartment to talk and then physically restrained her from re-entering. Defendant conceded that the officer did not cross the threshold of her doorway, but cast the officer's statement as a threat to enter. The appellate court ruled that the circuit court's findings were supported by the evidence. No unconstitutional seizure occurred. The officer did not enter defendant's apartment, nor did he threaten to do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lindskog


Appeal No. 04-1222-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2005 WI App 38; 279 Wis. 2d 519; 693 N.W.2d 147; 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 35



January 12, 2005, Decided  
January 12, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: JOHN R. RACE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CT000592.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Walworth County, Wisconsin, for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, second offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had argued that a "DUI" in Illinois could not be counted as a prior offense in Wisconsin because it was resolved with a supervision agreement without the entry of a judgment of conviction. The trial court rejected his argument, reasoning that under Wis. Stat. § 343.307(1)(d) (2003-04), the Illinois law permitting disposition of a "DUI" by court supervision was sufficiently similar to Wisconsin's drunk driving laws. On appeal, defendant contended that if his argument before the trial court lacked merit on appeal, then § 343.307(1)(d) was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court noted that defendant's argument before the trial court had previously been resolved against him by judicial precedent and would not be overruled. The appellate court held that § 343.307(1)(d) survived defendant's challenge because any person with common sense would know it permitted counting violations, not just convictions, of other states' statutes that prohibited the use of a motor vehicle while intoxicated.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Kruczek v. Wis. Dep't of Workforce Dev.


Appeal No. 04-0090


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 12; 278 Wis. 2d 563; 692 N.W.2d 286; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1077


September 27, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
December 28, 2004, Decided  
December 28, 2004, Opinion


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Kruczek v. Wis. Dep't of Workforce Dev., 2005 WI 60, 281 Wis. 2d 114, 697 N.W.2d 472, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 240 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown County: J.D. McKAY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03-CV-494.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, individual and company (company), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of respondent, the Department of Workforce Development (DWD), and affirmed the DWD's debarment of the company from projects for six months. The DWD cross-appealed the portion of the judgment determining that it could only debar the company from municipal projects.


OVERVIEW: The company was a contractor that worked primarily on municipal sewer and water projects. A prevailing wage complaint had been filed with the DWD, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 66.0903 (2001-02), concerning prevailing wages. The trial court affirmed the DWD's debarment of the company from municipal and state public works projects for six months. The court further upheld DWD's interpretation of the time frame as directory, pursuant to Wis. Admin. Code § DWD 294.05(5)(b) (2001-02). The court agreed with the DWD's interpretation and therefore affirmed that portion of the judgment. Further, the court concluded that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to consider the issue of whether the DWD could only debar the company from municipal, not state, projects, and therefore reversed that portion of the judgment. The company's failure to serve the joint committee for review of administrative rules, in accordance with Wis. Stat. § 227.40(5) (2001-02), deprived the trial court of jurisdiction to hear a challenge to that issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the DWD's interpretation of the time frame as directory and reversed the portion of the judgment determining that the DWD could only debar the company from municipal, not state, projects.

Green v. Litscher


Appeal No. 02-3279


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 21; 278 Wis. 2d 811; 691 N.W.2d 926; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1058



December 23, 2004, Decided  
December 23, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Grant County: GEORGE S. CURRY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CV003480, 02CV000160.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed an action in the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin) against defendants, several corrections officers, a warden, a corrections complaint examiner, a chaplain, and a corrections secretary, alleging that defendants had violated his rights. The inmate appealed after the circuit court dismissed all of his claims except as for one claim against the warden, which was transferred to a different court.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that his mail was unlawfully interfered with, that he was retaliated against, that an administrative complaint was intentionally impeded, that Wis. Admin. Code § DOC 303.20 (2000), which prohibited gang-related activities in prison, was unconstitutional, that he was placed under restriction without due process, that legal documents were illegally confiscated, and that he was discriminated against because of his political beliefs. The circuit court dismissed all of the claims, except for one claim asserted against the prison warden, for failure to exhaust administrative remedies as required by Wis. Stat. § 801.02(7)(b) (2001-02). In reversing in part, the court found that the inmate had exhausted his administrative remedies with regard to his claims of interference with his mail and the denial of his requests to possess certain literature; he had filed administrative complaints raising both of those claims. The rest of the claims were properly dismissed. The inmate had failed to properly serve the secretary; none of the other defendants were proper parties to litigate the inmate's constitutional challenge to the gang regulation.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the warden from the appeal. It affirmed the circuit court's dismissal order in part, reversed it in part, and remanded the case back for further proceedings as to the inmate's claims that his mail was interfered with and his that his requests to possess certain items of literature were improperly denied.

City of Madison v. Crossfield


Appeal No. 04-1052


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 21; 278 Wis. 2d 813; 691 N.W.2d 927; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1028



December 16, 2004, Decided  
December 16, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: DIANE M. NICKS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CV002254.
City of Madison v. Crossfield, 267 Wis. 2d 961, 671 N.W.2d 717, 2003 WI App 225, 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 907 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, truck owner, appealed two orders of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin. The first order affirmed a decision of the Municipal Court for the City of Madison, Wisconsin, regarding a city ordinance prohibiting off-street parking of certain vehicles and a second order denying his motion to reconsider the first order, in the underlying action with respondent, City of Madison, Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: The owner's truck had a cargo box, and it was stipulated that the truck weighed 7200 pounds empty. A city zoning inspector testified that the owner parked the truck at the owner's residence on eight dates. The municipal court found the owner guilty of violating Madison, Wis., Gen. Ordinances § 28.11(3)(a)1. The ordinance provided off-street parking facilities solely for the parking of passenger automobiles, including passenger trucks, limited in size to less than one ton in capacity. The appellate court determined that the question was not whether the circuit court erred, but whether the municipal court erred, and the owner made no complaints of any municipal court error. Though the owner asserted in passing that his truck had less than one ton capacity and less cargo volume per passenger than other personal use vehicles and had four wheels, rather than six, that was the extent of his argument. The owner cited no statutes, administrative rules, ordinances, court cases, or other authority showing that vehicles with these characteristics were less than "one ton in capacity."


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded to the circuit court with instructions to file an amended judgment of conviction, if it concluded that its standard of review permitted it to do so, and, if the circuit court did not so conclude, it should remand to the municipal court for further proceedings.

Justmann v. Portage County


Appeal No. 03-3310


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 9; 278 Wis. 2d 487; 692 N.W.2d 273; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1029


August 5, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
December 16, 2004, Decided  
December 16, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Portage County: JOHN V. FINN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CV000252.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which awarded them $10,700 for property taken by defendant County for highway construction.


OVERVIEW: The property owners appealed from a judgment on a jury verdict awarding them $ 10,700 for property taken by the County for highway construction. They contended that, under Wis. Stat. § 32.09(6) (2001-02), they were entitled to an additional $ 43,894 in severance damages. Because the court concluded that the plain language of § 32.09(6) did not provide severance damages when compensation for a partial taking was based on the fair market value of the property taken, as it was in the current action, it affirmed. No language or punctuation marker set the severance damage portion of the section apart from the either/or construction set forth at the beginning of the sentence in § 32.09(6). Therefore, the court read the severance damages language to be a part of the either/or logic of the statute and concluded that such damages were available only under a "before and after" method of compensation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

900 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jeremy P. (In the Interest of Jeremy P.)


Appeal No. 04-0360


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2005 WI App 13; 278 Wis. 2d 366; 692 N.W.2d 311; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 990


November 3, 2004, Oral Argument  
December 7, 2004, Decided  
December 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL G. MALMSTADT, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02JV002206.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which required him to register as a sex offender pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 938.34(15m)(bm) and 301.45(1m) (2001-02) after he admitted to committing sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile, at age 13, engaged in fellatio with a five-year-old child on two occasions. Pursuant to a negotiated plea, the juvenile admitted that he committed one act of third-degree sexual assault. However, he reserved the right to challenge the statutory requirement that he register as a sex offender. The trial court required the juvenile to register as a sex offender. On appeal, the juvenile challenged the constitutionality of §§ 938.34(15m)(bm) and 301.45(1m). The court found that under Wisconsin law, requiring anyone to register as a sex offender was not a criminal punishment. Hence, there was no right to a jury trial guaranteed by the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution and Wis. Const. art. I, § 7. The court could not conclude that the juvenile proved that Wis. Stat. §§ 938.34(15m)(bm) and 301.45(1m) (2001-02) were unconstitutional. Because the court declined to recognize that children were members of a suspect class with a fundamental liberty right to have their best interest considered before the state made decisions about them, the court declined to apply the strict scrutiny test to the juvenile's equal protection analysis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the dispositional order requiring the juvenile to register as a sex offender and remanded so that the trial court could decide whether to stay the sex offender registration portion of the dispositional order as of the date of that order. The court affirmed the order of the trial court in all other respects.

 

901 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Myers v. Swenson


Appeal No. 03-2406


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 224; 277 Wis. 2d 749; 691 N.W.2d 357; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 954


March 18, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
November 18, 2004, Decided  
November 18, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  
Review denied by Myers v. Swenson, 2005 WI 21, 278 Wis. 2d 536, 693 N.W.2d 75, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 46 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CV001461.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After he was disciplined in an out-of-state prison, plaintiff inmate brought an action for certiorari review of the disciplinary decision. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, granted respondent prison warden's motion to quash and dismiss the action, concluding that it lacked competency to review the disciplinary decision and lacked personal jurisdiction over the warden. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate contended that the Wisconsin courts retained the ability to conduct certiorari review of a Wisconsin inmate's due process or equal protection challenge to a disciplinary action, even if the challenge involved conduct and a disciplinary proceeding that took place while the inmate was housed out of state. The appellate court concluded that the inmate failed to make a prima facie showing that he was entitled to certiorari review in Wisconsin. The inmate did not seek judicial review in the courts where he was in prison; instead, while still in the other state, he filed his certiorari action in Wisconsin. Because the inmate never sought judicial review in the other state, he never obtained a court decision asserting a lack of jurisdiction or competency to review the matter in that state. Since the inmate did not show that judicial review in the other state was unavailable because a court there concluded that it lacked jurisdiction or competency, the inmate failed to show that judicial review was unavailable under Wis. Stat. § 302.02(3t). Consequently, the inmate failed to show that Wisconsin courts had competency to entertain his certiorari action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Henriksen


Appeal No. 04-0705-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2005 WI App 1; 277 Wis. 2d 875; 690 N.W.2d 885; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 887



November 9, 2004, Decided  
November 9, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Oneida County: MARK A. MANGERSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CF-133.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; order affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Oneida County, Wisconsin, convicting him of seven counts of felony non-support and the resulting conditions of probation, and challenged the order denying his motion for postconviction relief, which sought elimination of the probation conditions regarding alcohol and payment of interest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his former wife had one child, and defendant had two more children by two other women. The trial court established multiple conditions for defendant's extended supervision, and these conditions were extended to the probation period as well. Defendant was prohibited from having any sexual relations unless he had the explicit permission of his probation agent, he could not consume any intoxicating beverages, and he was ordered to pay restitution comprised of his arrearage, accumulated interest on the arrearage as of the date of sentencing, as well as 12 percent statutory child support interest computed on the outstanding balance until the end of extended supervision or probation. The appellate court ruled that the sexual relations condition amounted to protection of the public, and requiring defendant to accept responsibility for any children he might produce forced him to acknowledge that his actions had consequences. Also, the condition of absolute sobriety was reasonably related to defendant's rehabilitation. Furthermore, interest could not be added to a restitution order.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, the portion of the order requiring defendant to pay interest on restitution was reversed, and the order was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Miller


Appeal No. 04-1181-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2005 WI App 1; 277 Wis. 2d 875; 690 N.W.2d 885; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 880



November 4, 2004, Decided  
November 4, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CM001502.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of lewd and lascivious behavior in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.20(1)(b) (2001-02). Defendant's postconviction motions for a directed verdict and a judgment notwithstanding the verdict were denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that the State failed to produce sufficient evidence supporting a finding of guilt beyond a reasonable doubt on elements one and two of Wis. Stat. § 944.20(1)(b) (2001-02): that he exposed his genitals and that he did so publicly. The appellate court disagreed, finding that although defendant was in his parked vehicle when he was caught, he was parked on the side of a main, frequently traveled public road, near a public park and playground, on a sunny day, and the officer had a clear view of defendant's penis as he approached the car. Thus, the evidence supported the inference that defendant knew or had reason to know that by parking there and exposing his genitals there, his genitals would be "open to view" to other persons. Further, defendant did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy where he was parked. Whether defendant intended for others to view him was irrelevant, as § 944.20(1)(b) did not require a finding of intent. The appellate court declined to consider defendant's argument that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because the issue was inadequately briefed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Brown County v. Wis. Empl. Rels. Comm'n


Appeal No. 04-0692


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2004 WI App 220; 277 Wis. 2d 591; 690 N.W.2d 26; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 828



October 19, 2004, Decided  
October 19, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Brown County: THOMAS S. WILLIAMS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CV1141.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county filed a declaratory judgment action in the Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, arguing that either judicial assistants could not constitutionally be included in a collective bargaining unit or that they were confidential employees under the Municipal Employee Relations Act, Wis. Stat. § 111.70(1)(i) (2001-02). The trial court dismissed the action. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county argued that the trial court improperly exercised its discretion because it concluded in a cursory fashion the issues to be resolved were factual rather than analyzing statutory and case law to resolve its motion, and that the trial court should have found that including judicial assistants in a collective bargaining unit violated the separation of powers by infringing on the inherent constitutional authority of the judicial branch. The appellate court noted that jurisdiction of agencies had to be given priority in the absence of a valid reason for judicial intervention. The appellate court held that the distinction between confidential and municipal employees often depended not on posted job descriptions but on a factual record that had to first be developed before the agency. The appellate court concluded that the Wisconsin Employment Relations Commission could find that judicial assistants were confidential employees thereby avoiding the constitutional question entirely.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Peterson v. Arlington Hospitality Staffing, Inc.


Appeal No. 03-2811


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 199; 276 Wis. 2d 746; 689 N.W.2d 61; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 755; 21 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1726


August 11, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
September 22, 2004, Decided  
September 22, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Peterson v. Arlington Hospitality, 2005 WI 1, 277 Wis. 2d 152, 691 N.W.2d 354, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 1085 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: ROBERT G. MAWDSLEY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CV000705.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee was sexually assaulted by a coemployee. She sued defendant employer for negligence, asserting the employer knew or should have known the coemployee had previous incidents of sexual assaults and employed him without advising her or other employees of his past history. The Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, granted summary judgment for the employer based on Wis. Stat. § 102.03(2) (2001-02). The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended that the Wisconsin Worker's Compensation Act's (WCA) exclusive remedy provision, Wis. Stat. § 102.03(2) (2001-02), should not have precluded a claim by an employee against an employer for negligent hiring, training and supervision when the injury was a sexual assault committed by a coemployee. She presented several public policy reasons in favor of the creation of an exception. However, the appellate court held that her claims for injuries caused by the sexual assault upon her by the coemployee were precluded by the exclusivity provision in § 102.03(2). The WCAs purpose, history and application demonstrated that the appellate court was not the proper authority to create a public policy exception to the WCAs exclusivity provision. The appellate court also held that § 102.03(2) did not violate the employee's rights to equal protection and due process. The appellate court noted that the multiple and protracted lawsuits in circuit courts which would have ensued if employers were exposed to tort claims for the intentional conduct of other employees would have emasculated the WCA, and would have adversely affected employers, employees and the public.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Allen v. Guerrero


Appeal No. 03-1356


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 188; 276 Wis. 2d 679; 688 N.W.2d 673; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 744


February 11, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
September 16, 2004, Decided  
September 16, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: C. WILLIAM FOUST, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CV001236.
State v. Allen, 192 Wis. 2d 766, 532 N.W.2d 470, 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 441 (Wis. Ct. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Department of Corrections parole agents (parole agents), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion to dismiss plaintiff inmate's action that the parole agents violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII by deliberately refusing to release him on parole.


OVERVIEW: The parole agents appealed an order denying their motion to dismiss the inmate's action filed under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The parole agents contended that they were entitled to qualified immunity from the inmate's claim that they violated the U.S. Const. amend. VIII's prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment by deliberately refusing to release him on parole for 377 days beyond his mandatory release (MR) date. The court affirmed, stating that a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 defendant was not entitled to qualified immunity, when, even if there was some uncertainty in the law regarding precisely which constitutional provision was violated, the law nonetheless clearly established that the alleged conduct violated the United States Constitution. Further, at the time the inmate reached his MR date, the law clearly established, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 302.11 (2001-02), that deliberately holding a person in prison beyond a statutorily prescribed release date violated a right guaranteed by the constitution. Accordingly, the court affirmed the order permitting the inmate's claim to proceed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
