State v. Middaugh


Appeal No. 04-0870-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2004 WI App 205; 276 Wis. 2d 865; 688 N.W.2d 784; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 716



September 1, 2004, Decided  
September 1, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Middaugh, 2005 WI 1, 277 Wis. 2d 153, 691 N.W.2d 355, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 1119 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: FRED H. HAZLEWOOD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CT000070.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed pro se from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County (Wisconsin) convicting her for operating while intoxicated, second offense, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: From the very outset of her encounter with an officer, defendant asked for an attorney. Because this request was not immediately accommodated, defendant argued that she was denied her right to counsel and that the forced blood test result should have been suppressed. Defendant's argument was previously rejected by the Wisconsin Supreme Court. In Wisconsin, there was no right under the implied consent statute to consult with an attorney before deciding whether to submit to a chemical test. Because defendant already consented to the test, it was unnecessary to secure the advice of an attorney about the decision to submit. Contrary to defendant's assertions, Wis. Stat. § 885.235 (2001-02) did not distinguish between a chemical test that resulted from a blood draw under the implied consent law or one obtained involuntarily following a refusal. The instant court upheld the circuit court's admission of the blood draw result, which reflected a blood ethanol concentration of 0.202 g/100 ml. In addition to the blood test result, the jury heard testimony from the officer. Based on his observations and experience, the officer believed defendant to be under the influence of intoxicants.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

City of Madison v. Spruill


Appeal No. 03-2296


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2004 WI App 186; 276 Wis. 2d 570; 687 N.W.2d 548; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 695



August 26, 2004, Decided  
August 26, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 03TR003491 03TR003493.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, charged with operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated and operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration, moved to suppress a chemical breath test and post-arrest statements to police. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, granted defendant's motion, and the City appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motion was decided, by stipulation, based on an officer's police report, which stated he saw defendant's vehicle drive "closely behind" others vehicles, veer within its lane, and make a right-hand turn without coming to a full stop or signaling. The officer stopped defendant's vehicle and noted a strong odor of intoxicants inside the vehicle. The circuit court held that too much information was missing from the report to support a reasonable suspicion that defendant's driving behaviors were unusual or erratic. The appellate court agreed, noting that an investigative stop was presumptively unconstitutional. The police report lacked such key facts as defendant's speed, the speed limit, and road and traffic conditions. Under Wis. Stat. § 364.14(1) (2003), following a vehicle "extremely closely" was unusual only if the driver followed more closely than was reasonable and prudent, having due regard for speed, traffic, and highway conditions. Under Wis. Stat. § 346.34 (2003), failure to give a right-hand turn signal was not a traffic violation unless other traffic was affected. Inconsequential movement within a lane did not give an officer the authority to make an investigative stop.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Filtz


Appeal No. 04-0324-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2004 WI App 186; 276 Wis. 2d 572; 687 N.W.2d 549; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 680



August 25, 2004, Decided  
August 25, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Filtz, 2005 WI 1, 277 Wis. 2d 153, 691 N.W.2d 355, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 1112 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Walworth County: ROBERT J. KENNEDY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which found in favor of defendant and suppressed all evidence obtained in an investigation of a hit-and-run accident involving defendant.


OVERVIEW: The police department was called about a hit-and-run accident in the parking lot of an establishment and employees notified the officer that they observed an intoxicated patron, defendant, leaving, stumbling as she left. Two officers went to her home and asked her 16-year-old son to wake her. At that time, the son left the door open and the officers followed him inside to the living room. The officers were successful in waking her and she admitted that she had been driving and that she had obviously hit something with her vehicle. The trial court suppressed the evidence as a result of a U.S. Const. amend. IV violation, but the court reversed. The officers were acting within their authority to investigate the hit-and-run accident and they also had consent from the son to enter defendant's home. Their entry into the home was neither unlawful nor unconstitutional. Further, defendant was not in custody while inside her home, or outside her home when inspecting her vehicle. She was not placed in custody until the officers had probable cause to arrest her. Therefore, the evidence obtained in the investigation should not have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Antonicci


Appeal No. 04-0292-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2004 WI App 186; 276 Wis. 2d 572; 687 N.W.2d 549; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 682



August 25, 2004, Decided  
August 25, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: JAMES R. KIEFFER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CM000123.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of disorderly conduct in violation of Wis. Stat. § 947.01 (2001-02) and denied his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conduct toward his ex-girlfriend's new boyfriend resulted in a conviction for disorderly conduct. The court affirmed, stating that his conduct offended the sensibilities of the reasonable person and was exactly the type of conduct contemplated by the "otherwise disorderly" provision of Wis. Stat. § 947.01 (2001-02). Defendant had a history of harassment against the victim. He had sent letters, left notes, and made many phone calls, all of which included thinly veiled threats against the victim. Indeed, defendant had a restraining order in place against him relating to the victim. Defendant also endangered the lives of other innocent motorists when he followed the victim. Further, because defendant's conduct constituted "otherwise disorderly" conduct that created a "real possibility" of disrupting peace and good order, Wis. Stat. § 947.01 was appropriately applied to his conduct in the case. The statute was not overbroad nor vague because defendant had sufficient notice that his actions would have been in violation of § 947.01.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Martin


Appeal No. 03-3131


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2004 WI App 167; 276 Wis. 2d 310; 686 N.W.2d 456; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 592



July 27, 2004, Decided  
July 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KAREN E. CHRISTENSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99CF006114.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denied defendant's original and "supplemental" Wis. Stat. § 974.06 (2001-02) motions for sentence modification. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with escape. He pled guilty, and he was sentenced to six months' confinement and ordered to provide a DNA sample. Defendant argued Wis. Stat. § 973.047 (2001-02) violated the Fourth Amendment. However, he did not offer any evidence showing that Wisconsin's DNA collection statute was established for anything other than future law enforcement purposes. Thus, he failed to show that § 973.047, as applied, was an ex post facto law. He contended trial counsel was ineffective because he did not advise defendant on what plea to enter. The trial court properly denied the ineffective-assistance claim because defendant presented only conclusory allegations. Defendant questioned whether the trial court properly denied his first Wis. Stat. § 974.06 motion. It did. Defendant did not offer a sufficient reason for his failure to raise all of his claims in his first § 974.06 motion and he did not do so on appeal. Accordingly, any claims raised for the first time in his second § 974.06 motion were procedurally barred, and the trial court properly denied his "supplemental" § 974.06 motion. Defendant could not seek sentence modification under § 974.06.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Diamondback Funding, LLC v. Chili's of Wis., Inc.


Appeal No. 03-2376


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 161; 276 Wis. 2d 81; 687 N.W.2d 89; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 599


July 7, 2004, Oral Argument  
July 27, 2004, Decided  
July 27, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Diamondback Funding, LLC v. Chili's of Wis., Inc., 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 468 (Wis. Ct. App., May 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CV008729.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent restaurant in a restrictive covenant dispute.


OVERVIEW: The owner purchased the lot from the seller. As part of the sale, the seller agreed to restrict an adjoining lot to prohibit the operation of any restaurants specializing in Mexican food. Modifications to the restrictive covenant were made by the seller and a third party. Subsequently, the lot was sold to the restaurant. After a dispute arose between the parties, the owner filed a complaint seeking to enjoin the restaurant from operating on the lot. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the restaurant after finding that the restrictive covenant was ambiguous. In reversing, the court determined that the modification of the restrictive covenant did not dilute the owner's rights under the original agreement. As such, the purported modification was a nullity. In addition, the terms "specializing in" and "primarily" were not ambiguous. The fact that the standard was difficult to apply did not make the terms ambiguous or vague. However, the court determined that summary judgment was inappropriate because there were genuine issues of fact that required a trial. The court noted that the seller may have been a necessary party to any further proceedings in the case.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

913 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ragsdale


Appeal No. 03-2795-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 178; 276 Wis. 2d 52; 687 N.W.2d 785; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 551


June 2, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
July 7, 2004, Decided  
July 7, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Ragsdale, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 30, 689 N.W.2d 57, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 929 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CF004207.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A gun was found in defendant's home after a police officer asked defendant's three-year-old son if there were any guns in the house and the child showed the officer where the shotgun was hidden. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence. Defendant appealed after pleading guilty to one count of felon in possession of a firearm, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.29(2) (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the police questioning of his son while he was not present constituted an invalid search leading to the discovery of the gun. He argued that the search was unconstitutional and the trial court should have granted his suppression motion. The appellate court was not persuaded. Defendant consented to police entry and search of his residence in response to the gun complaint. The dispute was whether the questioning of defendant's son, after defendant left his son alone with the officer in the living room, violated the scope of the consent and amounted to deceit or trickery. The appellate court held that such conduct suggested that defendant did not assert any reasonable expectation of privacy prohibiting the officer from speaking with his son. Moreover, the officer's question to the child probably did not even constitute a search. Rather, it was on-the-scene questioning of a potential witness in an ongoing investigation. What happened after the officer's question was solely at the child's own volition. The child proceeded to pull open a heating vent, plainly exposing a shotgun. At the point the child moved the vent, the gun was in plain view and had to be seized.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

914 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Grant County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Unified Bd. of Grant & Ia. Counties (In re Jane E.P.)


Appeal No. 03-0634


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 153; 275 Wis. 2d 680; 687 N.W.2d 72; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 547


April 27, 2004, Oral Argument  
July 1, 2004, Decided  
July 1, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Grant County Dep't of Soc. Servs. v. Unified Bd. of Grant & Iowa Counties, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 26, 689 N.W.2d 55, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 802 (2004)
Vacated by, Remanded by Grant County Dep't of Social Services v. Unified Board of Grant and Iowa Counties (In re Jane E. P.), 2005 WI 106, 283 Wis. 2d 258, 700 N.W.2d 863, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 343 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Grant County: ROBERT P. VAN DE HAY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02GN000029.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Grant County Department of Social Services, petitioned for guardianship and protective placement of an Illinois resident. Respondent board, the agency responsible for performing evaluations on individuals who were the subject of guardianships, moved to dismiss based on the residency requirement of Wis. Stat. § 55.06(3)(c) (2001-02). The Circuit Court for Grant County, Wisconsin, granted the dismissal. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The subject of the petition for guardianship was a 46-year-old woman who suffered from Wernicke's encephalopathy, was on Medicaid, and had family in Grant County. The appeals court reversed the dismissal of the petition, finding that the statutory residency requirements violated her right to interstate travel. The court reasoned that the subject could not live in the nursing home near her family without a protective placement order and, under Wisconsin statutes, she could not access the court to receive such an order without first living in a Wisconsin County. Because she was incompetent, she could not first move to Wisconsin outside a nursing home and have a petition for protective placement filed on her behalf. Therefore, § 55.06(3)(c) unconstitutionally burdened her right to travel. Section 55.06(3)(c) did not establish a bona fide residency requirement, but restricted the subject's ability to access the courts for consideration of her only means to move to Wisconsin. The board's claim of fiscal burden was speculative. The power of the State to confine its public services to residents did not entitle it to establish arbitrary barriers to a nonresident's becoming a resident.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the petition and remanded for proceedings consistent with the order.

Chenequa Land Conservancy, Inc. v. Vill. of Hartland


Appeal No. 03-2486


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 144; 275 Wis. 2d 533; 685 N.W.2d 573; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 524


March 18, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
June 24, 2004, Decided  
June 24, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03CV000192.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff conservancy corporation filed an action seeking a declaration that the conveyance of state property to defendant village was void because the conveyance violated Wis. Stat. § 84.09(5) (2001-02) and a manual of the Wisconsin Department of Transportation (DOT). The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted summary judgment in favor of the conservancy. The village, along with defendant association, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The conservancy entered into a contract with a village that made a competing offer for the property. The competing offer was rejected, and the conservancy brought a complaint challenging DOT's conveyance of the property. The complaint alleged that the letter report submitted to the governor was not a full and complete report as required by § 84.09(5). Defendants brought a motion to dismiss based on their position that the conservancy did not have standing to bring the action. The circuit court denied the motion. The circuit court then granted summary judgment in favor of the conservancy, determining that title to the property remained in the state. On appeal, the court reversed, stating that the conservancy did not have a legally protectible interest in the requirement in § 84.09(5) that DOT provide a complete report to the governor or in the requirement of the governor's approval. The "full and complete report" was plainly for the governor's benefit, not the benefit of potential purchasers. Additionally, a manual prepared by DOT for use in sales under that statute could not alter that result.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded with directions to enter an order dismissing the amended complaint.

State v. Thiel (In re Thiel)


Appeal No. 03-2098


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 140; 275 Wis. 2d 421; 685 N.W.2d 890; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 499


May 17, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
June 16, 2004, Decided  
June 16, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Thiel, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 29, 689 N.W.2d 57, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 896 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: PETER L. GRIMM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 97CF000152.
State v. Thiel (In re Thiel), 241 Wis. 2d 465, 626 N.W.2d 26, 2001 WI App 32, 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 42 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an alleged sexually violent person, requested discharge from involuntary commitment pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.09(2) (2001-02). The Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Wisconsin, denied the petition. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that he established probable cause to believe that he was no longer a sexually violent person by the submission of an examiner's report that recommended supervised release. Petitioner's reliance on Wis. Stat. § 980.09(2)(c) (2001-02) was misplaced. Probable cause to believe a person was no longer a sexually violent person was not satisfied by a recommendation of supervised release without more. Petitioner next argued that Wis. Stat. § 980.09 (2001-02) violated his due process rights. Nevertheless, under the statute, a committed individual who was unable to proceed under § 980.09 was not without the opportunity to pursue a less restrictive alternative to commitment. Petitioner next contended that his due process rights were violated because the circuit court failed to initiate proceedings following remand. Petitioner's letter asking the circuit court to take action in his case was filed 10 months after remittitur, well within the one-year time limit established by the statute. The circuit court responded promptly, requesting clarification. As soon as petitioner clarified matters, the trial court took swift and appropriate action.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

City of Berlin v. Bartol


Appeal No. 03-3492


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2004 WI App 149; 275 Wis. 2d 879; 685 N.W.2d 173; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 481



June 9, 2004, Decided  
June 9, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Green Lake County: WILLIAM M. MCMONIGAL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03TR000432.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Circuit Court for Green Lake County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of a first offense of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI) and first offense operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a), (b). The circuit court had denied her motion to suppress the results of a blood test administered following her arrest. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the arresting officer's request for a blood test, to which she consented, was unreasonable because less intrusive tests were available and should have been used because her case was deemed to be civil as a first offense. The court disagreed. In case law discussing the permissibility of blood tests, the Wisconsin Supreme Court had expressly addressed arrests for a drunk-driving related violation or crime. The phrase "violation or crime" revealed the contemplated application of these requirements to noncriminal offenses. Thus, a blood draw taken to obtain evidence of intoxication from a person lawfully arrested for a civil drunk-driving related violation was permissible if all remaining requirements were also satisfied. Defendant did not contest the three remaining requirements. Thus, the test did not violate the Fourth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. John S. (In re Stachel S.)


Appeal No. 04-0676


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2004 WI App 149; 275 Wis. 2d 880; 685 N.W.2d 173; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 480



June 8, 2004, Decided  
June 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. John S., 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 31, 689 N.W.2d 58, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 957 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOSEPH R. WALL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02TP000787.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which terminated his parental rights to a child.


OVERVIEW: The father claimed that actual notice regarding the termination of his parental rights was required. The court order removing the child from the mother's care specifically warned of the possible termination of parental rights, as required by Wis. Stat. § 48.356(2). Thus, the trial court's directed verdict was proper. Next, the father argued that Wis. Stat. § 48.415(1)(a)2, as applied to him, was unconstitutional, as there was no evidence that he actually received notice, thus, his due process rights were violated. The notice procedures in the statute satisfied basic due process rights. Thus, the father did not satisfy his burden of showing that the statute was unconstitutional. Finally, the father argued that the trial court erred when it instructed the jury that a parent's lack of opportunity and/or ability to establish a substantial parental relationship was not a defense to failure to assume parental responsibility. But, the State still held the same burden of proving failure to assume parental responsibility by clear and convincing evidence, and the father was still permitted present evidence that he established a parental relationship with the child.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) that denied his motion for modification of custody and physical placement of his minor son.


OVERVIEW: The father argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion for custody modification because he showed a substantial change in circumstances. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court erred in finding that there was no substantial change in circumstances because, at the time of the original custody and placement order, the father saw the child every day, and at the time of the modification hearing the father saw the child only every other weekend. The child was well adjusted, was doing well in school and was participating in both sports and an accelerated learning program. The father failed to rebut the presumption that the allocation of decision making under the legal custody order and the continuation of the child's primary physical placement with the mother were in the best interest of the child.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted the State of Wisconsin's petition to commit him as a sexually violent person pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 980.

State v. Thomas


Appeal No. 03-1369-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 115; 274 Wis. 2d 513; 683 N.W.2d 497; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 415


March 2, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
May 18, 2004, Decided  
May 18, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Thomas, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 28, 689 N.W.2d 56, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 855 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM SOSNAY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CF006130.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of felon in possession of a gun.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed: (1) Wis. Const. art. I, § 25 effectively repealed Wis. Stat. § 941.29 (2001-02); (2) section 941.29 was unconstitutionally vague, overbroad, and violated the Equal Protection Clause of the United States and Wisconsin Constitutions; and (3) he was entitled to a new trial in the interest of justice because the verdicts were inconsistent. First, the intent behind Wis. Const. art. I, § 25 was to preserve the Wisconsin Legislature's authority to restrict the possession of firearms by felons. Second, the right to bear arms was a qualified right, subject to reasonable restrictions under the State's police power. The restriction placed upon felons prohibiting them from possessing firearms was a reasonable exercise of the State's inherent police power. A rational relationship existed between statutes forbidding possession of firearms by any and all convicted felons and the legitimate state purpose of protecting the public from the misuse of firearms. Third, inconsistency in criminal verdicts was not per se grounds for reversal, and there was no inconsistency in the verdict in light of the evidence presented.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Auger


Appeal No. 03-3306-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2004 WI App 125; 275 Wis. 2d 278; 683 N.W.2d 94; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 405



May 11, 2004, Decided  
May 11, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by State v. Auger, 2004 WI 114, 684 N.W.2d 139, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 634 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Outagamie County: MICHAEL W. GAGE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CM000466.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, pro se, appealed a judgment of conviction for disorderly conduct with a domestic abuse assessment and an order denying his postconviction motions from the Circuit Court in Outagamie County (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous challenges, but the instant court rejected them all. Defendant first protested that the real controversy was not fully tried, as the jury was not charged with determining whether he was guilty of domestic abuse. However, the trial court imposed the domestic abuse surcharge under Wis. Stat. § 973.055 (2001-02). Thus, if the statutory conditions were fulfilled, the court was obligated to make the assessment. Here, defendant was convicted under Wis. Stat. § 947.01 (2001-02), fulfilling the first prong, and the conduct constituting the violation involved his wife, fulfilling the second prong. Moreover, the statute explicitly granted the sentencing authority to the court; there was nothing for a jury to deliberate. The assessment was properly imposed. The court properly ordered his wife's testimony. Defendant claimed that the jury should have been given a self-defense instruction, but he never objected to the instructions. To the extent that defendant claimed he made a prima facie case of discriminatory prosecution, it was not enough for him to claim a reasonable person, free of sexual prejudice, would have concluded that his wife was the aggressor.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

State v. Miller


Appeal No. 03-1747-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 117; 274 Wis. 2d 471; 683 N.W.2d 485; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 393


February 11, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
May 6, 2004, Decided  
May 6, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Miller, 2004 WI 123, 275 Wis. 2d 296, 687 N.W.2d 523, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 709 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CF001003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which entered a conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant (OWI). The charge resulting in the conviction was refiled after the trial court dismissed the charge without prejudice following its decision to exclude certain State's evidence as a sanction for a violation of the discovery statute, Wis. Stat. § 971.23 (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court in the second action erred in denying his motion to exclude evidence because of the decision in the first action to exclude it. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that exclusion in the second action was not required by § 971.23, by the equal protection clause, or by any of the preclusion and estoppel doctrines on which defendant relied. The court stated that there was nothing in § 971.23(7m) to suggest that the State could not obtain a dismissal of charges after evidence was excluded and then refile the charges. Additionally, the court stated that § 971.23(7m) did not violate the equal protection clause. The State had a legitimate interest in the prosecution of criminal charges, consistent with the constitutional rights afforded defendant. Allowing the State the opportunity to dismiss and refile charges when evidence had been excluded under § 971.23(7m) but might not be excluded in a new action furthered that interest in a rational way. Claim preclusion was inapplicable, because there was no final judgment on the merits. The order excluding the evidence did not in any sense decide the merits of the charges against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

925 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holze


Appeal No. 03-1506-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2004 WI App 125; 275 Wis. 2d 276; 683 N.W.2d 93; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 383



May 4, 2004, Decided  
May 4, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Holze, 2004 WI 138, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 862 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER and JOHN FRANKE, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 00CF004420.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered a conviction of one count of possession of child pornography in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.12 (1999-2000). Defendant also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Police executed a search warrant at defendant's residence and seized his computer. A floppy disk found in the computer contained an image of a child engaged in sexually explicit conduct. Defendant was subsequently convicted of possession of child pornography. On appeal, defendant contended that § 948.12 was both overbroad and vague. The court disagreed, stating that child pornography was not protected under the First Amendment and § 948.12 constitutionally prohibited its possession. Defendant also contended that the State should have been required to prove that the child was indeed under the age of 18 and that the child was an actual person. The court stated that, in this case, additional evidence regarding the age of the child was not necessary and that the determination of whether the image was an actual child was properly within the province of the jury. The court also held that computer disks that stored images of child pornography were included within the meaning of the phrase "or other pictorial reproduction" in § 948.12. Finally, the court rejected defendant's argument that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to bring a motion challenging the search warrant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

State v. Jones


Appeal No. 03-1436-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2004 WI App 125; 275 Wis. 2d 276; 683 N.W.2d 93; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 385



May 4, 2004, Decided  
May 4, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEAN W. DiMOTTO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CF000132.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was a police detective and youth minister, pled guilty to enticing a child for purposes of exposing a sex organ, Wis. Stat. § 948.07 (1999-2000), based on allegations of an extended sexual relationship with a 16-year-old girl. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, imposed seven years in prison and five years of extended supervision. Defendant appealed the conviction and the denial of postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: When imposing sentence, the trial court mistakenly referred to enticing the victim for purposes of sexual contact rather than for exposure. The reviewing court held that the error was harmless. The postconviction court had explained that the specific motive did not affect the basis for the sentence because the act of enticement was done for the purpose of a sexually inappropriate act. That explanation reflected an accurate understanding of the law. The postconviction court also properly rejected any argument that the victim's conduct reduced the gravity of the offense. Defendant did not establish the lower court's reliance on allegedly inaccurate information that he impregnated the victim or that she attempted suicide. The sentencing remarks established a clear focus on defendant's violation of his positions of trust. Thus, the disclaimer of reliance on pregnancy and attempted suicide was not implausible, as defendant argued. Finally, considering defendant's misuse of his position as a youth minister, his job as a police officer, his age, and his education, and considering the emotional trauma suffered by the victim and her family, the sentence is not unduly harsh or excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State ex rel. Harr v. Berge


Appeal No. 03-2611


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 105; 273 Wis. 2d 481; 681 N.W.2d 282; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 316


February 23, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
April 14, 2004, Decided  
April 14, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State ex rel. Harr v. Berge, 2004 WI 123, 275 Wis. 2d 297, 687 N.W.2d 523, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 729 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PAUL B. HIGGINBOTHAM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CV001131.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Real party in interest, an inmate, successfully pursued a common law certiorari action to overturn a disciplinary reprimand imposed after prison authorities intercepted a letter to his parents in which he described a corrections officer in derogatory terms. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, denied the inmate's motion for fees and costs. It also denied a motion to reconsider and reaffirmed its decision. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that Wis. Stat. § 814.25(2) (2001-02) violated his constitutional right to equal protection, because it prohibited him from an award of costs and fees after he prevailed in a common law certiorari action. The court disagreed. Prisoners did not constitute a suspect class for equal protection purposes, and therefore equal protection required only that the classification bear a rational relation to some legitimate end. The court found two rationales the legislature could have embraced. (1) In the case of prisoner actions challenging the conditions of confinement, the legislature could validly conclude that the successful prisoner should not be reimbursed from the public treasury, because the only person who benefited from the litigation was the prisoner. (2) The legislature could reasonably conclude that a prisoner was not entitled to the reimbursement of costs and fees, because the prisoner already received, from the public treasury, paper and pen to draft legal documents, and law libraries. In addition, a prisoner was given access to adequate assistance from "writ writers" and "jailhouse lawyers," a form of assistance a free person was not provided by the State.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Brown


Appeal No. 03-1717-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2004 WI App 109; 273 Wis. 2d 785; 680 N.W.2d 833; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 308



April 13, 2004, Dated  
April 13, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Brown County: DONALD R. ZUIDMULDER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CF000729.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of child enticement and possession of marijuana after the entry of a guilty plea. Defendant also challenged the decision requiring him to register as a sex offender under Wis. Stat. § 301.45 (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly supplied minors with marijuana for sexual purposes. Later, defendant entered a no-contest plea to child enticement under Wis. Stat. § 948.07(6) (1997-98) and possession of marijuana. After defendant was placed on probation, he was ordered to register under Wis. Stat. § 301.45 (2001-02). Thereafter, defendant sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the classification of defendant as a sex offender did not violate his due process and equal protection rights under the Fourteenth Amendment and Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. The Wisconsin Legislature could have rationally concluded that defendant's conduct posed a threat to public safety. It was disingenuous for defendant to argue that there was no rational relationship between enticing a child into a secluded place to use illegal drugs and the purpose of protecting children from sexual assaults. Moreover, the court rejected defendant's due process argument because the means chosen by the Wisconsin Legislature to effect a valid legislative objective bore a rational relationship to the purpose it sought to achieve. Therefore, the court rejected defendant's "as-applied" constitutional challenges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Jensen


Appeal No. 03-0106-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 89; 272 Wis. 2d 707; 681 N.W.2d 230; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 276


November 20, 2003, Oral Argument  
April 1, 2004, Decided  
April 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Jensen, 2004 WI 114, 273 Wis. 2d 654, 684 N.W.2d 136, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 491 (2004)
Affirmed by State v. Jensen, 2005 WI 31, 279 Wis. 2d 220, 694 N.W.2d 56, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 140 (2005)
Subsequent appeal at, Cause remanded by, Motion for new trial granted by State v. Jensen, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 973 (Wis. Ct. App., Nov. 8, 2007)
Subsequent appeal at, Cause remanded by, Motion for new trial granted by, Sub nomine at State v. Schultz, 2007 Wisc. App. LEXIS 974 (Wis. Ct. App., Nov. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 02CF002453, 02CF002454, 02CF002455.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, members of the Wisconsin State Assembly and an employee, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, which denied their motion to dismiss. The criminal complaint charged defendants with misconduct in public office as parties to a crime, Wis. Stat. §§ 939.05, 946.12(3) (2001-02), and intentional misuse of public positions for private benefit, Wis. Stat. § 19.45(2).


OVERVIEW: The criminal complaint alleged, among other things, that the assembly members hired the employee to solicit money for political campaigns while being paid as a state employee or using state resources. The court affirmed the decision not to dismiss the complaint, finding that: (1) Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) was not unconstitutionally vague, but adequately delineated a duty that could be ascertained by reference to applicable statutes and the Assembly Employee Handbook; (2) defendants had adequate notice, as their duties were delineated in the handbook, an internal e-mail and memo, an Ethics Board advisory opinion, and Wis. Stat. §§ 11.001(2), 11.36, 12.07(3), and 19.45, .46; a reasonable person would be aware that it violated one's duty as a public official to obtain a dishonest advantage by waging partisan political campaigns with state resources on state time; (3) it was irrelevant to the vagueness challenge that defendants were unaware they could be prosecuted for violating Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3); (4) the statute was not overly broad; (5) the prosecution did not violate the separation of power or political activity doctrines; and (6) the allegations supported probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order denying defendants' motion to dismiss.

March 25, 2004, Decided  
March 25, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Dane County v. McGrew, 2004 WI 138, 276 Wis. 2d 27, 689 N.W.2d 55, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 810 (2004)
Affirmed by Dane County v. McGrew, 2005 WI 130, 285 Wis. 2d 519, 699 N.W.2d 890, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 404 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: C. WILLIAM FOUST, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02TR008507.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of speeding, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4)(h) (2001-02), and denied his motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving on a highway when he was pulled over and issued a citation for speeding. He was subsequently convicted of speeding, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.57(4)(h) (2001-02), and his motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict was also denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant essentially argued that the deputy's testimony that he paced defendant's car at 80 miles per hour was incredible as a matter of law, because it was inconsistent with other parts of the deputy's testimony. But the flaw in defendant's argument was that he implicitly assumed that the jury was required to accept as accurate several of the details of the deputy's testimony, such as where he was when he first observed defendant. Further, defendant argued that he was denied due process because he was denied access to the deputy's incident report and the notations on the back of the citation, but defendant failed to show that the evidence was exculpatory. There was insufficient evidence to show that the radar unit could not have yielded a result consistent with the incident report and with the deputy's testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Zoellick, 2004 WI 114, 273 Wis. 2d 657, 684 N.W.2d 138, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 607 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Zoellick v. Wis., 543 U.S. 959, 125 S. Ct. 412, 160 L. Ed. 2d 322, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7163 (U.S., Nov. 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Calumet County: DONALD A. POPPY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CM000058.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Calument County (Wisconsin) of two counts of disorderly conduct. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. The victim's daughter observed a vehicle drive by the victim's residence twice in one morning. She believed that the vehicle was driven by defendant, the person stalking her mother. Later, the daughter again contacted the sheriff's department about a suspicious vehicle. That time, an officer located and stopped the suspect vehicle, making contact with defendant. Defendant was very evasive about why he was in the area. Defendant's conduct, when looked at in the context of his pattern of behavior over 25 years, showed an obsessive interest at the least. His appearance and conduct in the parking lot at a restaurant and his repeated driving by the home two days later exemplified the extent of his obsession. Such conduct had the tendency to disrupt the peace, safety, and good order, because, as the victim's testimony demonstrated, his contact was unwelcome and abusive in nature. Further, his conduct was likely to cause or provoke a disturbance because it caused concern from other members of the victim's family and the community as a whole, including the police.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Review dismissed by State v. Bathe, 2004 WI 50, 271 Wis. 2d 112, 679 N.W.2d 547, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 389 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part Bathe v. Benik, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 22268 (W.D. Wis., Sept. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: BRUCE E. SCHROEDER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 93CF000768.
State v. Bathe, 207 Wis. 2d 640, 207 Wis. 2d 643, 559 N.W.2d 923, 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1568 (Wis. Ct. App., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) as a party to the crimes of attempted first-degree homicide while armed, armed burglary, and conspiracy to commit armed robbery. Defendant's postconviction motion for ineffective assistance of trial counsel and postconviction counsel was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the postconviction court was not required to conduct a Machner hearing, as: (1) defendant waived his argument that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to seek lesser-included offenses; (2) the multiple prosecutions and resulting convictions for conspiracy to commit armed robbery and armed burglary as a party to the crimes did not violate defendant's double jeopardy rights; (3) while the record did not show that the jurors took notes, assuming that the trial court did allow note taking and failed to deliver the preliminary instructions required by Wis. Stat. § 805.13(2)(a)(1) (2001-02), defendant failed to demonstrate any resulting prejudice; (4) the facial conflict between the trial court's final instructions to the jury on armed robbery charge and the form of the verdict regarding that charge did not constitute error, much less reversible error, and trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise this issue; and (5) postconviction counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise defendant's challenges to the performance of his trial counsel, as trial counsel was not ineffective and defendant failed to establish prejudice.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Jennings


Appeal No. 03-1162-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2004 WI App 68; 271 Wis. 2d 819; 677 N.W.2d 733; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 172



February 25, 2004, Decided  
February 25, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE A PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Jennings, 2004 WI 114, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 561 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: PATRICK L. WILLIS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CF000308.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment convicting him of first-degree sexual assault of a child (penis-vagina) after a jury in the Circuit Court for Manitowoc County, Wisconsin, rejected his claim that he was not guilty by reason of mental defect. Defendant claimed the trial court erred in admitting the victim's statements under Wis. Stat. § 908.03(2), (24) (2001-02) and in admitting his statement to the police.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sexually assaulted a four year old child. The victim's brother observed the assault and told his mother's fiance, who also lived in the home. The victim told her mother's fiance what occurred, and also described the assault to a doctor. When the police went to question defendant, the police noticed that defendant seemed to be of limited intellectual ability. Defendant admitted to having sexual intercourse with the victim within the first 30 minutes of his conversation with the police. On appeal, defendant claimed the trial court erred in admitting his statement, and erred in admitting the hearsay testimony of the victim. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. The appellate court held defendant's statement was properly admitted as defendant was not under any particular pressure during the interview, no threats were made and he spoke freely with the detectives. Defendant's limited intellectual ability did not affect the voluntariness of the statement. The child's statements were properly admitted under the excited utterance exception and the residual exception to the hearsay rule as the victim was four and the statements were made within eight hours of the assault.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

State v. Chvala


Case No. 03-0442-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 53; 271 Wis. 2d 115; 678 N.W.2d 880; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 136


November 20, 2003, Argued  
February 12, 2004, Decided  
February 12, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Chvala, 2004 WI 114, 273 Wis. 2d 654, 684 N.W.2d 136, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 493 (2004)
Affirmed by State v. Chvala, 2005 WI 30, 279 Wis. 2d 216, 693 N.W.2d 747, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 141 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CF002451.
State v. Chvala, 2003 WI 91, 262 Wis. 2d 504, 665 N.W.2d 378, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 595 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Modified and, as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a senator and leader in the Wisconsin Legislature, was charged with felony misconduct in office, Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) (2001-02). The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) denied his motion to dismiss. Defendant appealed, arguing that § 946.12(3) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, that the prosecution violated Wisconsin's speech and debate clause, Wis. Const. art. IV, § 16, and violated the separation of powers doctrine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged, as majority leader, with hiring and directing senate caucus employees to conduct campaign activities using state offices, equipment, and supplies. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 946.12(3) was not vague or overly broad as applied. Defendant clearly had a duty to steer clear of a proscribed area of conduct, as determined by reference to a variety of sources, including the Wisconsin Senate Policy Manual, applicable statutes, and legislative rules and guidelines. The Senate Policy Manual prohibited political activity during working hours, as well as the use of State facilities, equipment, or supplies for political purposes at any time. The court found that the terms "political activity" and "political purpose" provided fair notice, because they plainly included political campaign activity. The speech and debate clause, Wis. Const. art. IV, § 16, also did not bar the prosecution, as the criminal complaint specifically identified personnel decisions that bore no resemblance to the due functioning of the legislative process. Examination by the court of the senate's unambiguous rules did not violate the separation-of-powers or political-question doctrines.


OUTCOME: The court modified the circuit court's order with regard to specific activities, as to which the court found ambiguity and therefore potential violations of the separation of powers doctrine. As modified, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Arnold v. Arnold


Appeal No. 03-1547


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 62; 270 Wis. 2d 705; 679 N.W.2d 296; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 104


January 22, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
February 4, 2004, Decided  
February 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Arnold v. Arnold, 2004 WI 50, 271 Wis. 2d 112, 679 N.W.2d 547, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 366 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Arnold v. Arnold, 160 L. Ed. 2d 122, 125 S. Ct. 112, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 6608 (U.S., Oct. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: RALPH M. RAMIREZ, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00FA000131.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, father, challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Wisconsin, awarding him placement of the children 102 days per year, not the 182.5 days of equal placement per year as he had requested, in the underlying case involving respondent, mother.


OVERVIEW: The father wanted equal placement, and argued that Wis. Stat. § 767.24(4)(a) (2001-2002) required it. The appellate court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 767.24(4)(a) had been construed to say that while the family court had to provide placement to be regularly recurring and meaningful, this was not tantamount to a presumption of equal placement. The father also argued that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated due process and equal protection. The father claimed that the physical placement statutes violated due process because they deprived him of a fundamental liberty interest in equally participating in the raising of his children. The appellate court ruled that the father failed to satisfy his heavy burden to show why the State of Wisconsin should be foreclosed from allowing its courts to set placement schedules commensurate with the best interests of the children even if it meant less than equal placement; while parents did have a natural right to the care and custody of their children, this did not mean that parents had a fundamental right to equal placement periods after divorce.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Lofthus v. Lofthus


Appeal No. 03-1754


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 65; 270 Wis. 2d 515; 678 N.W.2d 393; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 97


January 6, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
February 3, 2004, Decided  
February 3, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review dismissed by Lofthus v. Lofthus, 2004 WI 50, 271 Wis. 2d 113, 679 N.W.2d 547, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 393 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Chippewa County: FREDERICK A. HENDERSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 95-FA-000205.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court for Chippewa County, Wisconsin, which appointed a guardian ad litem, denied the father's motion for modification of a physical placement order, and required him to pay the full amount of the guardian ad litem's fees, rather than dividing them between the father and respondent mother. The father challenged the constitutionality of the placement and guardian ad litem statutes.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that anything less than equal placement unfairly burdened his constitutional right to the care and custody of his children. The court disagreed, finding that, although the right to custody and care undeniably warranted deference, the State had a countervailing interest in supervising divorced families because of the unique problems that existed in a home that was split by divorce. Wis. Stat. § 767.325(1)(b)1 also did not require modification of the unequal placement. Adopting the guardian ad litem's report that the children were adjusted under the current arrangement, the trial court implicitly ruled that a change would not be in their best interests. Further, the father did not overcome the presumption for maintaining the status quo, because none of the facts he relied on constituted a substantial change. Those facts included the natural aging process of the children, the father's move 16 miles closer to the mother, his being able to transport the children to school, his new marriage and new child, and the passage of Wis. Stat. § 767.24(4)(a)2, which did not, as he argued, mandate equal time. Ordering the father to pay the entire guardian ad litem fee was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Schulpius (In re Schulpius)


Appeal No. 02-1056


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2004 WI App 39; 270 Wis. 2d 427; 678 N.W.2d 369; 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 90


January 6, 2004, Oral Argument  
February 3, 2004, Decided  
February 3, 2004, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Schulpius, 2004 WI 50, 271 Wis. 2d 108, 679 N.W.2d 544, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 251 (2004)
Affirmed by State v. Schulpius (In re Schulpius), 2006 WI 1, 2006 Wisc. LEXIS 1 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN J. DiMOTTO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 95CF954690.
State v. Schulpius, 2003 WI 126, 265 Wis. 2d 421, 668 N.W.2d 560, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 779 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sex offender appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to enforce the trial court's previous order directing that he be released from the custody to which he was committed as a "sexually violent person" under Wis. Stat. ch. 980.


OVERVIEW: The offender sexually assaulted a four-year-old boy for whom he was babysitting. The offender had previously molested several siblings and neighbors. The trial court directed the Department of Health and Family Services and the county to prepare a plan to treat the offender on supervised release in the community. When, after several years, the offender was still being detained in secure custody, the trial court ruled that the offender's constitutional rights were violated and ordered his immediate release. Subsequently, however, the trial court found that the offender was no longer suitable for supervised release because of his dangerous mental condition. The court held that, given the offender's horrendous history of predatory sexual violence against children, the good-faith inability of the responsible persons to comply with the trial court's orders neither shocked the conscience nor trespassed on rights implicit in concepts of ordered liberty. Accordingly, the offender had not shown, by any standard, that he was deprived of substantive due process by the application of Wis. Stat. ch. 980 to him. Moreover, all of ch. 980's procedural safeguards were scrupulously applied to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Dane County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Ponn P. (In re Diana P.)

January 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Dane County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Ponn P., 2004 WI 50, 271 Wis. 2d 108, 679 N.W.2d 544, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 255 (2004)
Affirmed by Dane County Dep't of Human Services v. P.P. (In re Diana P.), 2005 WI 32, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 142 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 02TP000107, 02TP000108, 02TP000109, 02TP000110, 02TP000111, 02TP000112, 02TP000113.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, father, challenged the orders of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, terminating his parental rights to his seven children pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415 (2001-2002).


OVERVIEW: The State petitioned to terminate the father's parental rights pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(1), (2), and (6), and later amended its petition to allege that grounds for termination existed under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2) and (4). The father entered a no contest plea and waiver to the termination petition. The father argued that the circuit court was without jurisdiction to terminate his parental rights, because Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) was a facially unconstitutional statute, as it permitted the State to sidestep its duty to prove parental unfitness. The appellate court ruled that the issue was whether Wis. Stat. § 48.424(4), read in conjunction with Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4), was narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest. The appellate court ruled that the father failed to satisfy his burden of showing that the statutory scheme was unconstitutional. The statutory scheme reflected a Wisconsin Legislative determination that satisfaction of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(4) constituted a sufficient showing of unfitness. The father failed to address whether the Legislative determination was sufficiently narrowly tailored to meet constitutional standards.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

State v. Jackson


Appeal No. 03-2291-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2004 WI App 21; 269 Wis. 2d 544; 674 N.W.2d 681; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1200



December 23, 2003, Decided  
December 23, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLANT PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rusk County: FREDERICK A. HENDERSON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CF000107.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Rusk County, Wisconsin, for her part in being a party to the crime of entry into a locked coin box, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 943.125(1) and 939.05 (2001-02), and was sentenced accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial indicated that defendant acted as a lookout while her co-defendant pried a soap vending machine from a wall, attempted to pry open a vending machine, and attempted to remove coins from a commercial washing machine. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court's instructions to the jury erroneously contained a mandatory conclusive presumption and that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction. The appellate court noted that a jury instruction directing a jury to accept as true a judicially noticed fact that constituted an element of the crime was indistinguishable from a mandatory conclusive presumption on an elemental fact, which was unconstitutional; however, that type of constitutional instructional error was subject to the harmless error rule. The appellate court held that the trial court's jury instruction was harmless error, in that it was clear beyond a reasonable doubt that a rational jury would have found defendant guilty absent the error. The appellate court concluded that, by breaking into the coin mechanic component of the commercial washing machine, defendant and her accomplice unlawfully entered a locked coin box.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Arredondo


02-2361-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2004 WI App 7; 269 Wis. 2d 369; 674 N.W.2d 647; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1212


November 4, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
December 23, 2003, Decided  
December 23, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Arredondo, 2004 WI 20, 269 Wis. 2d 199, 675 N.W.2d 805, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 72 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Arredondo v. Pollard, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 38504 (E.D. Wis., May 25, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) of first-degree intentional homicide and second-degree sexual assault. The court denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he did not knowingly and voluntarily waive his right to testify. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court stated that defendant was fully advised of his rights in that regard both by it and by his counsel. He was advised of the same rights in a prior trial. He represented in the prior trial a full understanding of his rights to testify or not to testify in that matter. His attorney represented on the record in that matter that he fully understood his rights and options in that regard, and I am fully satisfied that defendant understands what the situation was and made an informed, knowing and voluntary decision. At the Machner hearing, counsel testified that defendant never told him before the defense rested that he wanted to testify. In contrast, defendant claimed that he told his counsel that he had to testify to prove his innocence. The trial court adopted the State's proposed finding that defendant told his attorney after the defense witnesses had testified that he still did not want to testify. Therefore, the evidence showed that defendant knowingly and voluntarily waived his right to testify.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Barbara B. v. Dorian H. (In re John R. B.)


Appeal No. 03-1877


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2004 WI App 21; 269 Wis. 2d 543; 674 N.W.2d 681; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1140



December 10, 2003, Decided  
December 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLANT PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 10, 2003.
Review granted by Barbara B. v. Dorian H., 2004 WI 20, 675 N.W.2d 804, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 41 (2004)
Affirmed by Barbara B. v. Dorian H.(In re John R. B.), 2005 WI 6, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 5 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: BARBARA A. KLUKA, JAMES E. FITZGERALD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 80PA001109.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) requiring him to pay child support arrearages in the amount of $ 24,690 and interest of $ 42,612. The trial court determined that he was not entitled to assert equitable estoppel against petitioner mother and that he was not entitled to credit for any sums paid to her outside of the terms of the judgment for child support issued by the court in 1982.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the retroactive application of Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1r) (2001-02) was unconstitutional. He conceded the mother's action was filed in April 2001, long after his ability to use equitable estoppel came to an end in 1993 when the legislature amended § 767.32(1m) to add language providing that the courts could not revise "an amount of arrearages in child support that has accrued, prior to the date that notice of the action is given to the respondent." 1993 Wis. Laws 481, § 118. However, the father argued that the change in the law came after he relied upon the mother's agreement that he would pay private school tuition for the child until graduation in lieu of paying child support. The instant court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1r) (2001-02) properly balanced the public interest in requiring parents to provide for the financial support of their children and the need to monitor the fulfillment of that obligation against the ability of the parties to make alternate or "off the record" agreements. Compliance with § 767.32(1r) was within the control of the father. The instant court rejected the constitutional challenge to the statute's retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The trial court order was affirmed.

Wood County v. Swank


Appeal No. 02-3347


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2004 WI App 1; 268 Wis. 2d 844; 673 N.W.2d 411; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1111



November 26, 2003, Decided  
November 26, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Wood County: JAMES M. MASON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-SC-62.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an owner of a holding tank for sewage, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Wood County, Wisconsin, which ordered a civil forfeiture of $ 500 plus costs pursuant to Wood County, Wis., Private Sewage System Ord. (PSSO) 702.09(2) after the owner failed to pay plaintiff county an annual reporting service fee under PSSO 702.04(4)A.3.d.


OVERVIEW: PSSO 702.04(4)A.3.d required tank owners to pay an annual reporting service fee of $ 36, the amount that was required per tank by the county's contract with a company that designed, installed, and maintained an alarm system to report the conditions of holding tanks. In affirming the forfeiture, the court held that: (1) Wis. Stat. § 145.20(4) authorized the county to assess tank owners for costs relating to the pumping of a holding tank; (2) the $ 36 was a fee, not a special assessment or tax because the amount charged was the cost of maintaining the reporting system and thus recovered costs rather than raising revenue; the fee did not serve the general benefit of the public but rather held tank owners responsible for the costs of recordkeeping related to monitoring tanks; (3) the ordinance did not violate equal protection, but appropriately charged only tank owners for the cost of services; (4) the county could contract with a private business for recordkeeping services, and the contract did not unlawfully bargain away the county's police power; and (5) the permit fee and recordkeeping fees were separate charges and were not redundant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of forfeiture.

County of Fond Du Lac v. Derksen


Appeal No. 03-1314


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2004 WI App 1; 268 Wis. 2d 846; 673 N.W.2d 412; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1117



November 26, 2003, Decided  
November 26, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: RICHARD J. NUSS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 03FO000178.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of underage consumption of alcohol, in violation of Fond du Lac County, Wis., Ordinances § 6-1 (adopting Wis. Stat. § 125.07(4)(b) (2001-02)), in the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County, Wisconsin. Defendant appealed, asserting that the trial court lacked jurisdiction over him because the violation of the underage drinking ordinance was a civil action and required a summons and complaint for proper service of process.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that a summons and complaint was required for proper service. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 800.01(1)(a) (2001-02), proper service occurred in cases involving a violation of a municipal ordinance when a citation was issued. Because defendant's underage consumption of alcohol was a violation of a municipal ordinance, a citation was proper service of process, and the trial court had jurisdiction. The appellate court also held that Fond du Lac County, Wis., Ordinances § 6-1 (adopting Wis. Stat. § 125.07(4)(b) (2001-02)), which regulated the consumption of alcoholic beverages by underaged persons was constitutional. The State had broad power to regulate the liquor industry and underage drinking. Such regulation served the purpose of protecting the safety of persons who might be injured as a result of the intoxication of underage persons, as well as for the health and morals of the underage persons themselves. Fond du Lac County derived its authority to pass municipal ordinances relating to underage drinking from Wis. Stat. ch. 125 (2001-02). Therefore, Fond du Lac County possessed the authority to regulate underage consumption of alcohol.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.
