State v. Barr


Appeal No. 03-1525-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2004 WI App 1; 268 Wis. 2d 846; 673 N.W.2d 412; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1066



November 18, 2003, Decided  
November 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for St. Croix County: EDWARD F. VLACK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CT-107.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin) of operating while intoxicated (OWI). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because even if the initial search in the home was valid, the officer had no probable cause to arrest him. The court of appeals disagreed. The officer had a rough description of the hit-and-run driver and vehicle, and he had confirmation of the vehicle's registered owner's name and address. When the officer arrived at the address, he found defendant, who matched the suspect's physical description. When the officer advised defendant that he wanted to discuss an accident, defendant asked whether anyone was hurt as opposed to denying any involvement in an accident. Defendant did not suggest someone else had used his vehicle that evening. The officer noticed that defendant seemed intoxicated, another factor about the driver that had been reported. Taken as a whole, the officer made a logical conclusion based on his knowledge at the time of the arrest. Therefore, the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Chvala


Appeal No. 03-0746-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 257; 268 Wis. 2d 451; 673 N.W.2d 401; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1058


October 29, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
November 13, 2003, Decided  
November 13, 2003, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CF002451.
State v. Chvala, 2003 WI 91, 262 Wis. 2d 504, 665 N.W.2d 378, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 595 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The criminal complaint in this action charged defendant, a senator in the Wisconsin Legislature, with extortion, misconduct in public office, and violations of campaign finance statutes. The issue on appeal was whether, as defendant argued, Wis. Stat. § 757.13 (2001-02) prohibited the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) from scheduling the trial before the last general business floor session ended on March 11, 2004.


OVERVIEW: The instant court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 757.13 (2001-02) violated the doctrine of separation of powers if it was construed to mandate that the trial court grant defendant's request that the trial not be scheduled until after March 11, 2004. The instant court construed the statute to direct courts to consider, in the sound exercise of their discretion, that a witness, party, or party's attorney was a member of the legislature in session when such persons requested a continuance or adjournment for that reason. The trial court correctly construed § 757.13 in denying defendant's request that the trial be scheduled after March 11, 2004.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's request for a continuance until after March 11, 2004 was affirmed.

State v. Kuechler


Appeal No. 02-1205-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 245; 268 Wis. 2d 192; 673 N.W.2d 335; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1004


August 22, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
October 29, 2003, Decided  
October 29, 2003, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Washington County: ANNETTE K. ZIEGLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CF-43.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Washington County, Wisconsin, which convicted him of seventh offense operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) (2001-02), and denied him motion for postconviction relief. Defendant argued that the sentencing court erroneously imposed a fine according to a local sentencing guideline and failed to consider his ability to pay the fine.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that a maximum term of confinement was not required but a maximum "overall sentence" was necessary and therefore imposed a fine, making reference to local guidelines. The court reversed as to the trial court's failure to make a determination as to defendant's ability to pay the fine, an issue that defendant timely raised in his postconviction motion. A hearing was necessary to avoid an unconstitutional application of the statutes. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment, finding that although local sentencing guidelines were only applicable to prohibited alcohol concentration offenses, it was not error, and therefore not unconstitutional, to make reference to local guidelines when sentencing for an OWI offense. There was also no requirement that the trial court give separate reasons for imposing jail time than it gave for imposing a fine. It was a proper exercise of discretion to highlight aggravating factors rather than mitigating factors where the trial court specifically characterized the case as "aggravated" and identified the factors that led it to that characterization.


OUTCOME: The court reversed as to the failure to determine defendant's ability to pay the fine and remanded the cause with directions. The court otherwise affirmed the decision.

State v. Faust


Appeal No. 03-0952-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 243; 267 Wis. 2d 783; 672 N.W.2d 97; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 927


June 16, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
October 1, 2003, Decided  
October 1, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Faust, 2004 WI 1, 268 Wis. 2d 133, 673 N.W.2d 691, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 1049 (2003)
Reversed by State v. Faust, 2004 WI 99, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 474 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: GARY LANGHOFF, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02CT000145.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated. Defendant moved to suppress the blood test results, arguing that since the breath test had already proved that his blood alcohol was over the legal limit, there was no longer any exigency justifying a blood draw without a warrant. The Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin) granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant took a breath test for the presence of alcohol, the police requested a blood test and defendant refused to consent. The blood test was performed forcibly and without a warrant. There was no evidence that the police were concerned about the breath test being in any way unsatisfactory or unusable and the officer testified that he did not request the blood test for the purpose of detecting the presence of controlled substances. The suppression of the evidence of the blood test was affirmed because once an individual who was arrested on probable cause for operating a vehicle while intoxicated provided a satisfactory and useable chemical test, the exigent circumstances justifying a warrantless and nonconsensual blood draw no longer existed.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

Appeal Nos. 02-1035, 02-1880


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE

September 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at City of Milwaukee Post 2874 v. Redevelopment Auth. of Milwaukee, 2006 WI App 56, 290 Wis. 2d 510, 712 N.W.2d 86, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 138 (2006)
Subsequent appeal at, Cause remanded by City of Milwaukee Post No. 2874 VFW of the United States v. Redevelopment Auth. of Milwaukee, 2008 Wisc. App. LEXIS 53 (Wis. Ct. App., Jan. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MAXINE A. WHITE, Judge. Dismissed. APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL P. SULLIVAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 01 CV 8011, Cir. Ct. No. 02 CV 1711.
City of Milwaukee Post # 2874 v. Redevelopment Auth. of Milwaukee, 2002 WI App 85, 252 Wis. 2d 768, 642 N.W.2d 646, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 198 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, appellant veterans post (VFW) challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that granted a writ of assistance to appellee City redevelopment authority to evict VFW from its leased property and from the non-final order directing the county condemnation commission panel to apply the "unit rule" to determine "fair market value," under Wis. Stat. § 32.09(5)(a) (2001-02), of the VFW's property.


OVERVIEW: The appellate question was whether, under § 32.09(5)(a), the City had to pay the VFW anything more than the "fair market value" of the property as determined under the "unit rule"? The Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One, concluded that the case law, including the appellate court's recent decision in Dotty, yielded an equally clear answer: No. The VFW argued that if the appellate court affirmed the circuit court's order requiring application of the "unit rule," it would have been barred from presenting evidence regarding the value of its lease and it would receive nothing as compensation for the termination of its lease. It was undisputed that, at the point that condemnation effectively terminated VFW's lease, 60 years remained and the lease value, without any adjustment for inflation, exceeded eight million dollars. The City responded, however, that the value of VFW's lease was not a proper component in the determination of the property's "fair market value." Notwithstanding the court's considerable sympathy for the VFW, it saw no basis on which to distinguish the instant case from Dotty and, therefore, had no authority to grant VFW its requested relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and the case was remanded.

Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus. Am., Inc.


Appeal Nos. 01-0724, 01-1031, 01-2486


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 202; 267 Wis. 2d 638; 673 N.W.2d 303; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 908; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P16,753


July 1, 2003, Oral Argument  
September 30, 2003, Decided  
September 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Ind. Am., 2004 WI 50, 271 Wis. 2d 108, 679 N.W.2d 544, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 250 (2004)
Reversed by, Cause remanded by Wischer v. Mitsubishi Heavy Indus. Am., Inc., 2005 WI 26, 2005 Wisc. LEXIS 137 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from judgments and orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DOMINIC S. AMATO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99 CV 6553.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee wives of decedent iron workers brought a negligence action against a crane manufacturer and a general contractor, and sought compensatory and punitive damages. The jury awarded $ 5,250,000 in compensatory damages and $ 94,000,000 in punitive damages. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) denied the contractor's post-verdict motions. The contractor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The construction workers were killed when a crane, leased by the contractor, collapsed and they fell to their deaths. The dispositive issue was, whether, based on the facts as conceded by the wives, the punitive-damage award was contrary to the calls of Wis. Stat. § 895.85(3) (1999-2000). The Court of Appeal of Wisconsin, District One, held that it was. The appellate court held that the phrase "intentional disregard of the rights of the plaintiff" in § 895.85(3) could only have been reasonably interpreted to have required either an intent by a defendant to cause injury to the plaintiffs or knowledge that the defendant's conduct was practically certain to cause the accident or injury to the plaintiffs. Based on that conclusion, together with the concession by both the wives and the trial court that there was no evidence demonstrating that the contractor intended to cause injury or knew that its conduct was practically certain to cause injury, the award of punitive damages was reversed. Based on the foregoing, the trial court's interpretation of the statute was erroneous. Having reached that conclusion, the trial court also erred in submitting the punitive damages issue to the jury.


OUTCOME: The trial court's punitive damage award was reversed.

 

951 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


United States Bank Nat'l Ass'n v. City of Milwaukee


Appeal No. 03-0724


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 220; 267 Wis. 2d 718; 672 N.W.2d 492; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 930


September 2, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
September 30, 2003, Decided  
September 30, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  
Review denied by U.S. Bank Nat'l v. City of Milwaukee, 2004 WI 1, 268 Wis. 2d 135, 673 N.W.2d 693, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 1137 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 02CV007447, 02CV007448, 02CV007449, 02CV007450, 02CV007451, 02CV007452, 02CV007453, 02CV007454, 02CV007455, 02CV007456, 02CV007457, 02CV007458, 02CV007459, 02CV007460, 02CV007461, 02CV007462, 02CV007463, 02CV007464, 02CV007465, 02CV007466, 02CV007467.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; motions denied and causes remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, 14 City of Milwaukee property-taxpayers, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that dismissed their actions brought under Wis. Stat. § 74.37 against appellee City for property-tax refunds. The trial court granted the City's motion to dismiss the consolidated cases and held that Wis. Stat. § 74.37 could not be used to challenge tax assessments on property in the City of Milwaukee.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that despite Nankin, § 74.37 could not be used to challenge tax assessments on property in the City of Milwaukee. Before Nankin, § 74.37 could only be used to challenge tax assessments on property located outside of Milwaukee County. Nankin declared that restriction unconstitutional. Nankin declared that § 74.37(6) violated the rights of Milwaukee County taxpayers to equal protection of the law guaranteed by Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. But the remainder of § 74.37, remained fully operative. The appellate court held that it would have defeated the intent of the legislature to apply provisions that were once, but no longer were, consistent with Wis. Stat. § 74.37, to deprive County property-taxpayers the use of § 74.37 merely because those taxpayers sought to contest their City of Milwaukee tax assessments. There was no indication that the specific January 31 deadline was essential to any legislative purpose in connection with claims brought by Milwaukee County taxpayers and the Court of Appeals of Wisconsin, District One, saw no reason why the "3rd Monday in May" deadline could not be applied to taxpayers using § 74.37 to challenge their property assessments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The motions were denied and the causes remanded.

City of Madison v. Crossfield


Appeal No. 02-3252


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 225; 267 Wis. 2d 961; 671 N.W.2d 717; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 907



September 25, 2003, Decided  
September 25, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Madison v. Crossfield, 2004 WI 20, 269 Wis. 2d 199, 675 N.W.2d 805, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 97 (2004)
Related proceeding at City of Madison v. Crossfield, 2004 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1028 (Wis. Ct. App., Dec. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: DAVID T. FLANAGAN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CV-792.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a municipal court trial, defendant was found guilty of parking a truck on a residential lot, in violation of Madison, WI, General Ord. § 28.11(3)(a)1, which limited parking to passenger vehicles with less that a one-ton capacity. Defendant filed a timely appeal to the Dane County Circuit Court, Wisconsin, opting for a de novo bench trial. The circuit court upheld the decision, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, because the terms "passenger truck," "capacity," and "ton" were not defined by the ordinance, Wis. Stat. § 349.03(1) required courts to defer to statutory definitions. The court disagreed, reasoning that the ordinance was a zoning regulation, not a traffic regulation within § 349.03(1). Further, the regulation was expressly authorized by "some other provision of the statutes," as allowed by § 349.03(1)(b), specifically the statutory authority to enact zoning regulations. The court also held that defendant did not have standing to challenge the regulation on the basis that it was unconstitutionally vague. The court reasoned that the truck had a "capacity" of over three tons and that therefore defendant's conduct was clearly proscribed. In arriving at that conclusion, the court used the value specified by the manufacturer rather than post-manufacture, "modified loaded weight," as argued by defendant, to determine the truck's capacity. The statute of limitations was not a bar. Although defendant had been parking his truck in the lot for 10 years, the statute did not run from the first day of a continuing violation, but from the day the violation ceased.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

State v. Doudna


Appeal No. 03-1080-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 225; 267 Wis. 2d 962; 671 N.W.2d 718; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 874



September 18, 2003, Decided  
September 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sauk County: PATRICK TAGGART, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01CT000120.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin) which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, second offense, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: At the time of defendant's first offense the statute imposed additional penalties for a second offense within five years. When defendant committed the current offense, the statute imposed additional penalties for a second offense within 10 years. Defendant's conviction was affirmed because applying the 10 year statute did not violate defendant's substantive due process rights in that he did not have a liberty interest under the five year statute, he failed to overcome the presumption of constitutionality, there was a public interest in deterring persons from driving while intoxicated, and defendant was on notice of the change in the law before he committed the current offense; (2) the 10 year statute was not an ex post facto law in that it merely increased the penalty for the current offense and defendant had fair warning of the change in the law; (3) the 10 year statute did not violate equal protection in that it was rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest; and (4) the 10 year statute did not subject defendant to multiple punishments in violation of double jeopardy in that it merely stiffened the penalty for the current offense.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Brienzo


Appeal No. 01-1362-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 203; 267 Wis. 2d 349; 671 N.W.2d 700; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 853


June 24, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
September 10, 2003, Decided  
September 10, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Brienzo, 2004 WI 1, 268 Wis. 2d 133, 673 N.W.2d 691, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 1054 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: WAYNE J. MARIK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CF-43.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a charge against defendant for child enticement in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.07 (2001-02). Defendant cross-appealed from the order that denied his motion to dismiss the charge of attempted sexual assault, Wis. Stat. §§ 948.02(2), 939.50(3)(6c), and 939.32 (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: The case arose from a prosecution for child enticement and attempted sexual assault resulting from an ongoing Internet sting operation. The State appealed from an order dismissing the charge against defendant for child enticement and defendant cross-appealed from the order, which denied his motion to dismiss the charge of attempted sexual assault. The court reversed in part, stating that Wis. Stat. § 948.07 (2001-02) did not violate defendant's First amendment rights. While the agent posing as a minor conducted much of the discussions regarding the putative sexual activity, defendant's appearance at the prearranged site signaled probable cause to believe that he had the intent to proceeding with the criminal sexual activity discussed between the two. The complaint charging attempted child enticement alleged sufficient facts to establish probable cause that defendant attempted to entice a child. On remand, the circuit court was ordered to reinstate the charge of attempted child enticement. Arranging a time and place were acts in furtherance of defendant's criminal objective; thus, there was probable cause that defendant attempted to sexually assault a child under the age of 16.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part and ordered the circuit court, on remand, to reinstate the charge of attempted child enticement; the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of attempted sexual assault was affirmed.

Raz v. Brown


Appeal No. 01-2436


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2003 WI App 225; 267 Wis. 2d 960; 671 N.W.2d 717; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 842



September 3, 2003, Decided  
September 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: CROSS-APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL GUOLEE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 90FA903638.
Raz v. Brown, 2003 WI 29, 260 Wis. 2d 614, 660 N.W.2d 647, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 211 (2003).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross-appellant father sought review of decisions by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, which denied his motion challenging the constitutionality of Wisconsin child-support guidelines under the Due-Process and Equal-Protection clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. He also challenged the denial of his motion for retroactive modification of a child-support order.


OVERVIEW: The father claimed that the physical-placement statutes violated the Due-Process Clause because they deprived him of a fundamental liberty interest of equally participating in the raising of his children. Although noting that parents had a fundamental right to the care and custody of their children, the court held that this did not mean that parents had a fundamental right to equal placement periods after a divorce. Therefore, the father's right to substantive due process was not violated. He also failed to show that the procedures were constitutionally inadequate. He had an opportunity to be heard at a meaningful time in a meaningful manner, participating in nine hearings over the course of three years. Under the Equal Protection Clause, the father did not show how or where the physical-placement statutes created an impermissible classification when he argued that fathers as a group prevailed in only about 10 percent of cases. The court also held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by not applying administrative changes to existing child-support guidelines that had not yet been adopted. Neither parent was entitled to costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Klatt v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n


Appeal No. 02-3218


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 197; 266 Wis. 2d 1038; 669 N.W.2d 752; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 750


June 17, 2003, Oral Argument  
August 13, 2003, Decided  
August 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Klatt v. Labor & Indus. Review Comm'n, 2003 WI 140, 266 Wis. 2d 65, 671 N.W.2d 851, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 946 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: J. MAC DAVIS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CV-892.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of defendant Labor and Industry Review Commission (LIRC) of the Department of Industry, Labor and Human Relations that denied unemployment compensation after defendant city challenged an appeal tribunal decision ruling that the employee had terminated her employment with good cause under Wis. Stat. § 108.04(7)(b) (2001-02).


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the city's police department, which had a residency requirement in its collective bargaining agreement. After becoming engaged to a sheriff's department investigator in another county that also had a residency requirement, the employee sought an exemption from her department's residency requirement so that she could live with her husband. After multiple unsuccessful attempts at obtaining an exemption, the employee moved, in violation of the residency requirement. She was terminated and initially found ineligible for unemployment compensation as having terminated her employment within the meaning of § 108.04(7)(a). The employee appealed from a final decision holding that she had voluntarily terminated her employment without good cause attributable to the city. Applying a deferential standard of review, the court held that the employee's act of moving in violation of the residency requirement was inconsistent with the continuation of the employer-employee relationship and she therefore voluntarily terminated her employment. Further, despite her unfortunate situation, the employee failed to demonstrate that she had good cause to terminate her employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed LIRC's decision.

State v. Hulbert


Appeal No. 02-3202-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 201; 267 Wis. 2d 278; 670 N.W.2d 558; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 722



August 5, 2003, Decided  
August 5, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

 [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Florence County: ROBERT A. KENNEDY, JR., Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CM-122.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possessing marijuana, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 961.41(3g)(b). Earlier, the Florence County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) denied his pretrial motion challenging the validity of a search warrant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A search warrant had been issued for the house where defendant was staying as a guest. Drugs were found in the bedroom where defendant was staying. The warrant had been issued on the basis of an officer's affidavit, which claimed an anonymous tip informed the officer that drugs were going to be delivered to the house. Specifically, defendant argued that the anticipatory search warrant lacked sufficient probable cause and failed to set forth the conditions precedent for the warrant's execution. The appellate court ruled that anticipatory search warrants were constitutional and did not need to explicitly state the conditions precedent for the warrant's execution. Here, the affidavit named the driver of a dark colored conversion van with lots of windows, which was to deliver the marijuana to the house for a large birthday party, which a record check indicated would be on a specific date. The information was sufficient for the magistrate to have found that the drugs would be present at the house on the day of the birthday.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dismuke


Appeal No. 02-2164-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2003 WI App 201; 267 Wis. 2d 277; 670 N.W.2d 557; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 728



August 5, 2003, Decided  
August 5, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

 [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Dismuke, 2003 WI 140, 266 Wis. 2d 63, 671 N.W.2d 850, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 890 (2003)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay granted by Dismuke v. McCaughtry, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 88090 (E.D. Wis., Dec. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN and MARTIN J. DONALD, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 00CF5186.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered no contest pleas to homicide by use of a vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration and injury by intoxicated use of a vehicle with a blood alcohol concentration of 0.1 percent or more, in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin. Defendant's postconviction motion was denied. He appealed, asserting his sentencing was unconstitutional and that his statements were obtained in violation of his constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: A police officer saw defendant's car collide with the victims' car. The officer saw defendant get out of his car and run away from the accident scene. After being apprehended, but before being either questioned or advised of his Miranda rights, the officer claimed that defendant blurted out, "I knew you were going to come after me, so I tried to get away." Defendant was taken to a nearby hospital and read his Miranda rights. Defendant then admitted to being the driver of the car. Later, he was again advised of his Miranda rights, after which he gave the police a more extensive statement admitting his involvement in the accident. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the subject statements were inadmissible. The first statement was voluntary, despite the fact that defendant was in custody and not advised of his constitutional rights. The abbreviated statement at the hospital was voluntary and admissible, as defendant's argument he could not recall being Mirandized was not credible. As to his third statement, defendant never invoked his right to silence. Finally, the truth-in-sentencing law that called for determinate sentences was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

State ex rel. Widmer-Baum v. Litscher


Appeal No. 02-0449


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 188; 266 Wis. 2d 1059; 668 N.W.2d 562; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 712



July 31, 2003, Decided  
July 31, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CV-2106.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee department of corrections denied appellant inmate's petition for declaratory judgment against appellee department officials challenging a proposed department rule change. Later, the inmate filed a petition for writ of certiorari and declaratory ruling challenging the rule change and sought review of a disciplinary action against him. The Circuit Court of Dane County, Wisconsin, dismissed the inmate's petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the inmate contended the trial court erred in dismissing his petition. Contrary to the department's contention, the appellate court found that the department's denial of the inmate's request for declaratory judgment ruling did not prevent him from seeking a declaratory ruling in the trial court with respect to the challenged rule. However, the department was not obligated to issue a declaratory judgment ruling regarding the validity of the rule under Wis. Stat. § 227.41(1) (2001-02), as the inmate was not seeking a ruling with respect to the applicability of the rule to him, but, rather, on the constitutionality of the rule. As the inmate's substantial interests were not adversely affected by the department's action, the inmate was required to comply with Wis. Stat. § 227.40(1) (2001-02) in order to receive judicial review of the proposed rule. Because the inmate's summons and complaint were not filed together, he failed to initiate a civil action for declaratory judgment with the trial court and, therefore, the trial court lacked competency to hear his complaint. The inmate's parole from prison rendered his request for review of his disciplinary action moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State ex rel. Irby v. Litscher


Appeal Nos. 02-2368 02-2741


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 188; 266 Wis. 2d 1061; 668 N.W.2d 563; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 713



July 31, 2003, Decided  
July 31, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CV-1552.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner filed a complaint for writ of certiorari against defendant Secretary of the Wisconsin Department of Corrections, specifically on the issue of a legal opinion he loaned to another inmate, which was confiscated and destroyed by prison officials. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, dismissed the complaint and assessed a strike against the prisoner. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Another inmate borrowed the decision from the prisoner and attempted to return it by mail to the prisoner. That was when prison authorities confiscated and destroyed the decision. The prisoner asserted such action was vindictive and intended to, and did, interfere with his right to be represented by counsel of choice and his right to access to the courts. The department asserted the mailing of the opinion from the other inmate violated the rule against unauthorized transfers of property, pursuant to Wis. Admin. Code § DOC 303.40. The appellate court noted that § DOC 303.40 required prisoners to obtain prior authorization from prison officials before sending legal materials. Therefore, if the prisoner truly was providing legal services, he could have gotten prior authorization to send the document to the other inmate, and the other inmate could have done likewise before mailing it back. Because the prisoner's certiorari complaint did not allege that the other inmate obtained prior authorization before sending the decision back to him, he failed to state a claim that the departmental review decision was incorrect in concluding the transfer was unauthorized.


OUTCOME: The appellate court also held the circuit court properly assessed a "strike" against the prisoner, as the matter was dismissed for failure to state a claim. The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Lombard (In re Lombard)


Appeal No. 00-3318


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 163; 266 Wis. 2d 887; 669 N.W.2d 157; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 711


October 14, 2002, Submitted on Briefs; January 29, 2003, Oral Argument  
July 31, 2003, Decided  
July 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 27, 2003.
Review granted by State v. Lombard, 2003 WI 140, 266 Wis. 2d 59, 671 N.W.2d 847, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 812 (2003)
Affirmed by State v. Lombard (In re Lombard), 2004 WI 95, 684 N.W.2d 103, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 464 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Dane County: ROBERT A. DeCHAMBEAU, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CI-1.
State v. Lombard, 108 Wis. 2d 778, 324 N.W.2d 828, 1982 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3839 (Wis. Ct. App., 1982)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in 1981 of several counts of sexual assault. Prior to his mandatory release date, the State petitioned to have him committed as a sexually violent person. The State's allegations were tried to a jury, which returned a verdict finding him to be a sexually violent person. The Circuit Court for Dane County, Wisconsin, denied the committee's motions for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed error in the following respects: (1) the trial court's failure to give his requested instruction on "lack of volitional control;" (2) the unconstitutionality of 1999 Wis. Laws 9; (3) the trial court's instruction to the jury that sexually violent persons were eligible for supervised release; and (4) a violation of his Fifth Amendment rights stemming from the State's use at trial of statements he made during a pre-petition psychological evaluation. The appellate court held: (1) the trial court did not err in rejecting defendant's proffered instruction to add "volitional control" to the standard instruction, relevant to the issue of "a sexually violent person;" (2) the amendments to Wis. Stat. ch. 980, which removed the possibility for immediate supervised release of a sexually violent person, did not violate substantive due process or equal protection; (3) the trial court properly gave a curative instruction that a commitment under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 was "not" a commitment for life; and (4) the State could use, at a ch. 980 trial, any statements made by defendant to a pre-petition State examiner that could not subject defendant to future criminal prosecution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Henry


Appeal No. 01-2181-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2003 WI App 188; 266 Wis. 2d 1059; 668 N.W.2d 562; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 701



July 29, 2003, Decided  
July 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICIA D. McMAHON, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00 CF 4995.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, which convicted him for carrying a concealed weapon, following his guilty plea, and from the order denying his motion for postconviction relief. He argued that Wis. Stat. § 941.23 (1999-2000) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Police attempted to stop defendant's vehicle after an individual was seen displaying a handgun, and, when they arrested him, a .45 caliber semi-automatic pistol was found on the driver's seat of the vehicle. He argued that the concealed weapons statute, § 941.23, violated Wis. Const. art. I, § 25, which guaranteed the right to bear arms. In affirming the conviction, the court noted a recent Wisconsin Supreme Court case that found the statute to be a reasonable time, place, and manner restriction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

964 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


Sauk County v. Gumz


Appeal No. 02-0204


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 165; 266 Wis. 2d 758; 669 N.W.2d 509; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 692


February 27, 2003, Oral Argument  
July 24, 2003, Decided  
July 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 27, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Sauk County: DANIEL GEORGE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CV-214.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant event organizer appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin), which granted plaintiff county's request to enjoin the organizer's event from taking place due to the fact that no license had been obtained under the county's open-air assembly ordinance. The trial court held that Sauk County, Wis., Code of Ordinance § 12.01 et seq. was constitutional and dismissed the organizer's counterclaims.


OVERVIEW: The organizer intended to hold his event, which promoted legalization of hemp and marijuana, without first obtaining the necessary permit. The county obtained a temporary restraint. Thereafter, the trial court granted summary judgment to the county, holding the ordinance constitutional and permanently enjoining the event until such time as the permit was obtained. The trial court held that the ordinance satisfied the criteria for a constitutional time, place, and manner regulation, that it was content-neutral, and that, under the standards set out in Forsyth, it was constitutional. On appeal, the court thoroughly reviewed the provisions of the ordinance under a First Amendment analysis and determined that there were various provisions that were not narrowly tailored to serve a significant governmental interest. These included the time period for processing and filing the license, the prohibition on advertising and promotion of the event prior to obtaining the license, the zoning certification requirement, and the license fee above the flat rate of $ 100 per application. The processing time requirement could not be severed without causing an invalidation of the entire ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment dismissal of the organizer's counterclaim with respect to challenging the ordinance's constitutionality and ordered judgment in his favor, finding it unconstitutional. It reversed the order permanently enjoining him from holding his event without a license under the ordinance. The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the organizer's other counterclaims and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Schaefer


Appeal No. 01-2691-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 164; 266 Wis. 2d 719; 668 N.W.2d 760; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 693


January 28, 2003, Oral Argument  
July 24, 2003, Decided  
July 24, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 27, 2003.
Review denied by State v. Schaefer, 2003 WI 140, 266 Wis. 2d 61, 671 N.W.2d 848, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 846 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waushara County: LEWIS MURACH, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CF-6.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Waushara County (Wisconsin) of 18 counts of possession of child pornography. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the search warrant was not supported by probable cause. The court of appeals disagreed. The cut-up pictures found in defendant's trash established that he retained his interest in juvenile males as sex objects. Defendant had internet access and had visited an internet site where visual child pornography was available for downloading. The narratives he printed out explicitly described sexual encounters between adults and juvenile males. Defendant's computer was a significant tool in allowing him access to children, and to child pornography, and there existed ample probable cause justifying the search of defendant's computer files. Authorizing the seizure of every photograph of a child was reasonable when investigating the crime of child exploitation. Even lawful photographs could help to identify children with whom the accused had interacted, thereby aiding in the discovery of other victims. The affidavit and warrant were not defective. Reviewed in the context of a child pornography and sexual exploitation investigation, the items to be seized were described with sufficient particularity and provided adequate guidance for the executing officer.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

966 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. St. Croix County


Appeal No. 02-1645


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 173; 266 Wis. 2d 498; 668 N.W.2d 743; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 643


December 9, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
July 10, 2003, Decided  
July 10, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 27, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for St. Croix County: SCOTT R. NEEDHAM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CV-181.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county passed a zoning ordinance (the riverway ordinance) to regulate a portion of the Lower St. Croix River that lay within the County. The County then amended the riverway ordinance leaving a portion of the river without zoning adequate to meet appellee State's mandate. The State sued to nullify the amendment, and the Circuit Court for St. Croix County (Wisconsin) granted its motion for summary judgment. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The County contended that the State was prohibited from enacting statutes requiring ordinances controlling the portion of the St. Croix River that was federally administrated under the Wild and Scenic Rivers Act, 16 U.S.C.S. § 1271 et seq., because Congress preempted regulation in that zone and also because Congress did not specifically state that local governments could regulate in the federal zone. The State contended that federal administration did not encompass zoning regulation, that local and federal regulations could co-exist in the federal zone, so long as the local regulations did not conflict with the Act, and that there was no conflict in the instant matter. The appellate court agreed with the State and concluded the State retained the power to authorize zoning in the federal zone at issue. Furthermore, given the Act's stated areas of federal and state cooperation, the absence of any explicit or implicit statement of federal preemption and the cooperation evidenced in the master plan, the federal government had not preempted the regulation of the Lower St. Croix River in either the federal or the state zone. Wis. Stat. § 30.27 (2001-02) remained in full force and effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court nullifying the amendment to the County's riverway zoning because it was enacted in excess of the power granted to the County by the State was affirmed.

State v. Heaney


Appeal Nos. 03-0422-FT, 03-0423-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 188; 266 Wis. 2d 1063; 668 N.W.2d 564; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 624



July 2, 2003, Decided  
July 2, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: ROBERT J. KENNEDY, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 02TR002930, 02TR002946.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI). The sole issue on appeal was whether the trial court erred when it denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained subsequent to a traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: A trooper pulled defendant over for failing to change lanes while an emergency vehicle was parked on the side of the road, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.072. As a result of this stop, defendant was charged with OWI. In affirming, the court found that evidence in the record supported the factual findings. Although the trooper did not recall whether he waved his flashlight at the car, a ride-along officer testified that he did so. He also testified that the car passed within five feet of the squad car without moving over and that there was no traffic that would have prevented defendant from pulling into the opposite lane of traffic. Defendant and his passenger testified to contrary facts. Defendant argued that the trial court created a "third version" of the facts not found in the record in order to support its conclusions that there was probable cause for the traffic violation and that the stop did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. The court noted that a trier of fact could do just that, as long as the finding was supported by the record. The trial court simply heard the conflicting testimony and made a judgment based on credibility.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's denial of the motion to suppress and affirmed the judgment of conviction.

State v. Johnson


Appeal No. 02-2778-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2003 WI App 188; 266 Wis. 2d 1062; 668 N.W.2d 563; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 613

NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEAN W. DiMOTTO, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01 CF 6389.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to theft from a person as party to a crime, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.20(1)(a), 939.05 (2001-02). The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) imposed a sentence of 10 years of imprisonment, with 5 years' initial confinement and 5 years' probation, upon condition that defendant was not to enter a portion of the city. Defendant's motion for sentencing modification was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took part in a vicious attack on the victim, culminating in theft of the victim's automated teller machine card. As a condition of probation, the trial court ordered defendant not to enter a specified portion of the city where the crime occurred. Defendant's sentence was affirmed, as: (1) the condition imposed did not violate a constitutional right to travel, in that the condition was not overly broad, it was reasonably related to a legitimate protective purpose to give peace of mind to the community, and it was appropriate to provide a margin of territorial safety where victims could live in peace; and (2) given defendant's extensive criminal background and the viciousness of the crime, the sentence imposed was not unduly harsh or excessive, in that it did not exceed the maximum sentence.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Burr

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Burr, 2003 WI 140, 266 Wis. 2d 65, 671 N.W.2d 851, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 952 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Burr v. Bertrand, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 80805 (E.D. Wis., Oct. 31, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Burr, 2013 Wisc. App. LEXIS 628 (Wis. Ct. App., July 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Pepin County: DANE F. MOREY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CF-26.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment entered on a jury's verdict in the Circuit Court for Pepin County, Wisconsin, convicting him of first-degree intentional homicide, aggravated battery, and false imprisonment, all as a party to a crime. Defendant also appealed the denial of his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried for murder; his accomplices were given reduced sentence for their testimony against him. Defendant claimed that the trial judge was biased because he refused to recuse himself from defendant's postconviction motion and because he had made comments during trial that implied that the prosecutor's improper comments and objectionable actions did not matter. Defendant also claimed that the prosecutor committed misconduct, the trial court made several evidentiary rulings, and improperly instructed the jury. The appellate court held that a trial judge would generally oversee the postconviction motions, and that the judge's comments to defendant about allowing the prosecutor to argue the case without continual objections from defendant did not show judicial bias. The appellate court also held that the prosecutor's comments during closing, and the trial judge's rulings on evidence were not an abuse of discretion, and, at most, resulted in harmless error. Finally, the trial judge did not err in allowing the county coroner to testify that it was likely that more than one person committed the murder, as the coroner had specialized training in death investigation.


OUTCOME: The judgment and the order denying defendant's postconviction motion were affirmed.

Rasin v. County of Walworth


Appeal No. 02-2561


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 162; 266 Wis. 2d 693; 667 N.W.2d 377; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 534



June 4, 2003, Decided  
June 4, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Rasin v. Walworth County, 2004 WI 114, 273 Wis. 2d 655, 684 N.W.2d 136, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 519 (2004)
Subsequent appeal at Driehaus v. Walworth County, 2009 Wisc. App. LEXIS 234 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Walworth County. JOHN R. RACE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CV-839.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners filed a declaratory judgment challenging respondent county land management committee's decision to grant a variance to respondent, the landowners' neighbor. The Circuit Court of Walworth County, Wisconsin, affirmed the committee's decision and the landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The committee first granted the neighbor a conditional use permit to establish a planned residential development on his property on the condition that he obtain a variance to side yard setback requirements. The underlying action arose when the committee later granted the neighbor the variance. The trial court ruled that under applicable county zoning ordinances, a variance was unnecessary and thus affirmed the committee's granting of the conditional use permit, striking the variance requirement as surplusage. On review, the landowners contended, inter alia, that applicable county ordinances required a variance and that the committee lacked jurisdiction to grant the variance. The appellate court agreed, finding that the county board of adjustment had exclusive authority to grant variances. Further, even if the committee did have jurisdiction to grant the variance, the granting of the variance was unsupported by the evidence of record as the neighbor failed to establish "no reasonable use" of the property and, hence, did not establish unnecessary hardship in the absence of a variance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded with directions that the trial court enter an order reversing the committee's grant of a variance to the neighbor.

State v. Williams


Appeal No. 02-2359-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 134; 265 Wis. 2d 938; 664 N.W.2d 684; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 515



May 28, 2003, Decided  
May 28, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Barron County: EDWARD R. BRUNNER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CT-237.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin) of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by concluding that the arresting officer had a legal basis to approach her car under either the community caretaker analysis or, alternatively, had a reasonable suspicion to make an investigatory stop. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant's van was creating a potential traffic hazard while already stopped on the roadway when the officer activated his emergency lights and walked to the van to see what was wrong. Thus, the officer's action did not intrude on defendant's freedom to leave. Although the record was not clear as to why the officer activated the emergency lights, it was reasonable to infer that it was for safety reasons under the circumstances. The public interest in the officer checking on the driver parked on a roadway in the early morning hours outweighed the minimal intrusion involved. In addition, the officer observed the van at 2:04 a.m. weaving within its lane of travel numerous times and for several blocks. He then observed the van stop in the middle of its traffic lane for no apparent reason and remain stopped in the lane for approximately 45 seconds with the driver sitting in the van.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hoover


Appeal No. 02-1687-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 117; 265 Wis. 2d 607; 666 N.W.2d 74; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 518


March 26, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
May 28, 2003, Decided  
May 28, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 25, 2003.
Review denied by State v. Hoover, 2003 WI 126, 265 Wis. 2d 418, 668 N.W.2d 558, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 677 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: WILBUR W. WARREN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 98-CF-944.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) of first-degree intentional homicide, party to a crime and conspiracy to hide a corpse. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his constitutional right to confront and cross-examine witnesses testifying against him was violated by the trial court's rulings and trial counsel's deficient performance or confusion over what questioning was permissible. The court of appeals disagreed. Prior to the witness's testimony, the trial court held several discussions with defense counsel and the prosecutor concerning the appropriate scope of cross-examination. Defense counsel argued that he should have been able to question the witness about what counsel characterized as "the break" he received in sentencing as a result of his statement. The trial court did not prohibit questions concerning the terms of the plea agreement. Rather, it suggested that questions concerning the plea agreement would be appropriate. Defense counsel was able to and, in fact, did question the witness about his charges and whether he expected to get a benefit from testifying. However, eliciting information about the actual sentence imposed was not relevant to any incentives the prosecution gave him for testifying on behalf of the State. Therefore, defendant's right to confrontation was not violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Fecke


Appeal No. 02-1598-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 134; 265 Wis. 2d 938; 664 N.W.2d 683; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 470



May 8, 2003, Decided  
May 8, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOHN R. STORCK, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CF-86.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Dodge County of three counts of delivering illegal articles to an inmate, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 302.095(2) (2001-02). Defendant appealed the conviction and an order that denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict, that § 302.095(2) was unconstitutionally vague, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and his conviction should have been reversed in the interest of justice. The appellate court rejected defendant's claims. Inter alia, the court held that taking items out of the prison for an inmate, and particularly the transaction for which defendant was to have been paid $ 500, constituted providing a service for an inmate, in violation of the fraternization policy. The appellate court held that it was not necessary to rely on the separate work rule prohibition against delivering articles to an inmate in violation of § 302.095. A reasonable person reading the fraternization policy and the work rules would have understood that taking items out of the prison for inmates was prohibited by the work rules and would understand that receiving items from an inmate for that purpose was prohibited by § 302.095(2). Indeed, when confronted with evidence of his actions, defendant told the police that, inter alia, he "knew it was wrong" to take the items from the prison. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Willow v. City of Menomonie


Appeal No. 02-2959


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 134; 265 Wis. 2d 939; 664 N.W.2d 684; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 456



May 6, 2003, Decided  
May 6, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:

 [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dunn County: ROD W. SMELTZER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CV-116.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car dealer sought declaratory relief to prevent appellee developer from developing, for retail purposes, land he purchased in a city's industrial park. The Circuit Court for Dunn County (Wisconsin) determined that Wis. Stat. § 66.1101 (2001-02) did not apply and that the zoning classification permitted commercial retail use of the property. The court entered summary judgment dismissing the car dealer's claim. The car dealer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The car dealer argued that § 66.1101(3) prohibited the development, for other than industrial purposes, of the 6 acres the developer purchased. The appellate court held that § 66.1101(3) did not apply. The city purchased and developed the land without benefit of the financing mechanisms under § 66.1101. The land was not a site purchased for "industrial development" under § 66.1101. As a result, the limiting provisions of subsection (3) did not apply, and the section did not prohibit the developer's commercial retail development and use of the property. The land sales policy adopted by the city stated that the city purchased land to expand its economic base and attract business and industry to the area. The city could have rationally concluded that selling the 6 acres for more than half of what the total 73 acres cost the city and the construction of a new automobile dealership on the site would have benefitted the city and attracted other business and industry to the site. Because increasing the tax base and improving the economic climate were public purposes consistent with the sale of the land for retail development, the sale did not violate the public purpose doctrine.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Miller


Appeal No. 02-2681-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 111; 264 Wis. 2d 895; 664 N.W.2d 127; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 440



April 30, 2003, Decided  
April 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Miller, 2003 WI 140, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 913 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MARK GEMPELER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CT-532.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress his blood alcohol test in a driving while intoxicated case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress his blood alcohol test, as the method was unreasonable and he made a reasonable objection based on his religious beliefs. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant did not make a reasonable objection, not because his professed theology was unsound, but because he furnished absolutely no support for his claims of church membership or church doctrine. In addition, the officers informed him of what they were going to do before they did it, and he refused to cooperate. Later, halfway through the process, he offered to cooperate, if they would let him sit up. The trial court found that offer was "a whimsical change of mind" that was not credible under the facts and circumstances. Because the methods used to obtain the blood draw were reasonable under the circumstances, and defendant made no reasonable objection to the procedure, the judgment denying the motion to suppress the results of the blood sample analysis was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kaster


Appeal No. 02-2352-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 105; 264 Wis. 2d 751; 663 N.W.2d 390; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 409


March 24, 2003, Oral Argument  
April 22, 2003, Decided  
April 22, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 28, 2003.
Review denied by State v. Kaster, 2003 WI 126, 265 Wis. 2d 418, 668 N.W.2d 558, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 699 (2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Kaster, 2006 Wisc. App. LEXIS 263 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Brown County: MARK A. WARPINSKI, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CF-138.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, convicting him of two counts of sexual assault of a student by school staff and one count each of fourth-degree sexual assault and disorderly conduct and denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a high school boys' and girls' swim coach during the 1998-99 school year and was not a teacher, nor did he hold any other position at the school. Defendant was charged with several crimes stemming from allegations that he had sexual contact with four members of the girls' team. On appeal, defendant only challenged the conviction of sexual assault of a student stemming from the March 14, 1999, incident. Defendant argued the only way he could have been liable under Wis. Stat. § 948.095 (1997-1998) was if he was under contract on March 14, and the jury should have been so instructed. While defendant's coaching duties were done at the end of the boys' season on February 20, defendant had out-of-season contact with the school and his athletes. The appellate court ruled that the evidence was sufficient to allow the jury to conclude that defendant was providing services to the school or school board when he committed the alleged assault. The appropriate interpretation of the statute was to view an "employe" and persons "under contract" as examples of persons included within the group of people that provided services to a school or school board.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

Step Now Citizens Group v. Town of Utica Planning & Zoning Comm.


Appeal No. 02-2760


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 109; 264 Wis. 2d 662; 663 N.W.2d 833; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 394


February 26, 2003, Oral Argument  
April 16, 2003, Decided  
April 16, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 28, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Winnebago County: WILLIAM H. CARVER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02-CV-351.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, company and property owners, sought a rezoning of the owners' property for an ethanol plant. Appellant town and appellant county approved the change. Respondent citizens group filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to find the rezoning illegal. The Winnebago County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) found the rezoning was unconstitutional spot zoning, but dismissed the group's claim of invalidity and nuisance. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, appellants argued that the rezoning decisions did not constitute illegal spot zoning. The appellate court noted that because the parcel was granted privileges that were not granted to other land in the vicinity, this was spot zoning. However, the zoning was not illegal because the zoning would benefit the community and not just the interested partied. The town and county also considered the site plan, odor emissions, noise and traffic considerations, employment and tax base considerations, fire control considerations, water considerations and the general effects of zoning gradation for future objectives of planning. Thus, the court reinstated the town's and the county's zoning decisions. Appellees cross-appealed, arguing, inter alia, that the rezoning was null and void because the town failed to follow necessary notice requirements. The appellate court disagreed because the town complied with all state notice requirements but failed to comply with its local ordinance requirements. Failure to comply with the town's notice requirements, when all statutory notice requirements were met, did not defeat the purpose of the ordinance's notice provision.


OUTCOME: The rezoning was not illegal spot zoning, therefore, that portion of the judgment was reversed and remanded with directions to reinstate the town's and the county's rezoning decisions. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

State ex rel. Robinson v. Town of Bristol


Appeal No. 02-1427


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 97; 264 Wis. 2d 318; 667 N.W.2d 14; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 375


December 9, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
April 10, 2003, Decided  
April 10, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 28, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CV-1478.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) dismissing their claim that the assessment for the cost of removing gravel and dirt and for legal fees levied by respondent, the Town of Bristol, was unlawful and void. The landowners also sought review of the trial court's determination that the claim was frivolous, an award of attorney fees, and the entry of a protective order.


OVERVIEW: The dispute arose between the landowners and their neighbors concerning a drainage ditch that crossed the landowners' property, carrying water from a wetland on the neighboring farm. After the Town sent the landowners the assessment, the landowners filed a petition for a writ of mandamus. The court agreed with the trial court that the claim was time-barred by Wis. Stat. § 893.72 insofar as it challenged the assessment for the cost of removing gravel and dirt. However, the court concluded the Town was without power to make an assessment for the legal fees. Therefore, the one-year limitation in § 893.72 did not apply. Attorney's fees were properly assessed against the landowners in connection with their motion for reconsideration because the motion raised arguments that the trial court had previously held were frivolous. The trial court properly exercised its discretion in determining that the landowners' counsel violated Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 20:4.2 when counsel signed, swore to, and filed a petition containing facts that were not true at the time, because the events referenced therein had not yet transpired. As such, sanctions were proper under Wis. Stat. § 802.05(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment, which had dismissed the claim and awarded attorney fees, and remanded the cause for further proceedings. The court affirmed the award of attorney's fees imposed for the frivolous motion for reconsideration, the protective order, the attorney fees imposed for the frivolous objection and for the frivolous motion for reconsideration, and the sanction.

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay denied by, Motion denied by Howard v. Benik, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76262 (E.D. Wis., Oct. 19, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Howard, 2010 Wisc. App. LEXIS 755 (Wis. Ct. App., Sept. 21, 2010)

State v. Howard, 2001 WI App 137, 246 Wis. 2d 475, 630 N.W.2d 244, 2001 Wisc. App. LEXIS 506 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Brown County, Wisconsin, denied defendant's motion to withdraw his no contest plea and his subsequent motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to a concurrent sentence of 10 years' imprisonment on the sexual assault conviction and consecutive sentences for 8 years' imprisonment on 3 of the 4 convictions for recklessly endangering safety. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Monroe County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Kelli B. (In re Zachary B.)


Appeal Nos. 03-0060, 03-0061, 03-0062


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 88; 263 Wis. 2d 413; 662 N.W.2d 360; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 319


March 3, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
March 27, 2003, Decided  
March 27, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  
Review granted by Monroe County Dep't of Human Servs. v. Kelli B., 2003 WI 91, 262 Wis. 2d 500, 665 N.W.2d 375, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 480 (2003)
Affirmed by Monroe County Dept' of Human Services v. Kelli B. (In re Zachary B.), 2004 WI 48, 271 Wis. 2d 51, 678 N.W.2d 856, 2004 Wisc. LEXIS 248 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Monroe County: STEVEN L. ABBOTT, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 02TP000009, 02TP000010, 02TP000011.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner department of human services sought to terminate respondent mother's parental rights to her children under the provisions of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7) (2001-02). The mother moved to dismiss, and the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin) denied the motion. After a disposition hearing, the circuit court terminated the mother's parental rights. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother was the victim of her father's sexual assaults while she was under the age of 13, and the mother's father was the father of all of her children. The mother contended that the ground of incestuous parenthood, Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7) (2001-02), was unconstitutional as applied to her, as she was the victim of her father's assaults. The appellate court found that: (1) the mother had a fundamental liberty interest in parenting her children, regardless of the fact that they were born out of an incestuous relationship; (2) the incestuous parenthood of the children did not, in itself, show that the mother was an unfit parent, as the mother was a minor, a victim of sexual assault, and she did not want to raise the children with her father as a parent; (3) the trial court's discretion to decide not to terminate parental rights did not satisfy the requirements of due process; and (4) the application of Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7) (2001-02) to the mother and the finding of unfitness violated her right to substantive due process, as the fact that the other parent of the mother's children was her father did not, in itself, make the mother an unfit parent.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's judgment was reversed.
