State v. Salzwedel


Appeal No. 02-2573-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 89; 263 Wis. 2d 433; 662 N.W.2d 679; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 290



March 20, 2003, Decided  
March 20, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Green County: JAMES R. BEER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CT-101.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Green County, Wisconsin, for driving while intoxicated, second offense, and sentenced accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated and was read the "Informing the Accused" form in compliance with Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) (2001-2002). He submitted to an evidentiary chemical test of his blood. Defendant later moved to suppress the test result as violations of his Fourth Amendment right against unreasonable searches and seizures. He contended a warrant was needed for the blood draw and that the implied consent statute was unconstitutional because it compelled a person to choose between abandoning the Fourth Amendment protection against unreasonable searches and seizures on the one hand, and suffering the sanctions of lost driving privileges on the other. The trial court denied the motion. The appellate court held the warrantless seizure of defendant's blood did not violate the Fourth Amendment because it came within the exception to the warrant requirement for exigent circumstances. The appellate court further held the implied consent law was not unconstitutional because it compelled drivers to consent to submitting to a chemical test by threatening loss of driving privileges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Henderson


Appeal No. 02-2023-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 89; 263 Wis. 2d 432; 662 N.W.2d 679; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 292



March 20, 2003, Decided  
March 20, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: MICHAEL J. MULROY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CT-91.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for La Crosse County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of operating while intoxicated, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a), as a second offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it denied his motions to suppress the results of the blood draw taken incident to his arrest. Defendant argued that the blood draw and analysis of the blood sample was a warrantless seizure in violation of the Fourth Amendment. The appellate court noted that the exigent circumstances exception to the Fourth Amendment allowed the police, following an arrest for operating while intoxicated supported by probable cause, to perform a blood test for alcohol concentration, regardless of the existence of a breathalyzer. Wis. Stat. § 343.305(2) required an individual arrested for OWI to choose between submitting to a blood draw or immediately losing his driving privileges. Section 343.305(2) was not unconstitutional because, even if the coercive event occurred when the officer read the "Informing the Accused" form, as opposed to when the individual applied for a driver's license, the limited intrusion posed by a blood draw was reasonable when weighed against the State's interest in protecting the public from intoxicated drivers. The analysis of blood after it was drawn was not a second search subject to Fourth Amendment protections.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Calbert v. Briggs


Appeal No. 01-1471


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 89; 263 Wis. 2d 430; 662 N.W.2d 678; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 277



March 13, 2003, Decided  
March 13, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Calbert v. Briggs, 2003 WI 91, 665 N.W.2d 375, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 490 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: JAMES P. DALEY, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CV-1206.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff relatives sued defendants, correctional officer, sheriff, and county, for the death of the decedent, who committed suicide while in the county jail. The Circuit Court for Rock County, Wisconsin, dismissed the relatives' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims against all defendants and dismissed state law negligence claims against the sheriff. The relatives appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent, a pretrial detainee, filled out a form during the booking process as to whether he had ever attempted or was considering suicide. The decedent placed a small mark in the "no" column and a larger check in the "yes" column. The officer said that it was his practice to review yes answers with the detainees. The officer did not recall following that practice with the decedent, but was sure that he had and that the decedent had indicated he was not presently considering suicide. The decedent committed suicide six days later. The appellate court affirmed the grant of summary judgment on the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims as the court noted defendants were not "deliberately indifferent" to the risk that the decedent would commit suicide. As "deliberate indifference" was greater than negligence, the relatives failed to show that defendants knew of and disregarded an excessive risk to the decedent's safety. There was no liability by the officer in his official capacity, and thus no liability on the county, as the relatives failed to prove that the sheriff had an unconstitutional practice, policy, or custom that deprived the decedent of his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

State v. Schell


Appeal No. 02-1394-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 78; 261 Wis. 2d 841; 661 N.W.2d 503; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 257


February 13, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
March 11, 2003, Decided  
March 11, 2003, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 30, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: JOHN A. DES JARDINS, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CM-39.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which amended its judgment to prohibit a sheriff from placing defendant on home monitoring as a probation condition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of several crimes after helping prisoners escape from jail. As part of her probationary sentence, defendant was ordered to serve some active jail time. The trial court declined to place defendant on home monitoring. After the sentence was imposed, the sheriff placed defendant on home monitoring. The trial court then amended its judgment to preclude the sheriff from placing defendant in the program. Defendant then sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the trial court's order improperly infringed upon the executive branch's authority. Once the sentence was imposed, the adversary system was terminated. The sheriff had the discretion to place prisoners on home monitoring under Wis. Stat. § 302.425(2). The decision to place a prisoner on home monitoring was best decided by the sheriff of a particular county, who was vested with the oversight of the county jail under Wis. Stat. § 59.27(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the amended judgment prohibiting the sheriff from placing defendant on the home monitoring program.

State v. Malcheski (In re Malcheski)


Appeal Nos. 02-0104 02-2086-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR

February 27, 2003, Decided  
February 27, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OF AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CT-1523.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) of driving while intoxicated, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a), third offense. The trial court also suspended his license on the ground that he refused to submit to a chemical test pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305, the implied consent statute. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant conceded that, under precedent, the warrantless seizure of his blood did not violate the Fourth Amendment, as it came within the exception to the warrant requirement for exigent circumstances. However, he contended the analysis of his blood was a separate search that must be justified by an exception separate from that for the seizure of his blood, and exigent circumstances did not justify the analysis of his blood once it was drawn. The appellate court recently rejected the same argument in another opinion, as defendant acknowledged in his letter explaining he would not be submit a reply brief. The appellate court also rejected the argument in another decision that the implied consent law was unconstitutional, as it compelled drivers to consent to submitting to a chemical test by threatening loss of driving privileges. It followed that there was no constitutional impediment to sanctioning defendant's refusal by suspending his license. The appellate court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress the results of the chemical test of his blood and correctly concluded the implied consent statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and its license suspension order.

State v. Swinson


Appeal Nos. 02-0395-CR; 02-0396-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


2003 WI App 45; 261 Wis. 2d 633; 660 N.W.2d 12; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 192


December 12, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
February 26, 2003, Decided

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Swinson, 2003 WI 126, 265 Wis. 2d 417, 668 N.W.2d 557, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 647 (2003)
Review denied by State v. Swinson, 2003 WI 126, 265 Wis. 2d 417, 668 N.W.2d 557, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 648 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: TAPPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: L. EDWARD STENGEL, Judge. Cir. Ct. Nos. 93-CF-335 95-CF-160.
United States v. Swinson, 993 F.2d 1299, 1993 U.S. App. LEXIS 11685 (7th Cir. Wis., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of 15 counts of theft by fraudulent misrepresentation, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.20(1)(d) (1999-2000).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a trial court judgment convicting him of 15 counts of theft by fraudulent misrepresentation, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.20(1)(d) (1999-2000). The court affirmed however, stating that the State produced sufficient evidence to establish venue in the county, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.19(2) (1999-2000), as the invoices in question were received in the county. In applying the first part of the multiplicity test, the court concluded that the charges were not identical in fact, because each theft charge against defendant required proof of an additional fact that the other charges did not, namely, the proof of the existence of each individual invoice. Furthermore, the charges were different in fact, as they were separated by time and involved separate volitional acts. Defendant's equal protection challenge failed, as he failed to prove the unconstitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 939.71 (1999-2000) as applied to him. The court concluded that defendant's counsel was not ineffective, because it was apparent that a motion raising either venue or multiplicity would have been unsuccessful.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Peckham


Appeal No. 02-1494-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2003 WI App 67; 261 Wis. 2d 878; 659 N.W.2d 507; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 115



February 4, 2003, Decided  
February 4, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Peckham, 2003 WI 32, 260 Wis. 2d 754, 661 N.W.2d 102, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 321 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MARTIN J. DONALD, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 00 CF 5936.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, convicting him of one count of first degree sexual assault of a child, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1) (1999-2000), and denying his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: The eight-year-old victim stated that defendant put his hand down the victim's pants and touched his penis, which occurred while the victim was at defendant's home using his computer. The victim told police that defendant touched his penis many times before the incident as well. The appellate court found that the trial court admitted evidence to support defendant's theory that the victim's mother fabricated the assault, but excluded evidence relating to the specifics of her own criminal conviction sentencing hearing. The appellate court ruled that this was a reasonable decision, and it would not be disturbed. Also, the trial court did not erroneously exercise its discretion when it summarily denied defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim. Defendant failed to provide any specific facts to suggest that, but for counsel's advice, the outcome of his trial would have been different. Furthermore, defendant's assertion that the sentence imposed was unduly harsh and excessive was moot, due to defendant's death, as any decision regarding the length of sentence would have no practical effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

TOPS Club, Inc. v. City of Milwaukee


Appeal No. 02-1904


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


2003 WI App 62; 260 Wis. 2d 563; 659 N.W.2d 484; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 113


January 7, 2003, Argued  
February 4, 2003, Decided  
February 4, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by TOPS Club, Inc. v. City of Milwaukee, 2003 WI 32, 260 Wis. 2d 755, 661 N.W.2d 102, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 338 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM J. HAESE, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 02 CV 1918.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant weight loss club sought a declaration that it was exempt from appellee city taxation under Wis. Stat. § 70.11(4), which, inter alia, exempted from general property taxes property owned and used exclusively by educational or benevolent associations. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) dismissed the complaint, because, under Wis. Stat. § 74.35(2m), such declaratory-judgment actions were not permitted. The club appealed.


OVERVIEW: The club paid the taxes "under protest." The club admitted that it had not followed the procedure mandated by Wis. Stat. § 74.35, even though the assessor's letter denying the requested exemption alerted it that, if it wanted to dispute the determination, it had to follow the procedures set forth in Wis. Stat. 74.35. The appellate court held that the club's contention was that its property was exempted from taxation was not premised on Wis. Stat. §§ 70.11(21)(a) or 70.11(27). Rather, it claimed that it was both an educational and benevolent organization and, therefore, its property was exempt under Wis. Stat. § 70.11(4). Thus, it did not fall under the exceptions to the exclusive procedure mandated by § 74.35(2m), the main aspect of which was set out in Wis. Stat. § 74.35(2). The appellate court held that Wis. Stat. § 74.35(2m) was enacted after Friendship Village was decided, 1997 Wis. Act 237, § 311m, and was, based on uncontroverted legislative-history, enacted with the specific legislative intent to overrule Friendship Village's holding that the denial of tax exemption could have been challenged via a declaratory-judgment action.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

996 of 1225 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gray (In re Gray)


Appeal No. 01-1032


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


2003 WI App 67; 261 Wis. 2d 876; 659 N.W.2d 506; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 102



February 4, 2003, Decided  
February 4, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO WIS. STAT. RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Gray, 2003 WI 32, 260 Wis. 2d 752, 661 N.W.2d 100, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 231 (Apr. 22, 2003)
Decision reached on appeal by In re Gray v. Gray, 2017 Wisc. App. LEXIS 320 (Wis. Ct. App., May 3, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DANIEL L. KONKOL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99 CI 5.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before defendant was released from incarceration for two sexual assault convictions, the State filed a petition under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 alleging defendant was a sexually violent person. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, found defendant was a sexually violent person and ordered him committed to the department of health and family services. Defendant's motion for post-commitment relief was denied and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that his constitutional rights were violated by the dismissal of the only African-American juror on the jury panel and that his lawyer was deficient for agreeing to the removal of the juror without consulting him. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the decision to have the juror removed as a result of her failure to pay attention during the trial was reasonable. Moreover, defendant was not unfairly prejudiced by the decision to dismiss the inattentive juror. Thus, defendant failed to show that his counsel provided ineffective assistance. Further, defendant was not entitled to a new trial as the real controversy was whether he was a sexually violent person, not whether he was a sexual sadist, as defendant contended. Nor was he entitled to a new trial based on articles he attempted to admit to support his claim that the issue of future risk of dangerousness was not fully tried as the articles were not newly discovered evidence. The State was not required to prove lack of volitional control under Wis. Stat. ch. 980; expert testimony that defendant's disorders created a probability that he would re-offend was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Meicher


Appeal No. 02-1363-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 42; 260 Wis. 2d 602; 658 N.W.2d 88; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 84



January 30, 2003, Decided  
January 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia County: RICHARD L. REHM and JAMES O. MILLER, Judges. Cir. Ct. No. 00-CT-191.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment that found him guilty of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated as a second offense under Wis. Stat. § 343.307 (2002). The arresting officer read an "informing the accused" form to defendant, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4). Defendant moved to suppress the blood sample and the blood test results. The Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin) denied the motion, and defendant pled no contest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that evidence obtained from a blood draw taken after his arrest should have been suppressed for two reasons: (1) his consent was involuntary, as the implied consent law unconstitutionally coerced consent; and (2) without consent, a search warrant was needed to analyze his blood sample. The blood sample was analyzed two days after it was drawn. Defendant contended the implied consent law produced coerced "consent," as it effectively threatened citizens with a penalty, if they did not consent. The appellate court rejected that argument, concluding that any coercion imposed by the implied consent statute was not unreasonable and was thus constitutional. Therefore, defendant's consent was voluntary. Because defendant's consent was voluntary, his assertion that a search warrant was needed to analyze his blood necessarily failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Swansby


Appeal No. 02-1365-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 42; 260 Wis. 2d 602; 658 N.W.2d 88; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 82



January 30, 2003, Decided  
January 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Columbia County: RICHARD REHM, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 99-CT-325.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment convicting her of operating a motor vehicle under the influence of an intoxicant (OMVWI). She claimed the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin) erred in denying her motions to suppress evidence of the result of a blood test administered following her arrest. Inter alia, defendant argued that Wisconsin's "implied consent" law was unconstitutional, as it was impermissibly coercive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the allegedly "coercive" implied consent statute, Wis. Stat. § 343.305(2) (1999-2000), and thus, in her view, VanLaarhoven was not controlling. The appellate court concluded in State v. Wintlend, that the provisions of § 343. 305(2), which conditioned a driver's privilege to operate a motor vehicle on Wisconsin highways on the surrender of his or her right to refuse a chemical test for alcohol concentration did not violate the Fourth Amendment. One who applied for and accepted a license to drive did so on the condition that a failure to submit to the chemical tests would result in the revocation of his license, unless the refusal was reasonable. The appellate court concluded that, to the extent that that condition constituted "coercion," it was nonetheless not unreasonable under the Fourth Amendment, given the minimal intrusion at issue balanced against the State's compelling interest in detecting and deterring drunk driving.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Wittig


Appeal No. 02-2061-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


2003 WI App 42; 260 Wis. 2d 603; 658 N.W.2d 88; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 92



January 30, 2003, Decided  
January 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DALE T. PASELL, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01 CT 366.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the La Crosse County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) which rejected defendant's motion to suppress the admissibility of the results of a chemical test, and convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the admissibility of the results of the chemical test performed on her blood. Defendant did not challenge the warrantless seizure of her blood, but argued that the analysis of her blood was a separate search that required a justification under the U.S. Const. amend. IV separate from that for the seizure of her blood, and exigent circumstances did not justify the analysis of her blood once it had been drawn. The appellate court rejected defendant's argument. The court found that the analysis of defendant's blood did not constitute a separate search for constitutional purposes; rather, it was an examination of evidence already seized. Therefore the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress the results of the chemical test of her blood.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Lichtenberg


Appeal No. 02-2300-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


2003 WI App 42; 260 Wis. 2d 603; 658 N.W.2d 88; 2003 Wisc. App. LEXIS 63



January 28, 2003, Decided  
January 28, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OF LAW OF THE CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Lichtenberg, 2003 WI 32, 661 N.W.2d 103, 2003 Wisc. LEXIS 351 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: DEE R. DYER, Judge. Cir. Ct. No. 01-CT-538.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Outagamie County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) of operating while intoxicated (OWI), third offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to dismiss on speedy trial grounds. The court of appeals disagreed. Raising the issue of the delay from the dismissal of the first case to the recharging was irrelevant, as, during that period, no trial was pending. Additionally, as the trial court was scheduling motion hearings and briefing, nothing indicated that defendant objected to the expanding timetable. In effect, defendant waived his right to a trial within 60 days of his initial appearance. Defendant could not benefit from a presumption of prejudice, as the delay between his initial appearance and his trial was only 10 months, and the presumption did not arise until 1 year passed. Nothing indicated that the State was more responsible for the delay than defendant, nor was there any indication the State tried to cause a delay so as to hamper the defense. Defendant failed to affirmatively assert his right to a speedy trial. Finally, defendant did not show that he was prejudiced in any way by the delay. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
